The Space Between Notes

by trappedinamatchbox

Summary

World renowned pianist Agatha Harkness likes structure, precision, and a well-placed musical note.

Rockstar Rio Vidal leads one of the most popular rock bands today -- The Coven. Rio is chaos wrapped in leather, tattoos and guitar strings. Literally everything Agatha hates when it comes to music. After all, rock doesn't have the elegance and structure and beauty of classical music.

Their worlds collide when Rio’s teenage daughter starts taking piano lessons from Agatha, while Agatha’s starstruck 10-year-old son latches onto Rio like a groupie.

Notes

So this was born out of an annoying writer's block for Luminous. I needed to get my writing juices flowing again and this story just happened. I don't know how long it's going to be. All I know is that I'm already in love with these characters who keep talking in my head, and I hope you guys like them.

See the end of the work for more notes

One

The scent of freshly brewed coffee filled the kitchen as Agatha Harkness stood by the counter, stirring a splash of cream into her cup with slow, methodical movements. The world was quiet in the mornings—before the phone started ringing, before her music school filled with students, before life demanded anything from her. Mornings were hers.

Or at least, they used to be.

Across the table, her 10-year-old son, Nicky, practically vibrated with excitement as he shoveled cereal into his mouth like he hadn’t eaten in days. His tablet sat propped up beside his bowl, replaying one of the most recent The Coven concerts, the sound low but unmistakable—the pulse of drums, the wail of a guitar, the unmistakable growl of her voice.

“Did you see that solo?” Nicky asked, barely pausing to breathe before launching into full-on hero-worship. “Did you see how Rio Vidal absolutely destroyed that riff? She’s so cool, Mom. Like, actually the coolest person on the planet. Maybe the universe.”

Agatha sighed and turned a page of the Los Angeles Times. “Must we do this over breakfast?”

Nicky ignored her, too caught up in his own enthusiasm. “I mean, she’s a legend. Top five greatest living guitarists—maybe top three! And that song? Ugh. Perfection .” He made a dramatic hand gesture, nearly knocking over his orange juice in the process.

Agatha reached out, steadying the glass before it spilled. “Language, Nicky.”

“What? I didn’t even say a bad word!”

“You said ‘destroyed’ and ‘ugh’ with entirely too much feeling.”

“Because it deserved feeling,” Nicky insisted, exasperated. He turned the screen toward her, rewinding the video. “Just look at this—watch her hands, the way she moves—”

Agatha sighed again, glancing up briefly. The camera panned in on Rio Vidal, all wild long dark hair and tattooed arms, her guitar slung low as she played like the instrument was a part of her body. The crowd roared, the stage lights bathed her in red, and she grinned, eyes half-lidded, like she knew she had them in the palm of her hand.

Agatha turned back to her paper. “Yes. Very impressive.”

“You didn’t even watch!”

“I watched enough.”

Truthfully, Agatha had heard of Rio Vidal. It was impossible not to when the woman’s face was plastered on billboards along Sunset Boulevard, her smirk promising a good time to anyone reckless enough to take the invitation. She was the kind of musician who burned fast and bright, the kind who made headlines as often as she made music.

And Agatha had no patience for that kind of chaos.

Still, Nicky’s admiration was relentless. “If she ever—ever—walked into your school, I think I’d actually pass out.”

Agatha snorted. “Then I suppose it’s good we don’t take in rockstars.”

~*~

 

After dropping Nicky off at school—where he barely managed a rushed, “Bye, Mom!” before darting off to find Billy and Tommy—Agatha made her way to Sonata Grove.

Nestled in a quiet Los Feliz neighborhood, Sonata Grove was both Agatha’s sanctuary and her life’s work. She had founded the school eight years ago, not just to teach music but to create a place where discipline and artistry could coexist. A place where structure could nurture talent instead of stifling it.

Housed in a restored Spanish-style building, the school had an undeniable charm—arched doorways, warm wooden floors, and walls lined with framed concert programs and black-and-white photographs of classical greats. A baby grand piano sat in the main lobby, flanked by a few well-loved guitars, their polished surfaces reflecting the soft morning light. The sound of music filled the air at all hours—piano scales drifting from one room, a violin being tuned in another, and the occasional hesitant pluck of a guitar from a student still finding their footing.

As Agatha stepped inside, the familiar scent of aged sheet music and cedar wrapped around her. The building always smelled like this—a mix of history and possibility.

“Morning, boss,” came Wanda’s voice from down the hall.

Agatha found her best friend standing at the front desk, glasses perched on the bridge of her nose, scanning the day’s schedule on her tablet. A cup of tea—Agatha’s, no doubt—sat beside her, already steeped to perfection.

“Morning,” Agatha replied, setting down her bag.

“Busy day,” Wanda said, barely glancing up. “And before you ask—yes, your tea is ready, because I am an angel sent from above.”

Agatha exhaled in relief, taking the cup. “Remind me why I keep you around?”

“My sparkling personality, cutting wit, and the fact that I single-handedly keep this place from descending into anarchy,” Wanda said, deadpan.

“Debatable.”

“Oh, come on, we both know you’d rather deal with an off-key oboe than handle scheduling conflicts and tuition disputes.”

Agatha hummed, sipping her tea. It was perfect, as always—Earl Grey, just the right temperature, brewed exactly the way she liked. Wanda had long since memorized her preferences, which Agatha supposed was a mark of both their friendship and Wanda’s preternatural ability to keep Sonata Grove running like a well-oiled machine.

The front door opened, letting in a warm breeze along with Lilia, who strode in with her usual dramatic flair, a script tucked under one arm and an oversized coffee in hand.

“Good morning, darlings,” Lilia greeted, tossing her sunglasses onto the desk. “Agatha, dear, I need you to settle a debate—” She paused, sniffing the air. “Ah, tea’s been handled. Wanda, you’re a goddess.”

“I know.” Wanda smirked.

Agatha pinched the bridge of her nose. “I haven’t even finished my first cup, and you’re already dragging me into one of your nonsense debates?”

Lilia placed a hand over her heart. “Nonsense? Nonsense? Agatha, please. This is a theatrical emergency.”

“She’s been arguing with her director about whether Lady Macbeth should or should not wear heels in Act Two,” Wanda supplied, not looking up from the tablet.

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “That’s the emergency?”

Lilia huffed. “Heels change posture, posture changes presence, presence changes performance, Agatha.”

Agatha sighed. “You’ll wear whatever your director tells you to wear.”

Lilia gasped, deeply betrayed. “Et tu, Harkness?”

“Moving on,” Agatha said dryly, holding out a hand for the schedule. “What’s on the agenda today?”

Wanda handed over a folder instead. “You’ve got a new student. Fifteen-year-old, piano. Her mom filled out the paperwork online last night. You’re meeting her at four.”

Agatha opened the folder, skimming the application.

Amelia Vidal.

Her fingers stilled. The last name tugged at something in her mind—familiar, but not immediately concerning. Then her gaze flicked lower, to the emergency contact section.

Parent/Guardian: Rio Vidal.

Agatha inhaled sharply.

She knew that name. Everyone did.

She closed the folder with a crisp snap.

Wanda, who had been watching her, raised an eyebrow. “Something wrong?”

Agatha set the folder down. “Not at all.”

But as she took another sip of tea, she suddenly wished it were something stronger.

~*~

 

The name Rio Vidal echoed in Agatha’s mind long after she set the folder down.

It wasn’t just that Rio was famous. That much, Agatha could handle. She had spent enough of her career rubbing shoulders with renowned musicians, attending events where legends floated through the room like ghosts, their names spoken in hushed, reverent tones.

But Rio Vidal wasn’t just famous. She was loudly famous.

Lead guitarist and vocalist of The Coven , one of the biggest rock bands of the last decade. Known for blistering solos, whiskey-soaked vocals, and an unpredictable energy that made her performances electric. The kind of musician who played by instinct rather than theory, who thrived on improvisation rather than careful composition.

The complete antithesis of everything Agatha valued.

And now, her daughter was about to become Agatha’s student.

She pressed her lips together, forcing the thought aside. This wasn’t about Rio. This was about Amelia. Whatever reason Rio had for enrolling her daughter in Sonata Grove, it was none of Agatha’s business. If Amelia was serious about classical music, Agatha would teach her like she would any other student.

She would be professional.

And yet, some part of her—the same part that still remembered Nicky babbling excitedly about Rio Vidal’s guitar solo this morning—couldn’t quite shake the sense that this was going to complicate her life in ways she had no time or patience for.

“Earth to Agatha.”

Wanda’s voice yanked her back to reality.

Agatha blinked, realizing she had been staring at the same spot on the desk for longer than was reasonable. Wanda and Lilia were both watching her with varying degrees of amusement.

“You never space out like that,” Wanda said, crossing her arms. “What gives?”

“Nothing,” Agatha said smoothly, picking up her tea.

Lilia narrowed her eyes and picked up the folder, opening it immediately. “Oh no. That was definitely something. Who’s Amelia Vidal?”

“A new student,” Agatha replied, a little too quickly.

“And?”

“And nothing.”

Wanda’s eyes flicked to the folder. “Vidal… As in Rio Vidal?”

Agatha sighed, knowing resistance was futile.

“Yes,” she admitted. “Apparently, I’m teaching her daughter.”

There was a beat of silence.

Then Lilia let out a delighted cackle.

“Oh, this is rich,” she declared. “Agatha Harkness, teaching the Rio Vidal’s kid. A rockstar’s offspring in your perfectly curated temple of classical precision. This is fate, darling.”

Agatha shot her a flat look. “Fate has a terrible sense of humor.”

“I’m just saying,” Lilia went on, clearly enjoying herself, “it’s rather poetic, isn’t it? The queen of structure and discipline, forced to interact with the wild, untamed force of nature that is Rio Vidal.” She grinned. “You two are going to hate each other.”

“I don’t intend to interact with her at all,” Agatha said. “I’m teaching Amelia. That’s it.”

Wanda hummed, an infuriatingly knowing expression crossing her face.

“Right,” she said. “You keep telling yourself that.”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “I am not engaging in this nonsense. I have work to do.”

“Of course, of course,” Wanda said breezily, already heading toward her office. “Just don’t say I didn’t warn you when this blows up in your face.”

“It won’t,” Agatha called after her.

But even as she gathered her things for her first lesson of the day, she couldn’t shake the uneasy feeling settling in her chest.

~*~

 

The afternoon sun cast long shadows through the arched windows of Sonata Grove as Agatha prepared for her final lesson of the day.

She straightened the sheet music on the piano, took a slow sip of her now-lukewarm tea, and exhaled. It was ridiculous how much she was thinking about this.

It’s just another student.

A knock at the door pulled her from her thoughts. Wanda’s head peeked in.

“Your four o’clock is here,” she announced, tone entirely too amused.

Agatha smoothed a hand over her skirt. “Send her in.”

Wanda disappeared, and a moment later, the door swung open again.

And there she was.

Amelia Vidal.

The girl was tall for her age, all long limbs and sharp angles, her dark curls half-heartedly pulled into a bun that was already coming undone. She wore a loose hoodie over ripped jeans, and her expression carried the distinct air of someone who would rather be anywhere else.

She barely looked at Agatha as she stepped inside, shifting the strap of her bag higher on her shoulder.

Ah, Agatha thought. A challenge.

“Amelia,” she greeted, offering a small nod. “I’m Agatha Harkness. Welcome to Sonata Grove.”

The girl stiffened slightly at the sound of her own name. “Uh, yeah. Thanks.”

Interesting.

“Go ahead and take a seat,” Agatha instructed, gesturing toward the bench. “I’d like to start with a scale. Just to get a sense of where you are.”

Amelia hesitated, then moved to sit at the piano, her fingers hovering over the keys. There was tension in her shoulders, a sort of uncertainty that Agatha immediately clocked.

She waited.

A long moment passed.

Then, Amelia played.

The first few notes were tentative, careful. Then the next. And the next. A simple C major scale, played with textbook precision but none of the fluidity that came with confidence.

Agatha folded her arms. “Again.”

Amelia shot her a glance but complied. This time, it was slightly smoother.

“Hmm,” Agatha murmured. “You’ve had training before?”

“Sort of,” Amelia muttered.

“Sort of?”

The girl’s fingers twitched. “I picked up a little on my own.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow. “Self-taught?”

Amelia nodded once.

Interesting.

“Your technique is solid,” Agatha said, moving to stand beside the piano. “But you hesitate. That tells me you’re thinking too much about each note instead of feeling the movement between them.”

Amelia’s jaw tightened. “I don’t hesitate.”

Agatha smiled, just slightly. Teenagers.

“Of course not,” she said lightly. “Let’s try again.”

She reached out, gently adjusting the position of Amelia’s hand. The girl didn’t flinch, but there was a shift—subtle but telling.

A discomfort with being corrected.

A need to prove herself.

Agatha recognized it well.

“Again,” she instructed.

This time, the scale was smoother.

Better.

Amelia exhaled sharply, but there was the barest flicker of satisfaction in her expression.

Agatha noticed.

She nodded. “Good.”

For the first time, Amelia met her gaze directly.

And Agatha knew, in that moment, that this was going to be very interesting indeed.

~*~

The lesson continued in carefully measured steps. Agatha assessed Amelia’s posture, her finger placement, the way she carried tension in her shoulders. The girl took corrections with a quiet kind of resistance—she listened, but she didn’t like it.

Still, Agatha had taught enough students to know when someone was genuinely invested, and despite Amelia’s apparent aloofness, the way her fingers moved across the keys spoke volumes.

She cared.

She just didn’t want Agatha to know that she cared.

“Tell me,” Agatha said as she watched Amelia attempt a simple etude, “what made you interested in classical music?”

A muscle in Amelia’s jaw ticked. She didn’t answer right away, and for a moment, Agatha assumed she wouldn’t answer at all.

Then—

“I like how structured it is,” Amelia muttered, not looking up. “It makes sense.”

Agatha tilted her head slightly. “Unlike other kinds of music?”

Amelia’s fingers faltered for half a second before she recovered. “Rock is just noise.”

Ah. There it is.

Agatha hummed. “I imagine your mother might disagree.”

The words were barely out of her mouth before Amelia’s entire expression shuttered.

“Can we just focus on the lesson?” she said flatly.

Agatha lifted a brow but didn’t push.

Noted.

They continued in near silence, the only sound between them the deliberate notes of the piano. Amelia was determined, Agatha would give her that.

At the end of the lesson, Amelia finally turned to face her.

“How bad was I?” she asked, bracing herself.

Agatha regarded her for a moment.

“You’re disciplined,” she said, “but you don’t trust yourself yet.”

Amelia frowned. “What does that mean?”

“It means you play like someone who’s afraid of getting it wrong,” Agatha said simply. “Technique can be taught, but confidence? That’s something you have to find for yourself.”

Amelia didn’t say anything for a long moment. Then, with a barely-there nod, she grabbed her bag.

“See you next week, I guess.”

And with that, she was gone.

Agatha exhaled, turning back toward the piano. She let her fingers drift across the keys, playing a few soft notes as she considered the lesson.

Then a voice from the door:

“Well, that was tense.”

Agatha didn’t have to turn around to know who it was.

“Wanda,” she said dryly, still playing. “Do you always eavesdrop on my lessons?”

“Only when they’re interesting,” Wanda said, stepping into the room with an all-too-knowing smirk. “And this one? Very interesting .”

Agatha sighed, shaking her head. “She’s just another student.”

Wanda’s smirk deepened. “Sure she is.”

Agatha shot her a look.

Wanda raised her hands in mock innocence. “Hey, I’m just saying—there’s a lot going on there. That girl’s got a chip on her shoulder the size of the Hollywood sign.”

“Yes, well,” Agatha said, pressing a final chord before standing, “she’s not my problem outside these lessons.”

Wanda hummed. “Mmm. Unless her mother becomes your problem.”

Agatha frowned. “What are you talking about?”

Wanda grinned. “Oh, you don’t know?”

“Know what?”

Wanda’s eyes sparkled with mischief. “Rio Vidal just pulled up outside.”

Agatha went very, very still.

Wanda laughed. “Oh, this is going to be good.”

Agatha took a slow, measured breath and followed her friend out to the main lobby.

She wasn’t the type to be easily rattled. She had built an entire career on poise, precision, control. But there was something undeniably unsettling about the knowledge that Rio Vidal—rock legend, media darling, general force of chaos—was standing outside her music school.

And then the door swung open.

Rio Vidal walked in like she owned the place.

She was dressed in ripped black jeans and a faded band tee (not even her own band, Agatha noted, but an old Fleetwood Mac tour shirt), a leather jacket slung over her shoulder. Dark hair framed sharp features, and her smirk was the kind worn by someone who had never been told no a day in her life.

She was aggravatingly attractive.

Agatha straightened. Not relevant.

Rio’s gaze found her immediately, sharp brown eyes scanning her with obvious curiosity. Then she grinned, recognition flashing in her expression.

“So,” she said, voice smooth and amused, “you’re the one giving my kid piano lessons.”

Agatha met her stare evenly. “I am.”

Rio hummed. “Huh. Thought you’d be older.”

Agatha arched a brow. “Thought you’d be taller.”

From the doorway, Wanda made a strangled choking sound.

Rio blinked—then threw her head back and laughed.

Agatha hated how much she liked the sound of it.

“Alright,” Rio said, shaking her head. “I like you.”

“I don’t recall asking,” Agatha replied smoothly.

Rio grinned like that only entertained her further.

She shoved her hands in her pockets, glancing around. “So, how’s she doing?”

Agatha didn’t need clarification. “Amelia has a natural ear for melody. Strong technique. But she’s holding herself back.”

Rio tilted her head. “How so?”

“She’s precise, but hesitant. She plays like someone waiting for permission,” Agatha said simply. “She’s afraid of making mistakes.”

Rio let out a short breath, nodding like that made perfect sense. “Yeah. That sounds about right.”

Agatha studied her. “She doesn’t want to be compared to you.”

Something flickered in Rio’s expression. For a moment, the playful ease dropped, and Agatha saw something much sharper underneath.

“Yeah,” Rio muttered. “I know.”

Agatha hesitated before continuing. “I believe she enjoys classical music.”

That made Rio snort. “Yeah, no shit. She listens to Chopin the way other kids listen to pop music. Don’t get me wrong, I love that she’s into music at all, but—”

“But it’s not your music,” Agatha finished for her.

Rio gave her a wry look. “Exactly.”

Agatha considered her for a moment. Despite everything—her overwhelming presence, her effortless confidence—Rio Vidal was a mother first. And Agatha could see the complicated tangle of emotions in her expression: pride, confusion, maybe even a little hurt.

“She doesn’t have to be you,” Agatha said carefully. “And I don’t think she wants to be.”

Rio let out a short, humorless chuckle. “Yeah. That’s the part I’m still wrapping my head around.”

She ran a hand through her hair and checked the time on her phone. “Anyway. Thanks for being patient with her. She, uh… she quits things a lot. So, we’ll see how long this lasts.”

Agatha straightened. “If she stays, I’ll make sure she excels.”

Rio grinned. “Yeah, I get that vibe from you, Miss Harkness.”

She turned to leave, then hesitated.

For a split second, it looked like she wanted to say something else.

Then she shook it off and shot her one last smirk. “See you around.”

And just like that, she was gone, apparently content to wait for her daughter on her own.

Agatha exhaled, only now realizing how tightly wound she’d been standing.

Behind her, Wanda cackled.

Agatha turned, scowling. “Not a word.”

Wanda smirked. “Oh, darling. I wouldn’t dare.”

Agatha closed her eyes. She had a feeling she was going to regret all of this.

~*~

Agatha had exactly three seconds of peace before he arrived.

The front door swung open, and in barreled Nicky—freshly dropped off from baseball practice, still in his uniform, backpack slung haphazardly over one shoulder. He was mid-sentence about something, when he froze.

Agatha could only watch in muted horror as his expression morphed from vague exhaustion to startled recognition, and then— oh no —outright elation.

Rio Vidal was standing just a few feet away, casually leaning against the wall outside the bathroom, arms crossed, looking at her phone as she waited for Amelia.

Nicky’s baseball bag hit the floor with a dull thud. His mouth opened. No sound came out.

Agatha could practically see the moment his brain caught up with reality.

Like watching a car crash in slow motion, she knew what was about to happen, couldn’t stop it, and was entirely powerless to look away.

Nicky inhaled sharply—

“OH MY GOD.”

Rio startled slightly, glancing up. Then she blinked, eyes flicking to Agatha and back to the ten-year-old currently vibrating with barely restrained excitement.

“Uh,” Rio said.

“ Oh my God ,” Nicky repeated, louder this time, practically bouncing on his toes. “ You’re Rio Vidal !”

Rio tilted her head, grinning slightly. “That’s what they tell me.”

“MOM!” Nicky whipped around so fast he nearly tripped over his own feet, his expression caught somewhere between betrayal and ecstatic disbelief. “ You didn’t tell me you know Rio Vidal! ”

Agatha pressed her lips together, inhaling sharply through her nose. “I don’t know Rio Vidal.”

Nicky turned back to Rio, eyes wide. “Do you know my mom?”

Rio, clearly entertained, shrugged. “We just met.”

Nicky gasped as if this was the single most unfair thing in the entire world.

“AND YOU DIDN’T TELL ME?”

Agatha pinched the bridge of her nose. “Nicky—”

“I have posters of you in my room!” he blurted, addressing Rio now, as if Agatha no longer existed. “And The Coven’s entire discography on vinyl! And mom got me a signed copy of Devil in the details for my birthday!”

Rio’s eyebrows shot up. “Damn. That’s commitment. Even I don’t have the vinyls.”

Nicky let out a strangled sound, like he might actually combust.

Agatha sighed. This was exactly what she had been afraid of.

Before she could attempt damage control, the bathroom door swung open and Amelia stepped out, running a hand through her hair. She barely got two steps before stopping in confusion at the scene unfolding before her.

“What,” she asked slowly, “is happening right now?”

Agatha felt an oncoming headache press at her temples.

“Nicky,” she said, voice deceptively calm, “this is Amelia Vidal. My student. And Rio is her mother.”

Nicky whipped back to Rio, stunned. “You have a daughter?!”

Mia crossed her arms. “Yeah. Hi. I’m right here.”

Rio snorted, clearly having the time of her life.

Nicky’s brain short-circuited. “ Mom ,” he hissed in a stage whisper, as if Rio couldn’t hear him, “ How did you not tell me this ?”

Agatha, exhausted beyond measure, exhaled slowly and decided she was going to fake her own death before the week was out.

Rio clapped a hand over her mouth to hide her laughter. “Damn,” she murmured, voice full of amusement. “You’re in trouble now, Harkness.”

Agatha shot her a glare.

Nicky, meanwhile, had turned his awe back on Rio. “Okay, but—you’re really here? Like, actually here?”

Rio smirked. “Last time I checked.”

Nicky inhaled again, eyes shining with determination. “Can I play guitar with you?”

Amelia groaned audibly, rubbing her temples. “ Oh my God .”

Agatha silently wished for divine intervention.

And Rio?

Rio just grinned, looking entirely entertained.



Two

Chapter Notes

You guys are the absolute best! I'm so happy you're all as excited as I am about this story!

Rio Vidal had done a lot of nerve-wracking things in her life—played sold-out arenas, performed on live TV, even once climbed onto a rooftop mid-show just because Natasha dared her to—but none of that compared to the sheer, suffocating terror of driving her kid to her first piano lesson.

It wasn’t supposed to be terrifying. It was just music. She knew music. But this wasn’t about her. This was about Mia.

Mia, who had spent the past month dropping hints about maybe wanting to take piano seriously. Who had tentatively asked Rio if she thought it was stupid to want to study classical music instead of following in her mother’s rock-and-roll footsteps. Who, despite all her efforts to act like she didn’t care, was clearly nervous as hell about this lesson.

Rio glanced over at her daughter, who sat stiffly in the passenger seat, arms crossed like she was preparing for battle. The indie rock station played softly in the background—Mia’s choice, since she refused to let Rio play anything from The Coven.

“You good over there, honey?” Rio asked, tapping her fingers against the steering wheel.

Mia shrugged. “Yeah.”

Rio raised an eyebrow. “That was the most unconvincing ‘yeah’ I’ve ever heard.”

Mia sighed, fiddling with the sleeves of her hoodie. “I just—what if she thinks I suck?”

That she being Agatha Harkness, the apparently brilliant, slightly terrifying classical pianist Mia had insisted on taking lessons from.

Rio snorted. “Doubt it. But if she does, screw her. You’re the most badass kid I know.”

Mia huffed a small laugh, shaking her head. “I want to be good at this.”

Rio softened. “Then you will be.”

She reached over and squeezed Mia’s knee. Her daughter didn’t pull away—Rio counted that as a win.

A few minutes later, she pulled up in front of Sonata Grove, a name that sounded fancy as hell. She craned her neck, looking the place over. It was a beautiful house, Spanish architecture, and very fancy, just like the name. But it also exuded warmth.

Mia exhaled sharply, gripping the door handle. “Okay. Here goes nothing.”

“You want me to come in with you?”

Mia gave her a look. “Absolutely not.”

Rio grinned. “Alright, alright. I’ll be back in an hour. Try not to become a world-famous pianist before I pick you up.”

Mia rolled her eyes but smirked as she climbed out of the car.

Rio watched her disappear inside, then let out a breath she hadn’t realized she was holding.

For the first time in her life, she had no idea what came next.

 

~*~

 

Rio never really got to be alone. Not really.

Even in the quietest moments—hotel rooms between tour stops, late nights writing lyrics while Mia slept upstairs—there was always something. A text, a call, the lingering pressure of a life that didn’t stop moving.

So she treasured the rare moments like this, sitting in a tiny café a few blocks from Sonata Grove, where no one was looking at her, no one was asking for anything, and no one knew she was Rio Vidal.

The baseball cap helped, pulled low over her long, straight hair. The sunglasses did the rest, covering most of her face. She stirred her espresso absently, half-listening to the soft hum of conversation around her.

It was a little hole-in-the-wall place, the kind of café that smelled like fresh pastries and burnt espresso, with a chalkboard menu that hadn’t been updated in years. A couple of college kids sat in the corner, hunched over laptops. A man near the window read a newspaper like it was still 1995. The barista, a guy in his twenties with a septum piercing and very strong opinions about oat milk, hadn’t even given her a second glance.

Perfect.

She pulled out her phone, scrolling aimlessly. A few messages from Alice and Jen. Natasha had sent a voice memo that was probably just her screaming about something. Rio smirked but didn’t play it.

Then, a text from Mia.

Kiddo

I’m about to go in. No idea what I’m doing. This was a mistake .

Rio chuckled, shaking her head.

Rio

You’re fine. Don’t let your piano lady scare you.

No response. Which meant Mia was either too focused or too annoyed to text back.

Rio leaned back in her chair, sipping her espresso. This was good. A normal, boring, quiet moment.

She exhaled slowly, savoring it.

~*~

Rio had met a lot of impressive people in her life. Genius producers, guitar legends, icons who shaped the industry. People who could walk into a room and own it without saying a single word.

Agatha Harkness?

Yeah. She was one of them. Like, big time. She’d looked her up before letting her kid enroll in her piano lessons.

And that was annoying.

Because Rio had walked into Sonata Grove expecting some stuffy, uptight, old, classical purist who’d look down her nose at a rockstar. Someone rigid, polished to the point of being unyielding. Instead, she got this—a woman who moved through the space like she belonged there, with a presence so sharp and self-possessed it was almost unfair.

She wasn’t just elegant; she was deliberate. The way she held herself, the way she spoke—low, even, no wasted syllables—made it clear she was someone who expected to be listened to. Not in an arrogant way, but in a way that said people always listened.

And then there was the music. She had seen videos the night before, thoroughly investigating her kid’s future teacher.

Rio had heard a lot of pianists in her time—some technically perfect, others expressive, a rare few who were both. But Agatha Harkness played like she breathed music. Every note was effortless, fluid, precise in a way that wasn’t calculated but innate.

It wasn’t showy. She wasn’t trying to impress anyone.

She just was.

And that was the frustrating part.

Because Rio recognized greatness when she saw it, and Agatha had the kind that didn’t ask for your attention—it commanded it. The kind that made Rio’s fingers twitch like they needed a guitar in her hands just to do something with the energy buzzing under her skin.

She didn’t like that.

Didn’t like the way Agatha’s presence threw her off balance. Didn’t like the way those sharp blue eyes met hers with a cool, assessing weight, like she was measuring her.

Rio had spent years being judged by people from the classical world. Professors, critics, musicians who thought rock was cheap, that it wasn’t real music. She’d fought tooth and nail for her place, for every bit of respect she’d earned.

So if Agatha Harkness had any of that condescension in her—if she was about to look down on Rio like she was some undisciplined, talentless hack—well.

Rio was very good at being a pain in the ass.

And maybe, just maybe, she’d enjoy being one a little too much.

~*~

Rio had met fans of all ages in the past decade or so—kids, teens, grown-ass adults who cried when they met her. She was used to the wide-eyed stares, the excited stammering, the sheer shock that came with seeing someone in real life who had only ever existed on a screen or a stage.

But this kid?

This kid was next level.

He looked like he’d just discovered Santa Claus was real and currently standing in front of him. His hands curled into fists at his sides like he physically couldn’t handle his excitement.

“Holy crap,” he breathed, still staring. “You’re real. You’re actually real.”

Rio barely had a second to react before he turned to Agatha again, bouncing on the balls of his feet like he might just vibrate into another dimension.

“Mom—Mom, you don’t understand. It’s Rio Vidal .”

Oh, she understood, alright.

Agatha Harkness was standing perfectly still, her expression carefully blank, but Rio didn’t miss the way her fingers twitched at her sides, like she was caught between physically dragging her kid away or throwing herself into traffic.

And honestly? It was hilarious.

Rio crossed her arms, fighting back a smirk as she turned to Nicky, who still looked like he might spontaneously combust at any second.

“Oh my God,” he said again, as if his brain was short-circuiting. “You don’t understand, I have all your albums. Like, all of them ,” he repeated, like his mind still couldn’t compute that she was really there in the flesh, talking to him.

“Yeah?” Rio grinned. “What’s your favorite?”

“Easy—Blood Moon Riot.” The answer came so fast, so sure, that Rio actually blinked.

“No hesitation,” she said, impressed. “I like it.”

Nicky’s hands flapped wildly, like he didn’t know what to do with them. “It’s just—God—the guitar on that album? It changed my life . Your solo on Ritual Fire? I—I can’t even talk about it, I’ll start crying.”

Rio beamed.

Agatha, meanwhile, looked like she was contemplating walking into the sea.

Which, honestly, made all of this so much better.

“So, let me get this straight,” Rio said, shifting her weight to one side, gaze flicking between them. “You’re telling me Agatha Harkness’ kid is a massive fan of my band?”

“Not just a fan—” Nicky cut in, voice desperate. “A huge fan. Loyal fan. Die-hard fan.”

Rio let out a low whistle, grinning. “Damn, Harkness, didn’t know you were raising a kid with taste.”

Agatha’s entire body went stiff. Her lips parted, blue eyes flashing with something sharp and dangerous, like she was moments away from committing a murder.

Oh .

Oh, this was fun.

Agatha’s glare could have set fire to a lesser woman. Unfortunately for her, Rio had spent years in a band with Natasha Romanov—she was immune to death glares.

Nicky, meanwhile, was still vibrating with excitement, shifting from foot to foot like he had too much energy in his body and nowhere to put it.

“Wait—wait, I need to process this.” He took a deep breath, as if steadying himself. “You—”, he pointed at Rio, “are standing in my mom’s music school, and you—”, now he swung toward Agatha, “know Rio Vidal personally. Personally! And you didn’t tell me?! Mom, I—” He cut himself off with a strangled noise.

Agatha pressed two fingers to her temple, exhaling. “Nicky—”

“No, no, no—you don’t understand—” Nicky spun back to Rio. “Do you know how many times I’ve asked her to take me to one of your concerts? And she just—” He made an exaggerated, disbelieving gesture at Agatha. “Nothing. Stonewall. ‘We’ll see. You’re not old enough.’ ‘Maybe next time .’ Meanwhile, she just—casually meets you and doesn’t say a word?”

Rio grinned. “Brutal.”

“ I know !” Nicky looked genuinely betrayed.

Rio chuckled, leaning against the wall as she watched them. This was hilarious.

“Hey, relax, kid. I just got here today. Your mom and I aren’t exactly besties—”, she ignored Agatha’s sharp huff at that, ”—but I am gonna be around for a bit.”

Nicky’s entire soul looked like it left his body. “Oh my God. Oh my God. Oh my God.”

Rio gave him a lazy grin. “You play anything, or you just a fan?”

“Guitar.” Nicky’s voice was dead serious. “I’ve been playing for three years.”

Rio let out an impressed hum. “Three years, huh? Electric or acoustic?”

“Both, but—” he gestured wildly ”—mostly electric. My mom made me learn classical guitar first, but—”

“As she should,” Rio said, nodding sagely.

“I know, but—” Nicky let out a frustrated groan. “I just—I just want to shred, you know? Like you.”

Rio barked out a laugh. “I respect that.”

“Oh, thank you.” Nicky threw his hands up dramatically, turning to Agatha. “See? She gets it .”

Agatha, who had been rubbing her temple like she was developing a massive headache, merely sighed.

“I don’t suppose there’s a chance you’ll react like this to your math homework.”

“ Mom .” Nicky glared. “Priorities.”

Rio laughed again, eyes crinkling with amusement.

Oh, she liked this kid.

“Well, Nicky,” she said, smirking. “I guess I’ll be seeing you around.”

“Oh my God,” Nicky whispered, looking like he was about to collapse.

Agatha closed her eyes. “He’s never going to shut up about this.”

“Nope,” Rio said, popping the p and enjoying every second of it.

~*~

By the time they pulled into the driveway of their house—a sleek but lived-in modern home tucked in the Hollywood Hills—Rio had mostly shaken off the whirlwind that was Nicky Harkness. Mostly.

As she cut the engine, she glanced at Mia, who was scrolling through her phone with an expression that was just a little too neutral.

“So,” Rio said, tilting her head. “How was the lesson?”

Mia shrugged, way too casual. “Fine.”

Rio narrowed her eyes. “Uh-huh. That’s it?”

Mia hesitated for a fraction of a second—just long enough for Rio to catch it—before saying, “I liked it.”

Rio blinked. She hadn’t expected that.

“Yeah?”

Another shrug, but this time, Rio could see it—the quiet thrill behind Mia’s usually guarded expression, the way her fingers twitched against her phone like she was holding back from saying more.

Rio smirked. “So, Agatha Harkness didn’t bore you to death, then?”

“No.”

Rio raised an eyebrow. “That’s almost high praise, coming from you.”

Mia rolled her eyes but didn’t argue.

Something warm settled in Rio’s chest. She knew how much her daughter hated being in the spotlight, how she resisted anything that might lump her in with her mother’s world. But right now, sitting in the car, Mia didn’t look like she was dreading this. She looked… interested. Maybe even excited.

And that ? That was huge.

Rio drummed her fingers against the steering wheel. “Guess that means you’ll be going back, then?”

Mia glanced at her, the corner of her mouth twitching. “Yeah. I think I will.”

~*~

A week later, Rio found herself pulling up to Mia’s school—a way-too-fancy private institution that looked more like a museum than a place where teenagers were supposed to be learning about algebra and literature.

She barely had time to shift the car into park before she spotted Mia making her way across the front steps, bag slung over her shoulder, head down. She stepped out of the car, ready to greet her kid. But before Mia could reach the car, Rio saw it happen.

Two students in crisp uniforms—both girls, probably around Mia’s age—noticed her. Their eyes widened, and Rio could practically see the moment they decided to approach.

“Oh my god, you’re Rio Vidal!” one of them squealed as they hurried up.

Rio plastered on a polite smile. She could hear the click of a phone camera before either of them had even asked.

“That’s me,” she said smoothly.

“Could you sign my notebook? My older sister is obsessed with The Coven.”

“And maybe a quick photo?” the other girl added eagerly.

This wasn’t new. It was far from the worst fan interaction Rio had ever had. So she obliged, signing the notebook with a quick flourish before shifting to let them take the selfie they so desperately wanted.

It was over in less than a minute, the girls thanking her profusely before scurrying away, already posting about it.

Rio sighed and turned back to the car—only to find Mia standing a few feet away, watching.

Her expression was unreadable, but something in the set of her shoulders made Rio pause.

“Hey, kiddo,” she greeted, trying to gauge her reaction.

Mia didn’t answer right away. She just climbed into the passenger seat, pulled the door shut, and buckled in.

Rio frowned, getting into the car. “You good?”

Mia nodded once, looking out the window.

Rio wanted to press—wanted to ask what that look had been about—but instead, she just pulled out onto the road, heading toward Sonata Grove.

The drive to the music school was mostly quiet. Mia scrolled through her phone, answering in monosyllables when Rio tried to make conversation.

Yup. Fine. No.

Yeah. She was upset about something.

Rio tapped her fingers against the wheel, glancing at Mia every few moments. She knew better than to push—Mia would talk when she was ready, not when Rio wanted her to.

So Rio let the silence settle.

By the time they reached Sonata Grove, Mia was already unbuckling her seatbelt before Rio had fully parked.

“You sure you’re good?” Rio tried again.

“I’m fine.” Mia reached for the door handle. “See you later.”

And just like that, she was out of the car, disappearing into the school without a backward glance.

Rio sighed, rubbing the bridge of her nose. Teenagers, man.

She climbed out of the car, locking it as she made her way inside.

The reception area was the same as last time—warm wood floors, soft lighting, the faint hum of piano drifting from somewhere down the hall. But this time, Nicky was already there.

He was sitting on one of the couches, guitar across his lap, fingers plucking out an admittedly pretty decent melody. As soon as he spotted Rio, his face lit up.

“Rio!” He shot to his feet, his baseball cap nearly falling off in the process. “You came back!”

“I did.” She grinned. “You live here or something?”

“No,” he scoffed, then paused. “Well. Kinda. My mom owns the place.”

Rio glanced up and spotted Agatha by the reception desk, sipping from a sleek black coffee cup. She was talking to a redheaded woman with sharp cheekbones and a violin case slung over her shoulder.

As if sensing Rio’s gaze, Agatha turned her head, meeting her eyes.

Her expression flickered to something she couldn’t quite discern yet—just for a second—before she composed herself.

Rio just smirked.

Agatha took one last sip of her coffee before excusing herself from the redhead’s conversation. As she walked over, her heels clicked softly against the wooden floor.

“Ms. Vidal,” she greeted, her tone polite but distant.

“Ms. Harkness,” Rio returned with a smirk, leaning against the reception desk.

Agatha’s eye twitched—just slightly.

“Mia is already in the classroom,” Agatha informed her, as if that was the only thing worth saying. “We’re starting with technique today.”

“Exciting,” Rio said, tilting her head. “Does she seem… into it?”

Agatha paused, considering her answer before nodding. “She’s focused. She wants to improve.”

That was something.

“She doesn’t usually get excited about new people,” Rio admitted, glancing toward the hallway where Mia had disappeared. “So, thanks. For whatever you’re doing.”

“It’s not magic, Ms. Vidal,” Agatha said dryly. “It’s discipline and proper instruction.”

“Right, yeah, totally,” Rio said, nodding in mock seriousness. “Sounds way less intimidating when you say it like that.”

Agatha exhaled, clearly deciding she had better things to do than entertain Rio’s antics. She turned toward Nicky instead.

“Nicky,” she said patiently. “Did you finish your homework?”

“Yes,” Nicky answered immediately.

Agatha narrowed her eyes.

“Some of it,” he corrected.

Agatha exhaled slowly, then turned back to Rio. “Try not to be a distraction.”

“No promises,” Rio said easily.

Agatha gave her a look, then turned on her heel and disappeared down the hall.

The moment she was gone, Nicky turned back to Rio with wide eyes.

“Dude,” he whispered. “You just messed with my mom and survived.”

Rio laughed. “She’s not that scary.”

“That’s what they all say before she assigns them extra scales.”

Rio grinned, ruffling his hair. “Good thing I’m not one of her students then, huh?”

Nicky beamed up at her, clearly delighted by this new alliance.

“So,” he said, shifting his guitar in his lap. “Are we playing today or what?”

Rio leaned back against the reception desk, arms crossed, smirking down at the kid.

“You don’t waste any time, huh?”

“Time is precious,” Nicky said, way too seriously for a ten-year-old.

Rio barked out a laugh. “You sound like my manager.”

“Does your manager also want to jam with you?”

“Not even a little.”

Rio took in his eager expression, the way he was practically vibrating with anticipation. It reminded her of herself when she was a kid, back when music felt like the only thing in the world that mattered. She glanced down at his guitar—clearly well-loved, a little too big for him but carried with confidence.

“Alright, kid. Show me what you got.”

Nicky’s eyes lit up like she’d just told him he’d won a lifetime supply of candy.

“Really?”

“Really,” Rio said, pushing off the desk. “But let’s take it outside. Your mom already thinks I’m a distraction. If we start playing in here, she might actually murder me.”

Nicky snorted. “Fair point.”

They made their way out to the small courtyard behind the building, where a couple of benches sat under a large oak tree. Rio sat down, stretching her legs out in front of her while Nicky practically bounced into place beside her, already adjusting the strap of his guitar.

“Alright,” Rio said, nodding toward him. “Hit me with something.”

Nicky took a deep breath, then started strumming—an enthusiastic but slightly choppy version of one of The Coven’s earliest songs.

Rio blinked, a little caught off guard.

“Wait—hold up,” she said, holding up a hand to stop him. “Is that Wicked Games?”

Nicky grinned. “Maybe.”

“How the hell do you know that song?”

“I have ears, don’t I?” he said cheekily. “Also, YouTube exists.”

Rio whistled lowly. “Man, I don’t know if I should be flattered or worried.”

“You should definitely be flattered,” Nicky said, then immediately went back to playing, his fingers more confident this time.

Rio watched him for a few seconds, then nodded.

“Alright, alright,” she said, grabbing the guitar out of his hands before he could protest. “Lemme show you something.”

She adjusted the tuning slightly, then started playing the same riff—only smoother, the way it was meant to sound, fingers gliding effortlessly over the strings. Nicky’s jaw dropped.

“Whoa,” he breathed.

Rio smirked. “Yeah, that’s the sound we’re going for. You’re almost there, kid.”

Nicky was staring at her like she had just parted the Red Sea. “Can you teach me how to do that?”

Rio winked. “Oh, I don’t know. Didn’t your mom say I was a bad influence?”

“She says that about Billy and Tommy too, and I still hang out with them,” Nicky said, completely unfazed. “So, what do you say?”

Rio chuckled, shaking her head.

“Alright, kid. Let’s jam.”

For the next twenty minutes, Rio worked through the song with Nicky, slowing down the riff, showing him where to place his fingers for a cleaner transition. He was quick—eager and determined in a way she recognized all too well.

“You’re picking this up fast,” she admitted, watching as he repeated the phrase back, his movements already a little smoother.

“I’ve been practicing,” Nicky said, his face scrunched in concentration.

“It shows,” Rio said, tapping her fingers on the bench. Then she picked up the extra guitar Nicky had gotten for them. “Alright, let’s try it together. I’ll take lead, you follow. And don’t worry if you mess up—just jump back in when you can.”

Nicky nodded so hard his cap nearly fell off.

They started playing—Rio keeping the rhythm steady, letting Nicky find his way through. The first few tries were a little rough, but by the fourth run-through, he was holding his own.

“Hell yeah, kid!” Rio whooped when they hit the last note. “That was solid.”

Nicky beamed. “You think so?”

“Dude, that was your first time playing it with me. Imagine what you’ll sound like after a few more sessions.”

“So, you’ll play with me again?”

Rio rolled her eyes, smirking. “I feel like I just got hustled.”

Nicky just grinned, completely unapologetic.

Before Rio could say anything else, the sound of the door opening caught her attention. She turned to see Agatha stepping out into the courtyard, arms crossed, one perfectly arched brow raised.

“You’ve been in my building for an hour, and you’re already luring my son to the dark side?” Agatha drawled.

Rio grinned. “What can I say? The force is strong with this one.”

Nicky laughed, but at the look Agatha shot him, he had the sense to at least try and look guilty.

“Nicky, go grab your things. We’re heading home soon.”

“But Mom—”

“No buts,” Agatha said, though her voice was more exasperated than stern. “Go.”

Nicky sighed dramatically but obeyed, heading inside.

Rio leaned back against the bench, stretching her arms out. “You know, you should be thanking me. Kid’s got talent.”

“I know he has talent,” Agatha said. “That doesn’t mean I want you filling his head with ideas of running off to become a rockstar.”

Rio smirked. “Relax, Harkness. I’m not trying to recruit him into The Coven.”

“Good. Because my son is not going on tour with you.”

“Damn,” Rio said. “And here I was, ready to offer him a spot as our new lead guitarist.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but there was something almost amused in the way she looked at her. Almost.

Before Rio could push her luck, the door opened again, and Mia stepped out.

“I’m ready,” Mia said, her voice carefully neutral.

Rio took one look at her and knew something was off.

“Everything okay, kid?”

Mia hesitated for half a second—so quick that most people wouldn’t have noticed. But Rio did.

“Yeah. Just tired.”

Rio didn’t believe that for a second, but she let it slide. For now.

“Alright,” she said, pushing off the bench. “Let’s head home.”

Mia nodded and started toward the parking lot.

Rio turned back to Agatha, giving her a two-fingered salute. “Until next time, maestra .”

Agatha huffed but didn’t respond.

Rio grinned as she followed Mia to the car, already looking forward to the next time.

~*~

The drive home was quiet. Too quiet.

Rio kept glancing at Mia, who sat with her arms crossed, staring out the window. No music, no humming, not even the occasional complaint about traffic. Just quiet.

“Alright, kid,” Rio finally said, tapping her fingers against the wheel. “You gonna tell me what’s eating you, or do I have to guess?”

Mia exhaled sharply, fingers tightening in the sleeves of her hoodie. “Some girls at school were talking about you today.”

Rio scoffed. “That’s nothing new. What’d they say?”

Mia hesitated, then muttered, “They were showing off pictures they took with you somewhere. Saying how cool you are. How lucky I am to have the Rio Vidal as my mom.” Her voice was flat.

Rio frowned. “Okay… and that’s bad because?”

Mia turned her head, shooting her a sharp look. “Because they don’t actually care about me. They just want to know if I can get them backstage, if I can get them to meet you. If I can get them closer to you.” She let out a humorless laugh. “One of them even asked if you were single.”

Rio grimaced. “Wow. That’s weird.”

“Yeah. No kidding. Then I get outside, and other kids are already stalking you,” Mia slumped deeper into her seat.

Rio clenched her jaw. She hated this. Mia had been dealing with it since she was a kid—people who pretended to be her friend just to get to Rio. It wasn’t fair.

“That why you barely said a word when you got in the car?” she asked.

Mia nodded. “Figured it’d be easier than pretending I was fine.”

Rio sucked her teeth, trying to figure out what to say. She wasn’t great at this part—at fixing things with words.

“Look, I know this sucks,” she said finally. “I know you want people to see you and not just some extension of me. And I wish I could change that for you.”

Mia was quiet for a long moment. Then, finally—“You can’t.”

“I know,” Rio admitted.

The car fell into silence again, but this time, it wasn’t so heavy.

“For what it’s worth,” Rio said, giving Mia a sideways glance, “Agatha seems to get you. Which is kinda impressive considering she’s only known you for two seconds.”

Mia made a small noise, like she wasn’t sure how to respond to that.

Rio smirked. “And hey, if all else fails, you can always start wearing a fake mustache to school. That way no one will know you’re my kid.”

Mia let out a reluctant snort. “You’re ridiculous.”

“Ah, but I’m your ridiculous mom.”

Mia rolled her eyes, but Rio could see the tension in her shoulders loosening.

She took the win as she pulled into their driveway. “C’mon. Let’s go inside before you decide to move out and start a new life in the woods.”

Rio shut off the engine but didn’t move to get out. Instead, she turned to Mia, draping an arm over the steering wheel.

“Alright, tell me something good—how was your lesson?”

Mia had been halfway to unbuckling her seatbelt, but she froze for a second, like she hadn’t expected the question. Then—just like that—something in her shifted. The sulking, the frustration, the weight of the school day—it all faded into something lighter.

“It was… good,” she said, and for once, she didn’t sound like she was just saying it to appease Rio. She sounded genuine.

Rio raised a brow. “Just good?”

Mia bit her lip, and Rio swore she saw the start of a smile. “Fine. It was really good.”

“Uh-huh. And?”

Mia huffed, but now she was definitely smiling. “And she’s really— I mean, she’s intense, but in a good way? Like, she actually listens. And she didn’t just throw a bunch of scales at me and call it a day. We talked about composers, and how music is supposed to say something, and—”

She cut herself off, as if she realized she was getting too excited. But Rio wasn’t about to let her backtrack.

“Oh no, don’t stop now. I was enjoying that,” Rio teased, grinning.

Mia rolled her eyes, but the warmth in her face didn’t fade. “She said I have a good ear for phrasing. And that my technique is strong.” A pause. Then, softer, almost hesitant— “I think she actually respects me.”

Something in Rio’s chest twisted. She reached over, ruffling Mia’s hair just to see her swat her hand away.

“Of course she respects you. You’re amazing.”

Mia shook her head, but she wasn’t arguing. Not really.

Rio smirked. “Careful, kid. If you start liking classical music too much, you might end up one of those super serious concert pianists. Imagine the horror.”

Mia shot her a look but still couldn’t hide the happiness on her face. “Let’s just go inside.”

Rio laughed, stepping out of the car. As they headed for the door, she glanced at Mia again—shoulders relaxed, a spark of something real in her eyes.

Yeah. That was way better.



Three

Chapter Notes

I'm so so happy to see you're enjoying this. Thank you so much for your thoughtful comments!

Agatha had seen many things in her life. The rise and fall of entire symphonies. The chaotic brilliance of a concert hall before the first note was struck. The way a student’s face lit up when they finally mastered a piece that had once seemed impossible.

But nothing—nothing—could have prepared her for the sheer, unshakable admiration her son had developed for Rio Vidal.

It had been four weeks since Amelia Vidal started as her student, and Agatha had to admit, the girl was exceptional. Focused. Disciplined. Talented in a way that went beyond natural skill—Amelia worked for it, studied each note with the kind of precision Agatha rarely saw in someone so young. But while Amelia’s progress at the piano had been impressive, it was nothing compared to the other thing that had completely spiraled out of control.

Nicky’s enthusiasm for Rio had started as a spark. A simple, casual admiration for a musician he already adored. But then Rio—legendary rockstar, famed guitarist, walking chaos incarnate—had made the mistake of jamming with him once. Just once.

It had happened in the small courtyard behind Sonata Grove, beneath the shade of a sprawling tree, where Rio had pulled out a guitar and played alongside him like it was the most natural thing in the world. That moment had changed everything.

Now, every Wednesday, Rio brought her own guitar, and Nicky all but counted down the hours until she showed up.

So today, when Mia arrived alone, Agatha felt Nicky’s disappointment before he even spoke.

“Where’s Rio?” Nicky asked, adjusting his backpack strap, his voice carefully neutral.

Mia sighed, shifting her bag higher on her shoulder. “She’s in the studio today.”

Nicky didn’t groan or complain, but Agatha noticed the slight slump in his posture, the way his fingers twitched at his sides.

“Oh,” he said, trying for casual and missing the mark entirely. “Cool. That’s—cool.”

Agatha shot him a look, but he ignored it.

“She told me to tell you she’ll see you next week,” Mia added, clearly picking up on his disappointment.

Nicky nodded, recovering quickly. “Yeah. Yeah, of course. It’s not like I was waiting or anything.”

Agatha almost rolled her eyes. If Rio Vidal had any idea how much power she held over her son’s emotions, she would never let him live it down.

~*~

Agatha sat at the piano bench, watching as Amelia settled beside her. The girl was quieter than usual, her fingers flexing like she was working out some unseen tension.

“Shall we begin?” Agatha asked.

Mia nodded but didn’t immediately place her hands on the keys. Instead, she exhaled sharply. “Can I ask you something?”

Agatha arched a brow. “Of course.”

Mia hesitated, then muttered, “Did you always want to be a musician?”

That wasn’t what Agatha had expected, but she answered without missing a beat. “Yes. There was never a time I didn’t want this.”

Mia nodded, filing that away. Then, in a quieter voice, “Must be nice.”

Agatha studied her, noting the slight bitterness in her tone. “You don’t want to be a musician?”

Mia huffed. “I do. Just… not the way everyone assumes I do.”

She flexed her fingers again, as if music might settle the restlessness inside her. “Everyone just expects me to pick up a guitar and start a band. Like I’m some kind of mini-Rio, just waiting to take the stage.” She let out a humorless laugh. “Doesn’t matter how many times I say I want to compose. That I want to play in an orchestra, maybe even conduct one someday. No one hears me. They just hear what they think I should want.”

“And at school?” Agatha prompted.

Mia scoffed. “They don’t even see me. They see Rio Vidal’s daughter. Like I’m a walking backstage pass.” She flexed her jaw. “Some of them act like I’m some kind of celebrity. Others think I must be full of myself because of who my mom is. Either way, they don’t care about me—just what my last name can do for them.”

Agatha was quiet for a moment. Then, “That sounds infuriating.”

Mia blinked at her, like she hadn’t expected such a simple acknowledgment. “It is,” she admitted.

“Does your mother know?”

Mia let out a breath. “She knows… some of it. She’s seen the way people treat me. She hates it.” A pause. “But she doesn’t know how to fix it.”

That, Agatha thought, made sense.

Mia continued, “She always tells me to own it. To not let them get to me. But that’s easy for her. She’s—she’s Rio Vidal. No one’s ever ignored her in their life. No one ever would.” Her fingers tightened on her lap. “And when she does try to help, it just makes it worse. If she posts about me or shows up to something, suddenly everyone remembers I exist again—but not as me. Just as an extension of her.”

Agatha considered that. Considered the way parents, even the most well-meaning ones, could fail to see the full picture.

“For what it’s worth,” Agatha said eventually, “I see you, Mia.”

Mia’s breath hitched almost imperceptibly.

Then she straightened her shoulders, placed her hands on the keys, and said, “Can we start now?”

Agatha only nodded, her chest unexpectedly tight as she turned her attention back to the music.

~*~

 

Friday night dinners at Agatha’s house had been a tradition for years, an anchor in the chaos of life. No matter what was happening, Wanda, Viz, Lilia, and the kids always found their way to her dining table by the end of the week. It was loud, messy, and often involved at least one near food fight between the boys, but Agatha wouldn’t trade it for anything.

She set down a dish of roasted vegetables in the center of the table just as Wanda poured them both a glass of wine.

“Alright,” Wanda said, settling into her chair. “Weekly recap—who has grievances to air?”

Billy immediately raised his hand. “Tommy stole my game controller and then lied about it.”

“I didn’t lie,” Tommy said. “I borrowed it.”

“Without asking!”

“That’s still borrowing.”

“No, it’s stealing—”

“Okay,” Viz cut in, rubbing his temples. “New rule: no litigating sibling disputes at the dinner table.”

Lilia smirked. “Where’s the fun in that?”

“It’s fun for you because you get to watch the chaos,” Wanda said, nudging Agatha’s arm. “Speaking of chaos—how’s your celebrity student doing?”

Agatha exhaled slowly, already regretting telling Wanda anything. “Amelia is doing well. Very focused, very talented.”

“And her mother?”

Agatha gave her a look. “Not my student.”

“No, but she is at your school constantly now, isn’t she?” Wanda teased, taking a sip of her wine.

Agatha resisted the urge to roll her eyes. “She’s just there to bring Amelia. And to play guitar under a tree with my son, apparently.”

“Ah, so she’s spending time with Nicky? You must love that,” Lilia said, smirking.

Agatha scoffed. “He already idolized her. Now it’s somehow gotten worse.” She glanced at Nicky, who was pushing food around his plate. “Especially since she didn’t show up this week.”

“She didn’t?” Wanda raised a brow. “And that ruined his whole day, huh?”

“Basically,” Agatha muttered.

“Hey,” Wanda said, turning to Nicky. “I know it sucks, bud, but rockstars have unpredictable schedules. Maybe she had something come up.”

Nicky sighed. “I know, I just… I thought maybe she’d actually want to jam again. It’s been fun.”

“Maybe she does want to,” Viz offered. “You never know.”

Billy, grinning, leaned in. “You do know you’re living every fan’s dream, right?”

“It’d be my dream if she actually showed up,” Nicky muttered.

Agatha smirked. “Welcome to the world of musicians, kid. We’re an unreliable bunch.”

“You’re not,” Nicky pointed out.

“No, but I’m the exception to the rule,” Agatha said, sipping her wine.

~*~

The following week, Rio showed up.

Agatha knew the moment she walked through the doors of Sonata Grove—not because she saw her first, but because of Nicky.

He had been sitting at the front desk, doodling absently in his notebook while Wanda balanced the books. The second the glass doors swung open, Nicky’s entire body went rigid, his pencil freezing mid-stroke. Then, as if propelled by some unseen force, he launched himself to his feet, nearly knocking his chair over in the process.

“You came!” he practically shouted, eyes wide with excitement.

Before Agatha could remind him of the importance of personal space, he launched himself at Rio in a full-bodied hug.

Agatha didn’t know who was more startled—her or Rio.

For a brief second, Rio tensed, clearly caught off guard. But then, something in her face softened. The smirk that usually curled at her lips faded into something more open, more unguarded. She let out a small breath and ruffled Nicky’s hair, her touch light, almost hesitant.

”‘Course I came,” she said, as if it were obvious. “I said I would, didn’t I?”

Nicky beamed up at her, practically vibrating with excitement. “I saved our spot! C’mon, let’s go.”

“Alright, alright, give me a second, kid,” Rio said with a small chuckle, gently prying him off.

Agatha, arms crossed, watched the exchange with a mixture of amusement and exasperation. “If you corrupt my child any further, I’ll have to take legal action.”

Rio smirked. “Define corrupt.”

“Encouraging him to have a rockstar’s sense of responsibility, for starters.”

“Hey, I showed up today, didn’t I?” Rio shot back, tipping an imaginary hat. “That’s gotta count for something.”

“Barely,” Agatha deadpanned.

“Are you guys gonna argue, or can we go play?” Nicky interrupted impatiently, shifting from foot to foot.

“By all means,” Agatha gestured toward the courtyard. “Take your bad influence outside.”

“Aye, aye, ma’am.” Rio threw her a lazy two-finger salute before following Nicky out the back doors, her guitar case slung over her shoulder.

Agatha sighed, shaking her head. A bad influence indeed.

Her gaze flicked toward Amelia, who had been standing quietly to the side, watching the exchange. Agatha caught the slight crease between her brows, the way her arms stayed crossed over her chest—not defensive, exactly, but… careful.

“Come on, Amelia,” Agatha said, shifting gears. “Let’s get started.”

Amelia’s lips pressed together briefly, but she followed without protest.

The lesson went well. Exceptionally well, in fact.

Amelia was progressing at an impressive rate, and Agatha made sure to tell her so.

“Your technique is improving,” she noted as she watched Amelia’s fingers glide over the keys, coaxing out a melody with steady confidence.

Amelia, as always, just shrugged like it was no big deal. But Agatha caught the tiny flicker of satisfaction in her eyes, the way her shoulders straightened ever so slightly.

“Have you been practicing extra?” Agatha asked, tilting her head.

Mia hesitated for a fraction of a second before shrugging again. “Maybe.”

That was as close to an admission as Agatha was going to get, and she smiled to herself as she turned the page of the sheet music.

After the lesson, as they walked back to the reception area, Agatha spotted a teenage boy waiting by the front desk.

He was tall and lanky, with dark hair that flopped over his forehead and a hoodie that looked two sizes too big for him. He was leaning against the counter, spinning a pen between his fingers, his expression a mix of boredom and barely contained energy.

Then Amelia walked in.

“Hey,” he said immediately, stuffing his hands into his hoodie pockets, his entire face brightening.

Amelia, who had spent the past hour schooling her expressions into their usual careful neutrality, cracked an actual smile. “Hey, Will.”

Ah.

Agatha recognized that look—the kind of easy familiarity that only came with time, the way Amelia’s  usually guarded posture eased just slightly. It was trust, comfort.

“William Kaplan,” Wanda supplied helpfully from behind the desk, clearly picking up on Agatha’s curiosity. “Her best friend apparently.”

Agatha hummed in understanding, watching as Amelia and William fell into an easy back-and-forth, their conversation already in full swing as if they hadn’t missed a beat.

Interesting.

Deciding to give her space, Agatha turned on her heel and went in search of her own son—who, if she knew him at all, was still outside under that tree, completely enraptured by the woman ruining his good sense.

Agatha stepped out into the courtyard, already knowing what she would find.

And sure enough, there they were—Rio sitting cross-legged on the ground, guitar in her lap, Nicky beside her, practically vibrating with excitement.

“Okay, little man,” Rio was saying, tuning one of the strings with a practiced flick of her fingers. “Let’s try that again. What’s the first chord?”

“G major!” Nicky said immediately, sitting up straighter.

Rio grinned. “Look at you, already a rockstar.”

Agatha folded her arms, leaning against the doorframe as she watched the scene unfold.

She’d spent the past few weeks watching Rio become something of a fixture in her son’s life, and as much as she wanted to pretend it didn’t bother her, it did.

Not because Rio was a bad influence—despite what Agatha might have joked about—but because of the way Nicky lit up around her. The way he looked at her like she hung the stars in the sky.

She had spent the past decade being her son’s entire world, and now here was this woman—this loud, brilliant, reckless woman—who had waltzed into their lives with her damn guitar and stolen that place in a matter of weeks.

It was infuriating.

“I see you’re still corrupting my child,” she said dryly, finally making her presence known.

Rio glanced up at her, looking entirely unrepentant. “And look at him, thriving.”

Nicky turned to Agatha, eyes pleading. “Mom, can I show you what I learned?”

Agatha sighed, pushing off the doorframe. “Go ahead.”

He scrambled to his feet, snatching his own guitar from where it rested against the bench. Rio nodded at him encouragingly, giving him a four-count before they both started playing.

And to Agatha’s surprise—he had actually improved. A lot.

He was still a little clumsy, his fingers sometimes hesitating before shifting to the next chord, but the progression was there. The foundation. And more importantly, the joy.

Because Nicky was beaming, practically glowing as he played alongside Rio, who was nodding in encouragement, playing along with him.

Damn it.

Damn her.

Agatha sighed, running a hand down her face. “I suppose it is good practice,” she admitted begrudgingly.

Rio smirked. “Don’t worry, Harkness. I’ll have him headlining stadiums in no time.”

“God help me,” Agatha muttered.

Agatha clapped her hands together. “Alright, bud, time to wrap it up. Go get your things so we can head home.”

Nicky let out a dramatic groan but didn’t argue, setting his guitar down carefully before running off inside.

Which left Agatha alone with Rio.

The silence between them wasn’t exactly uncomfortable, but it wasn’t easy either. Agatha wasn’t sure if that was because of Rio’s general existence or because of how aware she’d become of her own reactions to her lately.

The way Rio carried herself—so at ease, so self-assured—was infuriating. And distracting.

Agatha exhaled sharply, deciding to focus on the only thing she could control. “I hope you realize you’ve created a monster,” she said.

Rio tilted her head, smirking. “Yeah? He’s got talent.”

“And now he won’t shut up about you,” Agatha muttered, crossing her arms. “Do you have any idea how exhausting it is to listen to a ten-year-old wax poetic about your guitar solos?”

Rio laughed, leaning back on her hands. “You sound jealous.”

Agatha’s jaw tightened. “I am not—”

“Relax, Harkness.” Rio grinned, looking infuriatingly pleased with herself. “I’m flattered. The kid’s cool.”

Agatha let out a slow breath, pinching the bridge of her nose. “Yes, well, I would appreciate it if you didn’t fill his head with the idea that he’s going to be some rockstar prodigy.”

Rio raised an eyebrow. “Why not?”

“Because he’s ten,” Agatha said. “Because he gets obsessed with things and then forgets about them in a month. Because I know how this industry works, and it’s brutal. He’s not ready for that.”

Rio was watching her now, the teasing glint in her eyes softening into something more thoughtful. “You don’t have to be so scared for him, you know.”

Agatha’s jaw clenched. “I’m not scared—”

“Yeah, you are,” Rio said simply, still watching her with that quiet, almost infuriating understanding.

Agatha opened her mouth, but nothing came out.

Because, goddamn it, she was scared.

She had spent years making sure Nicky had stability, had safety. Had her.

And now here was this woman—this rockstar—walking into their lives, capturing Nicky’s attention, showing him a world Agatha had spent years trying to keep at bay.

Rio must have seen something shift in her face, because her voice softened. “I get it, you know. Wanting to protect them. Wanting to keep them from making mistakes, or getting their hopes up about something they might not even want in a year.”

Agatha blinked, caught off guard.

Rio shrugged, her gaze drifting toward the entrance of the school. “Mia’s a great musician. If she wanted, she could take over the world. But she doesn’t want what I want. She doesn’t want this life. And as much as I wish she did sometimes, that’s not my call to make.”

Agatha hadn’t expected this. Hadn’t expected this Rio—the one who wasn’t just a freewheeling rockstar but a mother who understood exactly what Agatha was feeling.

“She’s lucky you get that,” Agatha found herself saying, quieter than she intended.

Rio let out a dry laugh. “Maybe. Doesn’t make it easier, though.”

That—that—Agatha understood.

She exhaled slowly, glancing toward the school. “Just… don’t make promises you can’t keep,” she muttered, before turning toward the building to find Nicky.

And behind her, Rio let out a quiet, knowing hum.

“Noted.”

~*~

The rest of the week passed in a blur, and before Agatha knew it, she was right back at Sonata Grove, watching Nicky vibrate with anticipation, waiting for Rio to arrive.

Not that she’d admit it out loud, but Agatha had found herself thinking about their conversation more than she cared to. About the way Rio had spoken about Amelia, about the quiet resignation in her voice when she said it doesn’t make it easier, though.

It was one thing to acknowledge that she and Rio had some things in common—they were both musicians, both mothers, both deeply protective of their children. It was another thing entirely to admit that Rio Vidal, rockstar, actually understood her in ways not many people did.

The thought made her uneasy.

“She’s here!” Nicky all but shouted, snapping her out of her thoughts.

Agatha sighed, rubbing her temple as she watched Rio stroll through the entrance, guitar case slung over her shoulder, sunglasses perched on her head. “I don’t suppose I can convince you to keep your enthusiasm at a reasonable level?”

Nicky, predictably, ignored her. “Rio!”

Rio grinned, greeting Nicky with a casual fist bump before glancing at Agatha. “Good afternoon, Harkness. Looking serious as ever.”

“Some of us have responsibilities,” Agatha shot back, arching an eyebrow.

Rio smirked. “Right, and some of us just show up to corrupt children with music. Speaking of which—” She tapped her guitar case. “Ready, kid?”

Nicky practically lit up, looking at Agatha like he was about to start begging.

Agatha exhaled sharply. “Fine. Go.”

“Yes!” Nicky fist-pumped, already leading Rio toward their usual jam spot in the small courtyard.

Agatha watched them go, shaking her head.

“You’re doomed,” a voice said beside her.

She turned to see Wanda leaning against the reception desk, watching the scene unfold with an amused expression.

“You’re not helping,” Agatha muttered.

“I’m not trying to help,” Wanda said cheerfully. “I’m trying to enjoy this.”

Agatha shot her a look, but before she could retort, the door opened again and Amelia walked in, her bag slung over one shoulder, her usual quiet but purposeful demeanor in place.

“Good afternoon, Amelia,” Agatha said automatically.

Mia hesitated for a split second before sighing. “It’s Mia.”

Agatha blinked.

Mia shifted her weight. “I prefer Mia.”

Agatha didn’t say anything for a moment, then nodded once. “Alright, then. Mia. Shall we?”

Mia nodded, falling into step beside her as they walked toward the practice room.

Agatha didn’t miss the way Wanda was grinning at her from the reception desk.

She chose to ignore it.

~*~

On the drive home, the car was filled with the sound of Nicky tapping out a beat against his knees, humming an off-key version of whatever song Rio had taught him that afternoon. Agatha glanced at him from the corner of her eye, taking in the way he was practically glowing with excitement.

“I take it your jam session was a success?” she asked dryly.

“Mom, it was so cool,” Nicky gushed, turning to face her as if she wasn’t, in fact, trying to navigate Los Angeles traffic. “Rio taught me this really sick riff—like, I’m still kinda slow at it, but she said I’m picking it up fast. And then she let me try her guitar, and it was amazing. It felt so different from mine, and she said that’s because of the action and the strings, and she told me all about how she customizes hers to fit her playing style—”

Agatha hummed in response, letting him ramble as she focused on the road.

”—and then she told me about this time when her band played this tiny venue, and the power went out, but they kept going with just an acoustic set, and the crowd loved it. And then she said she might teach me one of The Coven’s songs—like, a real one, not just some random riff—”

That got Agatha’s attention. “I see,” she said, voice carefully neutral.

Nicky caught the shift in her tone and rolled his eyes. “Relax, Mom. It’s not like she’s trying to get me to drop out of school and go on tour with her.”

“Not yet,” Agatha muttered.

“Oh my God,” Nicky groaned, slumping dramatically against his seat. “You’re so dramatic.”

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “Pot, meet kettle.”

Nicky huffed but didn’t argue. He went back to tapping his fingers against his knees, a little more thoughtful this time.

“You know,” he said after a moment, “she’s actually a really good teacher. Like, I didn’t think she’d be, since she’s, y’know… her . But she explains things in a way that just makes sense.”

Agatha tightened her grip on the wheel slightly. She hadn’t expected Rio to be bad with Nicky—heaven knew the woman had a natural ease with people—but hearing him actually praise her teaching skills was…

Well.

She wasn’t sure how she felt about that.

“I’m glad you’re learning something,” she said, keeping her voice even.

Nicky grinned. “I really am. She’s awesome.”

Agatha inhaled slowly. This was getting out of hand.

~*~

A week later, Agatha paused just outside the door to the courtyard, fingers tightening around her barely touched coffee. Through the cracked door, she caught the tail end of Nicky’s excited chatter, his voice practically buzzing with energy—the way it always did when he was talking to her.

“And it’s gonna be so cool, Rio. We always do it at the school, and we decorate everything all spooky, and Aunt Wanda goes all out with the fog machine—it’s awesome.”

“Wait, hold on,” Rio interrupted, amusement laced in her voice. “You’re saying your mom’s birthday is actually on Halloween?”

“Yup!” Nicky chirped. “She hates when people make a big deal out of it, but, like… c’mon. It’s Halloween. That’s, like, the coolest birthday ever.”

Agatha pinched the bridge of her nose.

“Yeah, I can see that,” Rio mused. “I mean, I don’t know her that well, but she does give off serious Halloween energy.”

Agatha swore she could hear the smirk in Rio’s voice.

“Right? That’s what I keep telling her!” Nicky said. “Anyway, it’s gonna be amazing. You should totally come.”

Agatha’s stomach did something strange and undignified.

“Oh, I dunno, kid,” Rio replied easily. “Sounds like a student thing. Your mom probably doesn’t want some random rock star crashing the party.”

“You’re not random,” Nicky said, as if the very idea offended him. “You’re, like, part of the school now. And besides, Billy and Tommy aren’t students, but they always come too. And Mia’s coming this year. So, like. You should come too. Obviously.”

Agatha shut her eyes.

“Mia’s going?” Rio asked, her voice shifting just slightly.

“Yeah!” Nicky said. “She said she’d come to the school party. And she’s really good at piano too. Mom’s super impressed.”

Rio let out a low chuckle. “That so?”

“Yup, I’ve heard talking about it with Aunt Wanda,” Nicky confirmed. “Anyway. You should totally come. Mom won’t say it, but I know she’d be happy if you did.”

Agatha’s eyes snapped open.

That little traitor.

She was not happy about this.

Not at all.

And she needed to put an end to this conversation before Rio Vidal got any ideas.

Taking a steadying breath, she schooled her face into careful neutrality and stepped into the room.

“Nicky,” she said, voice cool. “I wasn’t aware we were sending out additional invitations to my birthday party.”
