Nicky turned, entirely unbothered. “I mean. It’s just Rio.”

Agatha arched a brow, cutting a glance at Rio, who was lounging against the wall with her guitar, amusement flickering behind those dark sunglasses.

“Yes,” Agatha said flatly. “Just Rio.”

Rio smirked. “Hey, don’t look at me. This is all your kid’s doing.”

“Yes, I can see that.”

Nicky just grinned up at her. “You always say Halloween’s about surprises, Mom. This is a good one.”

Agatha leveled him with a look.

Nicky just smiled wider.

She sighed.

“I suppose it’s too late to take you back to the hospital and demand a refund?”

“Way too late, mom,” Nicky said cheerfully. “So Rio can come, right?”

Agatha just sighed in resignation.



Four

Chapter Notes

I have the worst cold and I feel like crap. But this one was almost ready, so I figured I'd post it already.

Let me know what you think! Comments will definitely make me feel better ;)

Rio hadn’t felt nervous about a party since she was a teenager sneaking into underground shows with a fake ID and too much eyeliner.

But as she adjusted the wide-brimmed hat atop her head, smoothing the fabric of the deep red coat she’d thrown over her matching corset, she had to admit—she felt the tiniest bit unsettled.

Which was absolutely ridiculous.

It was just a school party.

A school party full of children and teenagers and parents.

And Agatha Harkness.

Yeah. That was probably the part that was throwing her off.

“Okay, you’re, like, way too committed to the part, Ms. V,” Will said from the backseat as they pulled into the parking lot of Sonata Grove. “Did you actually buy that, or did you just have a full-on sexy witch costume lying around?”

Mia groaned. “Will, why ? That’s my mom.”

“I’m just saying,” Will went on, undeterred. “That’s not a last-minute costume. That’s a statement.”

Rio smirked, adjusting her hat as she cut the engine. “Maybe I just like to make an entrance.”

“Oh my God,” Mia muttered, shoving open the passenger door before Will could add more fuel to the fire.

Rio chuckled, stepping out after them. Sonata Grove was already fully decked out for the occasion—cobwebs draped over the front entrance, jack-o’-lanterns lining the walkway, a flickering faux candle casting shadows from inside each one. From inside, music played, the muffled sound of laughter and conversation filtering through the walls.

For a moment, Rio hesitated.

It wasn’t like she wasn’t used to walking into a crowded room.

She’d just never done it while feeling quite so… out of her element.

But then Mia glanced back at her, brow raised in something like curiosity—like she could see the hesitation but wasn’t going to call attention to it—and Rio straightened.

This wasn’t about her.

Mia had actually wanted to come.

And she wasn’t about to let her kid see her falter.

So she squared her shoulders, grinned at Will and Mia, and said, “Alright, kids. Let’s go scare some music nerds.”

And with that, she pushed open the door.

The moment Rio stepped inside Sonata Grove, she was hit with the scent of cinnamon and warm cider, mingling with the faintest hint of something floral—probably from the dozens of fake cobwebs and plastic bats hanging from every corner of the room. The place was alive with music and laughter, kids and adults alike milling about in a sea of costumes.

She adjusted the strap of her bag, where she had tucked away Agatha’s birthday present—nothing too dramatic, just something she thought she might appreciate—and the small bag of Halloween candy and new guitar picks for Nicky.

Then her gaze landed on her.

Agatha Harkness stood across the room, deep in conversation with the redhead she’d seen around the school a few times, dressed in a flowing, elegant black-and-purple witch’s outfit, the long sleeves fitted perfectly to her slender arms, the corset-style bodice hugging her waist, and the skirt cascading in gentle waves to her ankles. A matching wide-brimmed hat sat atop her dark hair, and— fuck .

Rio swallowed, hard.

Because that was a problem.

A real problem.

It wasn’t like she didn’t already know Agatha was attractive—she had eyes, thank you very much. But seeing her like this, in something that looked like it had been designed specifically to make Rio’s brain short-circuit, was… interesting.

And it got even more interesting when Agatha turned, locking eyes with her.

Because for a split second— just a second—Rio saw something there. Something like… admiration. Maybe even desire.

It was gone in a blink, replaced by her usual cool composure, but Rio had seen it.

Well, well.

She smirked, making her way through the room, only vaguely aware of Mia and Will peeling off in search of whatever teenagers did at these things. She had more important things to deal with.

Like handing Nicky his gifts—because she was absolutely not above bribing her number-one fan—and, of course, Agatha.

Because now that she’d seen that look, she was suddenly very interested in pushing a little harder to see what else Agatha Harkness was trying to keep under wraps.

~*~

 

Rio found Nicky first, because of course she did. The kid had a way of making himself impossible to miss—bouncing on his feet near the snack table, wearing a pirate costume complete with a toy sword and an eyepatch he’d pushed up onto his forehead.

“Rio, hey!!” he greeted her with enough enthusiasm to power an entire concert hall. “You came!”

Rio grinned, pulling the bag off her shoulder. “Of course I did. You invited me, didn’t you? Wouldn’t miss it.” She handed him the small bag of Halloween candy and the new set of guitar picks—sleek, black with silver details, ones she’d had custom-made. “Figured you could use some fresh ones.”

Nicky gasped like she’d just handed him a bar of solid gold. “No way. These are so cool!” He flipped one between his fingers, testing the weight, and then gave her the most serious nod a ten-year-old could manage. “You get me.”

Rio chuckled. “Yeah, I do.”

Before Nicky could launch into another excited rant, she felt a presence behind her—strong, poised.

Agatha.

She turned, already grinning, but whatever she was about to say completely vanished from her brain the second she got a proper look at Agatha up close.

Jesus fucking Christ.

Up close, the outfit was even more unfair. The dark velvet of her bodice hugged her frame like a second skin, the neckline just low enough to make Rio’s mouth go dry. The deep purple skirt swayed as she shifted, her dark hair spilling over one shoulder, lips painted a rich shade of red.

She looked… dangerous. The kind of woman who could ruin a person’s entire sense of balance with a single glance.

“Having fun?” Agatha asked, her voice perfectly measured, but Rio knew she’d caught her staring.

Yeah, you caught me, Harkness.

Rio grinned, lifting her bag off her shoulder. “Brought you something.” She pulled out a small, carefully wrapped gift. “Birthday and Halloween combo. Thought it’d be rude to show up empty-handed.”

Agatha’s brows lifted slightly, eyes flicking down to the present before returning to Rio’s face, as if trying to gauge what the hell she was up to.

Agatha took the gift, her fingers grazing Rio’s in a way that felt almost deliberate. Or maybe Rio was just imagining things. Yeah, let’s go with that before I do something stupid, she thought to herself.

“You didn’t have to,” Agatha said, but she was already unwrapping it.

Rio shrugged, forcing herself to sound casual. “Didn’t seem right not to.”

The paper fell away, revealing a sleek, leather-bound notebook, the kind meant for composing music. Agatha’s fingers traced over the embossed initials on the cover—A.H.—and for the first time that night, she looked genuinely surprised.

Rio looked down at her hands, suddenly feeling like she’d said too much without saying anything at all. “Figured you might like a fresh place to put your genius.”

Agatha’s lips parted slightly, something shifting in her expression. For a second, Rio swore she saw a flicker of something dangerously close to warmth, maybe even gratitude. But just as quickly, it was gone, replaced by that signature smirk.

“Flattery will get you nowhere,” Agatha teased, but she held the notebook with an almost reverent grip, like she actually did appreciate it.

Rio smirked, tilting her head. “Wouldn’t dream of it.”

As Agatha turned the notebook over in her hands, Rio leaned in just slightly, dropping her voice low enough that only Agatha could hear.

“Happy birthday, Agatha.”

Agatha’s fingers paused on the cover. For a moment, Rio thought she wouldn’t respond, but then she looked up, her expression unreadable.

“Thank you,” she said, her voice softer than Rio had ever heard it.

And damn it, if that didn’t make something shift in Rio’s chest.

Then, before the moment could stretch into something too obvious, Nicky came barreling in, grabbing her wrist and yanking her toward the stage.

“You have to come watch me play!” he insisted, practically vibrating with excitement. “Please, please, please?”

Rio chuckled, shaking off whatever weird thing had just happened between her and Agatha.

“Alright, alright,” she said, letting herself be dragged away. “I’ll watch you play.”

As she glanced back one last time, Agatha was still standing there, fingers lightly tracing the edges of the notebook. And this time, Rio didn’t imagine it—Agatha was smiling.

~*~

 

The party was in full swing, and Rio had lost count of how many times someone had come up to her, phone in hand, asking for a selfie. She obliged each time, because it was part of the deal, but it wasn’t exactly fun to constantly be pulled out of a conversation or a moment just to pose for a camera.

She was just about to retreat to a quieter corner when a familiar voice cut through the noise.

“Alright, that’s enough of that,” Agatha said, stepping in between Rio and a particularly insistent guest. “She’s off duty. Go bother someone else.”

Rio blinked as Agatha’s firm tone sent the person scurrying away, and then—before Rio could even get a word out—Agatha’s hand wrapped around her wrist, tugging her away from the crowd.

“You looked like you needed rescuing,” Agatha murmured as she led her toward a quieter corner of the room where a small group was gathered.

“I was handling it just fine,” Rio replied, though she couldn’t help the smirk tugging at her lips. “But I guess I should say thanks.”

Agatha shot her a look that was both exasperated and amused before stopping in front of her friends.

“Everyone, this is Rio Vidal,” she said, gesturing toward her. “Rio, this is Wanda, Lilia, and Viz.”

Wanda, a striking redhead in a vampire costume, gave her an easy grin. “Oh, we know who you are,” she said. “Nice to finally meet you officially.”

Lilia, a silver-haired woman dressed as some kind of dramatic sorceress, arched an eyebrow. “So you’re the one corrupting Agatha’s child,” she said dryly.

Rio let out a laugh, throwing her hands up. “Guilty as charged.”

Viz, dressed as—Rio squinted—some kind of futuristic knight, nodded politely. “Nice to meet you,” he said, before adjusting his glasses. “I do my best to keep these ones in line, but it’s a full-time job.”

Agatha scoffed. “Excuse you, I am perfectly respectable.”

Wanda snorted. “Sure you are.”

Rio found herself grinning, enjoying the easy banter between them. But what caught her attention the most was Agatha herself. Though she was keeping up with the conversation, her fingers were still lightly touching the edge of the notebook Rio had given her, almost absently. She had put it in the pocket of her skirt, just the top of it popping out, but it was unmistakably her gift.

The sight made something warm curl in Rio’s chest. It wasn’t often that she gave someone a gift and saw them actually cherish it. But Agatha?

Yeah, Agatha liked it. A lot.

And for some reason, that pleased Rio more than it should have.

~*~

Rio leaned back against the table, arms crossed loosely over her chest, as she watched Agatha banter with her friends. It was… different.

The Agatha she was used to seeing—the one in the crisp button-downs at Sonata Grove, the one who carried herself with an air of quiet authority, the one who always seemed like she had a hundred things on her mind at any given moment—was still there. But here, at this party, in her witch costume, glass of wine in hand, with her friends teasing her and making her roll her eyes in fond exasperation, she seemed… lighter.

Rio found herself watching her more than she probably should.

“You know,” she said, smirking as Agatha turned to her, “I think this is the first time I’ve seen you actually enjoying yourself.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow. “Excuse me?”

“You heard me.” Rio took a sip of her drink, studying her over the rim of her cup. “I see you here at school, all serious and in charge, and I’ve seen you around Mia, making sure she’s learning the right techniques and all that. But this? You’re smiling.” She gestured vaguely at her. “You’re having fun. Who knew you were capable?”

Agatha scoffed, shaking her head. “I do have fun, I’ll have you know.”

“Uh-huh. When?”

Agatha opened her mouth, then hesitated.

Wanda, ever the troublemaker, grinned. “No, no, I want to hear this. When do you have fun, Aggie?”

Agatha shot her a glare. “I will kill you.”

Wanda just laughed, and Rio chuckled along with her.

Agatha huffed, taking a sip of her wine before muttering, “I have fun.”

Rio leaned in, smirking. “Sure you do.”

Agatha narrowed her eyes at her. “I do.”

“Uh-huh,” Rio drawled, taking another sip of her drink. “Give me one example.”

Agatha hesitated again, and Wanda outright cackled.

“You have no example, do you?” Rio teased, enjoying how Agatha’s glare sharpened.

“I run a music school,” Agatha defended, as if that proved anything. “That’s fun.”

“Oh, yeah,” Rio said, grinning. “Super fun. Nothing screams ‘letting loose’ like organizing schedules and making sure kids don’t break expensive instruments.”

Agatha gave her an unimpressed look. “For your information, watching students improve, helping them discover their potential, and giving them the tools to succeed? That is fun.”

Lilia laughed, sipping her cocktail. “You sound like an inspirational poster, darling.”

Rio bit her lip, holding back a laugh, and Agatha sighed, clearly regretting all of her life choices.

But Rio, now fully entertained, pressed on. “Okay, so the school is fun. What else?”

Agatha glanced toward the party, as if searching for an answer. “I enjoy playing music.”

Rio tilted her head. “That’s work.”

“It is not,” Agatha scoffed, looking personally offended.

Rio grinned. “It totally is.”

Agatha exhaled through her nose, then said, “Fine. I enjoy spending time with Nicky and my friends. We do this every year.”

“So, what you’re telling me,” Rio said, looking delighted, “is that the one time a year you truly let loose is your own birthday party?”

Agatha looked like she was debating whether or not she should throw her drink at her.

Viz, chuckling, decided to step in. “To be fair, Agatha has never been the reckless type.”

Wanda smirked. “That’s not entirely true.”

Agatha immediately turned to her with a warning look. “Wanda .”

Rio raised an eyebrow. “Oh ? Do tell.”

“Wanda ,” Agatha said again, more forcefully.

Wanda, grinning wickedly, ignored her. “Let’s just say there was a time when someone wasn’t as uptight as she pretends to be.”

Agatha sighed heavily, pinching the bridge of her nose. “I already regret introducing you to each other.”

Rio laughed, enjoying every second of this.

She looked at Agatha again, and for just a moment, something softened in her chest. She liked this version of her. The version that was flustered, exasperated, and—for once—not completely in control. It made her wonder what Agatha would be like if she ever really let go.

That was an interesting thought.

Rio leaned in slightly, eyes glinting with curiosity. “Okay, now I have to know. What’s the most reckless thing you’ve ever done, Harkness?”

Agatha took a measured sip of her wine, as if she could buy time with it. Then she gave Rio a perfectly cool look and said, “Letting you hang out with my son.”

Lilia let out a dramatic gasp. “Scandalous.”

Rio laughed, shaking her head. “Alright, I walked right into that one.”

“You did,” Agatha said, smug now.

But Rio wasn’t done with her. “Come on, really though. I refuse to believe you’ve never done anything impulsive in your life.”

Agatha exhaled, considering her. “I make calculated decisions.”

“Oh my God,” Wanda muttered. “It’s exhausting being friends with you.”

Agatha shot her a withering look, and Rio grinned.

“You mean to tell me,” Rio pressed, voice full of mock disbelief, “that you’ve never gotten into trouble? Never had a reckless night? Never made out with someone just because you felt like it?”

There was something about the way Agatha’s lips parted, about the way her fingers tightened ever so slightly around her glass, that made Rio pause.

Wanda and Lilia exchanged glances, and Agatha, after a long moment, finally said, “Not since college.”

Rio’s curiosity sharpened. “Oh?”

Agatha gave her a look that said don’t push it, but Rio was already invested.

“College Agatha,” Rio mused, tapping a finger against her chin. “I bet she was something else.”

Agatha gave a slow, deceptively pleasant smile. “College Agatha,” she said smoothly, “would’ve eaten you alive.”

Viz choked on his drink. Lilia burst out laughing. Wanda looked like she was about to keel over.

Rio? She just stared at Agatha, feeling something unspool in her stomach.

And for once, she had absolutely no idea what to say.

The moment stretched between them, charged and humming, until Rio finally found her voice.

“Damn,” she murmured, still processing. “Now that’s an image.”

Agatha smirked, clearly pleased with herself. “I thought you’d like that.”

Before Rio could come up with an appropriately flirty response, a familiar voice cut through the air—one full of absolute delight.

“Mom! You have to come see this!”

Rio turned to find Mia approaching, Will at her side, both of them looking uncharacteristically excited.

“See what?” Rio asked, grateful for the reprieve (because what the hell had just happened with Agatha Harkness? ).

Mia gestured toward the small stage that had been set up in the corner of the room, where a group of kids—including Nicky and the twins—were gathered around what looked like an impromptu jam session.

“It’s Nicky,” Mia said. “He’s really good.”

At that, Rio perked up. “Yeah?”

Mia nodded. “Come on.”

She and Will led the way, and Rio turned back to Agatha, who was watching Nicky with an unreadable expression.

“You coming?” Rio asked.

Agatha hesitated, then sighed. “I suppose I should see what kind of corruption you’ve inflicted on my child.”

Rio grinned. “That’s the spirit.”

They made their way through the crowd, and as they got closer, Rio could hear it—Nicky, guitar in hand, playing with an ease and confidence that was damn impressive for a ten-year-old.

He was playing a riff she recognized immediately—one of her songs.

Oh.

Rio felt something tighten in her chest, something warm and almost painful. She glanced at Agatha, wondering how she was feeling about all this, but Agatha was watching Nicky with something close to awe.

Then, as if she felt Rio’s gaze, Agatha turned to her and said, very softly, “You’ve made him better.”

It wasn’t an accusation.

It wasn’t even grudging.

It was something else entirely.

Something that made Rio’s heart trip over itself as she looked at Agatha Harkness in the dim, golden light of Sonata Grove, listening to a boy who adored them both.

Oh.

She was in trouble.

Before either of them could address the quiet thing that had passed between them, Nicky came bounding up, eyes wide with excitement.

“Rio, you have to play with me. Just one song. Please?” His hands were clasped together in dramatic pleading, and his cap had shifted slightly askew from all his excitement.

Rio blinked, still reeling from whatever that was with Agatha, before letting out a breathless chuckle. “You sure you can keep up with me, kid?”

Nicky puffed up his chest. “I’ve been practicing.”

Agatha groaned beside her, pinching the bridge of her nose. “I blame you entirely for this.”

Rio smirked. “I take full credit.” Then, glancing back at Nicky, she jerked her head toward the little impromptu stage area. “Alright, kid. Let’s see what you’ve got.”

Nicky let out an actual whoop and bolted off to grab his guitar, leaving Rio standing there, feeling—unexpectedly—like she’d just agreed to something far more dangerous than a simple jam session.

When she glanced back at Agatha, she caught the way her lips had twitched, like she was trying not to smile. And Rio?

Rio was definitely in trouble.

Nicky was vibrating with excitement as he adjusted his guitar strap, fingers barely staying still over the strings. Rio crouched down slightly, giving him a conspiratorial grin. “Alright, what are we playing?”

Nicky’s entire face lit up. “Wicked Games.”

Rio arched an eyebrow, impressed. “Solid choice, kid. Let’s make it good.”

She strummed her guitar, testing the sound, and then—because she was incapable of half-assing anything when it came to music—she sank into the opening chords, letting the notes hum through the space. Nicky followed her lead, his playing a little hesitant at first, but he had good instincts. He listened, adjusted, and as the melody built, his confidence grew.

The crowd quieted as the familiar song filled the air, and Rio, caught in the moment, closed her eyes, letting herself feel the music.

When she glanced up again, her gaze immediately found Agatha.

And oh.

She was watching.

No—she was staring.

Agatha Harkness, the picture of composure, stood with her arms loosely crossed, her head tilted just slightly, and her eyes—dark, deep, entirely transfixed—were locked onto her.

Rio felt it like a strike of lightning, sharp and unexpected.

The rest of the song passed in a blur of sound and rhythm, and by the time they hit the last notes, Nicky was grinning so wide it was a miracle his face didn’t split in two. The moment the music stopped, the crowd clapped and cheered, and Nicky turned to Rio, breathless and starry-eyed.

“That was so cool.”

Rio smirked, ruffling his hair. “Not bad, rookie. We’ll make a rockstar out of you yet.”

Nicky beamed, but Rio’s focus drifted back to Agatha.

She was still watching her.

And for once, she didn’t look away.

The air between them felt different now—charged, something unspoken crackling in the space where Agatha’s sharp, discerning gaze met Rio’s. It wasn’t admiration, not quite. It wasn’t even simple appreciation.

It was something else.

Rio handed her guitar off to Nicky, ruffling his hair one more time as he ran off, chattering excitedly with the twins about his “epic” performance. But even as she joked with him, even as she smiled at his enthusiasm, she could feel Agatha’s attention lingering on her like a ghost touch.

And when she turned—when their eyes met again—Rio swore the breath stalled in her throat.

Agatha didn’t look away.

Didn’t hide behind her usual perfectly curated distance.

Instead, she took a slow, measured step closer, just enough that Rio caught the faintest trace of her perfume—something warm and dark, like vanilla and spice.

“Not bad, Vidal,” Agatha murmured, voice smooth as a well-played piano chord. “I suppose all those years of performing have made you somewhat competent.”

Rio huffed a soft laugh. “Somewhat competent? Wow, that almost sounded like a compliment.”

Agatha’s lips curved just slightly, but there was something else in her expression now—something thoughtful. Almost hesitant. She shifted her weight, fingers drumming idly against her opposite arm.

And then, in a rare moment of something like sincerity, she said, “He adores you, you know.”

It took Rio a second to realize she meant Nicky.

Something in her chest tightened. She exhaled through her nose, rubbing the back of her neck. “Yeah. He’s a good kid.”

Agatha hummed, glancing briefly toward where Nicky was still basking in the afterglow of his impromptu performance. Then, softer, “He doesn’t… get attached to people like that often.”

Rio blinked.

And just like that, the moment shifted.

This wasn’t just a casual remark. This was something real. A peek behind the curtain of Agatha’s guarded world.

Rio swallowed, suddenly feeling like she was standing at the edge of something she didn’t quite understand yet.

Before she could think of what to say, someone called Agatha’s name from across the room. She exhaled through her nose, sending Rio one last glance—still unreadable, still layered with things Rio couldn’t quite name—before stepping away.

And Rio, for the first time in a long time, found herself wishing she hadn’t.

 

Five

Chapter Notes

I hope you guys enjoy this one. As always, thank you so much for your lovely comments!

Agatha moved through the crowd on autopilot, offering polite smiles and murmured thanks to those who wished her a happy birthday. But her mind was elsewhere—back in that moment, standing too close to Rio Vidal, with the scent of her lingering in the air and the unmistakable pull of something unsettling coiling deep in Agatha’s belly.

She didn’t want to name it.

Didn’t want to acknowledge the way her skin still prickled where Rio’s gaze had lingered, the way her breath had caught at the sight of her playing—completely in her element, fingers dancing over the strings with an ease that made it look effortless.

It had been a long time since Agatha had felt anything like this.

Too long.

And that was the problem.

She took a slow sip of the wine Wanda had handed her at some point, hoping it would steady her. 

It didn’t.

Instead, she found herself scanning the room—looking for her, like some part of her had already given in to whatever this ridiculous pull was. And when she spotted Rio, laughing at something one of the kids had said, Agatha exhaled sharply, forcing herself to look away.

This was ridiculous.

This was impossible.

And yet—

“Alright, spill,” Wanda’s voice cut through her spiraling thoughts, and Agatha barely had time to school her expression before her best friend appeared at her side, arms crossed, lips curled in the knowing smirk that meant trouble.

Agatha sighed. “Spill what?”

Wanda arched an eyebrow. “Oh, I don’t know. Maybe the fact that you’ve been eyeing a certain rockstar like she’s a particularly complicated piece of music you really want to figure out?”

Agatha scoffed, taking another sip of wine. “Don’t be ridiculous.”

Wanda just grinned wider. “I love when you get all flustered. It means I’m right.”

Agatha shot her a glare, but Wanda just looped an arm through hers, dragging her toward the dessert table. Except Agatha could feel Rio’s presence across the room, like a song she couldn’t quite tune out.

And if Wanda noticed the way her grip tightened around her glass, she was kind enough not to comment.

For now.

Agatha let Wanda drag her toward the dessert table, focusing on the spread instead of the lingering sensation of Rio’s presence in the room. The party was well underway, a lively hum of conversation and music filling Sonata Grove’s main hall. Normally, she would enjoy this—the warmth of good company, the ease of familiarity—but she felt anything but at ease.

Wanda was still watching her, clearly waiting for her to crack.

“So,” Wanda started casually, reaching for a mini pumpkin tart. “What did you think of her performance?”

Agatha hummed noncommittally, pouring herself another glass of wine. “She’s good.”

Wanda made a tsk sound. “She’s good? That’s all you’ve got?”

“She’s a professional musician, Wanda,” Agatha replied dryly. “It would be concerning if she wasn’t good.”

Wanda rolled her eyes. “Oh, come on. You were watching her like—”

“I was watching Nicky,” Agatha corrected, too quickly, too sharply.

Wanda raised her eyebrow again, unimpressed. “Right. Sure. Watching your son. That’s why you looked like you were about to either pass out or drag Rio Vidal into a dark corner.”

Agatha choked on her wine. “ Excuse me ?”

Wanda grinned, far too pleased with herself. “Oh, you heard me.”

Agatha leveled her with a glare. “I am not—”

“Incredibly attracted to her?” Wanda cut in. “Because Ags—” she placed a hand on Agatha’s arm, her expression turning far too knowing for Agatha’s liking— “I saw your face. And I saw hers.”

Agatha stiffened. “There was nothing on her face.”

Wanda snorted. “That’s hilarious. Because I distinctly remember her looking at you like she wanted to—”

“ Wanda .”

Her best friend smirked, then took a slow, deliberate bite of her tart. “I’m just saying,” she said around a mouthful. “You should—”

“I should nothing,” Agatha interrupted, then exhaled sharply, lowering her voice. “This is ridiculous.”

“You like her.”

Agatha scoffed. “I barely know her.”

“And yet you’re here all flustered.”

Agatha scowled, but Wanda simply grinned, enjoying this far too much.

Before Agatha could snap a response, she heard Nicky’s laughter across the room. He was still buzzing with excitement, chatting animatedly with Tommy and Billy. And next to him, Rio stood, hat now discarded, running a hand through her dark hair as she smiled at something Nicky said.

Agatha felt it again—the same unsettling sensation that had been chasing her all night.

It wasn’t just attraction, though she couldn’t deny that was part of it. It was something deeper, something unfamiliar, something she didn’t want to name.

She tore her eyes away. “I need more wine.”

Wanda just laughed.

~*~

As the party wound down, Agatha said goodbye to her students and their families, nodding along as many of them gushed about how incredible it had been to have the Rio Vidal at Sonata Grove.

She supposed it was a big deal. A world-famous rockstar at their little school event? Of course, people were excited.

Still, Agatha couldn’t help but feel a little exasperated as she overheard someone whisper, She’s even cooler in person.

Yes, yes. She’s magnificent. We should all bow before her.

Rolling her eyes at her own pettiness, Agatha turned her attention back to the room. That was when she spotted Mia.

The girl stood near a corner, arms loosely crossed, watching as yet another person approached her mother with a hesitant smile and a phone in hand.

Agatha braced herself, expecting Mia’s usual flicker of irritation.

But it never came.

Mia wasn’t tense or scowling. She wasn’t staring at the floor like she wanted to disappear.

Instead, she just… watched.

That was new.

Curious, Agatha approached. “Not annoyed this time?”

Mia turned, offering her a small shrug. “Not really.”

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “Interesting.”

Mia sighed, shifting her weight. “I dunno. It’s different here. At school, at events, it’s like I don’t exist. I’m just Rio Vidal’s daughter, and everyone acts like I’m some accessory to her life.” She gestured around them. “But here? This place is mine . This is my spot. So I don’t really care if people freak out over her. It’s not like she’s taking anything away from me.”

Agatha studied her, impressed by the self-awareness in those words.

She had seen it happening—Mia finding her place within these walls. The way she threw herself into her lessons, the way she focused, the way she came alive at the piano. It was the exact opposite of the reserved, uncomfortable girl she had first met weeks ago.

And now, Mia was finally acknowledging that.

Agatha offered her a small smile. “I’m glad you feel that way.”

Mia gave another shrug, but there was an ease in it this time. “Yeah. Me too.”

She glanced over at her mother again before straightening. “I should go look for Will, so we can go. Thanks for the party, Ms. Harkness.”

Agatha inclined her head. “See you next week, Mia.”

~*~

As the last of the guests trickled out, Agatha found herself lingering near the piano, listening to the quiet hum of conversation still floating through the room. She had just finished saying goodbye to Wanda and Viz when she felt a presence at her side.

“Hey.”

The voice was warm, familiar in a way that Agatha wasn’t sure she was ready to acknowledge. She turned her head and found Rio standing there, closer than expected, hands in the pockets of her red coat.

“Leaving?” Agatha asked, her voice steady despite the odd twist low in her stomach.

Rio nodded. “Yeah. Mia already stepped out with Will.” She tilted her head. “Figured I’d say goodbye before I go.”

Agatha inclined her head. “That’s very polite of you.”

Rio smirked. “I can be polite.”

“I’ll believe it when I see it.”

Rio chuckled, then let the sound settle between them. For a moment, neither of them spoke, the energy in the air shifting, crackling, as if something unsaid was hovering between them.

Then Rio exhaled, her voice quieter, more intentional. “Happy birthday, Agatha.”

Agatha opened her mouth, a response already forming, but it vanished the moment Rio reached out and touched her.

It was barely a touch—just the light press of fingers against her forearm, a fleeting, grounding warmth—but Agatha felt it everywhere. Her breath hitched, but she didn’t pull away. Couldn’t.

Rio lingered, thumb brushing absentmindedly over the fabric of Agatha’s sleeve before she let go.

Agatha exhaled, realizing only then that she had been holding her breath.

“See you next week?” Rio asked, as if nothing had happened. But the way her eyes flickered—like she knew something had—made Agatha’s pulse stutter.

She straightened, schooling her features into something composed. “See you next week.”

Rio grinned, that easy, knowing grin, and then she turned and walked away, leaving Agatha standing there, breath uneven, pulse thrumming, and deeply unsure of what the hell had just happened to her.

~*~

The restaurant was dimly lit, elegant without being pretentious, the kind of place Agatha had been meaning to try for months but never quite found the time for. Tonight, though, she wasn’t Professor Harkness, wasn’t Mom, wasn’t the carefully controlled head of Sonata Grove. She was just Agatha, out with her friends, drinking a very nice glass of red wine while Wanda and Lilia tried (and failed) to one-up each other with increasingly ridiculous stories about disastrous first dates from their youth.

It was perfect.

Their server had just brought out the appetizers—a spread of artisan bread, roasted olives, and a delicate burrata drizzled with balsamic—when Lilia leaned back in her chair and sighed dramatically.

“I am so mad I had to leave early last night,” she lamented, shaking her head. “I told them I needed the night off, but no—every other actor in the cast suddenly had an emergency, and I had to go on for all of them.”

“Don’t worry,” Wanda said, smirking as she cut into the burrata. “We only had a literal rockstar gracing our presence. She even performed. Nothing special.”

Lilia groaned. “That’s exactly why I’m mad! I heard she even performed after I left—tell me everything.”

Agatha took a long sip of her wine. “It was a school party, Lilia. Not a concert.”

Lilia scoffed. “Yes, and I am the Queen of England.” She turned to Wanda. “Spill.”

“She played a song with Nicky,” Wanda continued, undeterred. “You should’ve seen his face—kid was practically levitating.”

Lilia grinned. “And what about you, Aggie? I heard she gave you a present.”

Agatha set down her glass with an exasperated sigh. “I hate that Wanda has the biggest mouth on the planet.”

“Oh, darling,” Lilia purred. “You are so much fun when you’re flustered.” she leaned forward, eyes sparkling with mischief. “So? What did she get you?”

Agatha hesitated. She wasn’t sure why she suddenly felt so self-conscious about it. It was just a thoughtful gift. A strangely thoughtful gift, but still.

“A notebook,” she admitted, carefully keeping her voice neutral.

Lilia looked even more interested. Agatha wanted to die. “A notebook?”

“A personalized leather-bound notebook,” Wanda added knowingly. “With the most ridiculously high-quality staff paper I’ve ever seen.”

Lilia nearly choked on her wine. “Hold on. She gave you—” She turned to Wanda. “That’s not just a notebook, right?”

“No,” Wanda confirmed. “That’s a move.”

Agatha scoffed. “You’re both ridiculous.”

“No, you are ridiculous if you think we’re going to let this go.” Lilia pointed a fork at her. “That woman gave you a composer’s notebook. Do you understand what that means?”

“That she knows I’m a classical music composer? That I’m a pianist?”

Wanda rolled her eyes. “That she wants you to write something.”

Lilia snapped her fingers. “For her.”

Agatha scoffed. “She never said that.”

“She didn’t have to,” Lilia said smugly. “That’s what makes it brilliant.”

Agatha shook her head, reaching for her wine again.

“She also wrote in it,” Wanda added slyly.

Lilia gasped, looking delighted. “Did she really?”

“It was just one sentence,” Agatha muttered.

Wanda grinned. “What was it?”

Agatha hesitated.

A little magic for your music.

She hadn’t stopped thinking about it since she’d read it.

But there was no way she was telling them that.

“It’s not important,” she said instead, taking a deliberate sip of wine. “I don’t even know why you guys are being so obnoxious about this. I’m not even into women.”

Lilia and Wanda exchanged a look.

“Oh, Aggie,” Lilia said, shaking her head. “You are so screwed.”

Agatha was saved from answering by the sudden shift in the room’s energy. Conversations stuttered, heads turned, subtle murmurs spread like ripples in a pond.

And then she saw her.

Rio Vidal had just walked in, flanked by three other women who could only be her bandmates.

The entire restaurant practically buzzed with recognition. A couple at the bar subtly took out their phones, and a waiter practically tripped over his own feet trying to keep his composure as he led them to a table near the back.

“Oh,” Wanda said, a slow smirk pulling at her lips. “Well, well, well.”

Agatha stiffened. “Don’t.”

Lilia arched a brow. “Interesting. You’re already defensive.”

“I am not defensive.”

“You’re gripping your fork like a weapon,” Wanda pointed out.

Agatha scowled at her plate. “This was supposed to be a night off.”

“From what?” Lilia mused. “Your very normal and completely not tense interactions with your son’s favorite rockstar?”

“Exactly.”

Wanda hummed. “Right. Totally normal. Which is why you’ve been staring at her for a solid ten seconds now.”

Agatha forced herself to look away, suddenly very interested in the appetizers in front of her. But it was too late—her mind had already cataloged everything.

Rio wasn’t in a costume tonight, wasn’t playfully performing for an audience. She was just herself, all dark hair and easy confidence, dressed in ripped jeans and a fitted leather jacket that looked infuriatingly good on her. Her laugh—low and warm—cut through the restaurant as one of her bandmates said something, and Agatha hated that she recognized the sound immediately.

This is fine , she told herself. She’s not even looking this way. We will finish this meal, and I will go home, and—

Her thought process abruptly derailed when Rio turned, scanning the restaurant, and her eyes landed directly on Agatha.

There was a beat.

A shift.

And then, to Agatha’s absolute horror, Rio’s lips curved into a slow, knowing smirk.

“She saw you,” Wanda singsonged gleefully.

“She knows you saw her,” Lilia added.

Agatha let out a long-suffering sigh and picked up her wine glass. “I am going to need another drink.”

Agatha took a slow sip of her wine, schooling her expression into something neutral. Indifference. That was the key here.

She was an expert at that.

She just had to pretend that Rio Vidal’s smirk hadn’t sent a ripple of something entirely too dangerous through her bloodstream.

Easy.

Right?

“Wow,” Wanda drawled, utterly delighted. “That was intimate.”

Lilia, as always, was quick to pile on. “Did you see the way she looked at you?”

Agatha took a deliberate bite of her artisan bread. “No.”

Wanda huffed out a laugh. “Aggie. Sweetheart. Darling.”

Agatha scowled. “What?”

“She’s still looking at you.”

Agatha absolutely was not going to fall for that.

She stabbed at an olive. “Eat your food.”

Lilia, unhelpful as ever, propped her chin on her hand, grinning. “Oh, she’s making you work for it.”

“For what?” Agatha snapped, too fast, too sharp.

Wanda let out a scandalized gasp. “Oh my God. You want her to come over.”

“I do not.”

“Oh, yes, you do.”

“You’re both insufferable.”

Lilia waved her off. “We’re observant.”

“We just want you to be happy, Aggie,” Wanda said, placing a dramatic hand over her heart.

Agatha leveled her with a glare. “I am very happy.”

Wanda snorted. “Yeah, sure. You’re glowing with joy.”

Agatha resisted the urge to fling a piece of bread at her. “I am having a lovely evening with my dear friends.”

Lilia grinned. “And Rio Vidal.”

Agatha ignored her. “A lovely evening,” she repeated firmly. “And nothing— nothing —is going to disrupt that.”

Lilia hummed. “You know, it’s funny—”

“Doubtful.”

“—because it sort of looks like she’s about to get up.”

Agatha’s fork clattered against her plate. “She is not.”

“Uh-huh.”

“I’m not looking.”

“Okay.”

A pause.

Then Wanda said, far too smugly, “You’re going to cave.”

Agatha lifted her chin. “I have no idea what you’re talking about.”

Another pause.

Then, finally, finally—

She risked a glance.

And immediately regretted it.

Because Rio was still looking at her.

But worse?

So much worse?

The second their eyes met, Rio winked.

Agatha inhaled sharply, hating the way her stomach clenched, the way a heat curled low in her belly, the way—

“Oh, my God,” Lilia gasped, delighted. “Look at you.”

Wanda nearly choked on her wine. “This is so much better than I expected.”

Agatha slammed her glass onto the table, looking around wildly, desperate for an out.

And that was when she saw him.

A waiter—bless him—was coming their way, bottle of wine in hand, clearly prepared to top off their glasses.

Perfect. A distraction.

Agatha turned to him immediately. “You know what? Just leave the bottle.”

~*~

Agatha was fine .

She was perfectly fine.

She was enjoying a wonderful dinner with her dear—if insufferable—friends, and nothing was going to shake her.

Not Rio Vidal’s smirk.

Not her stupid wink.

Not the way her pulse had jumped in response to it.

She took a long sip of wine, listening very intently as Lilia launched into some dramatic retelling of a nightmare audition process.

It was working.

For a moment, she almost forgot—

Laughter.

Low, warm, familiar.

Agatha’s hand tightened around her glass.

She didn’t have to look to know exactly where it was coming from.

At the other end of the restaurant, a waiter had just finished pouring a round of drinks for Rio and her bandmates.

Rio accepted her glass with a lazy sort of ease, a grateful smile, something amused flickering in her eyes as an Asian woman muttered something to her.

Then, as if she could feel Agatha’s gaze—

Rio looked up.

Smirked.

And then—

Agatha’s stomach dropped as Rio suddenly pushed her chair back and stood. And now Agatha noticed she had taken her leather jacket off, wearing only a silk halter neck black blouse. Her tattooed arms were on display and Agatha felt her breath hitch when her eyes swept over how toned they were.

“Oh my God,” Wanda whispered, as if witnessing a miracle.

Agatha, wide-eyed, panicked. “No.”

“Yes,” Lilia beamed.

“No.”

“She’s coming over.”

Agatha’s breath caught.

And sure enough—

With all the confidence of someone who had never once questioned herself a day in her life, Rio crossed the room, easy and unapologetic, her gaze locked onto Agatha like she already knew how this was going to go.

And it wasn’t just Agatha’s table that had noticed.

As Rio weaved through the restaurant, more than a few heads turned, murmurs bubbling up in her wake.

Agatha barely heard them over the blood rushing in her ears.

Her fingers clenched around her napkin.

She willed herself to look bored. Indifferent. Unmoved.

Which was remarkably difficult given the way Rio was looking at her.

She stopped just short of their table, tipping her head in greeting.

“Ladies.”

Wanda and Lilia exchanged looks.

Agatha swore she heard a silent squeal of excitement from Wanda, but she didn’t dare check.

She forced a polite smile. “Ms. Vidal.”

Rio’s mouth tugged up at the corners, as if she found Agatha’s attempt at casual deeply amusing.

“Happy birthday,” she said smoothly, gaze dipping to the wine glass in Agatha’s hand. “Still celebrating?”

Agatha lifted her chin. “I like to be thorough.”

Rio huffed out a quiet laugh, eyes twinkling with something dangerous. “Can’t fault you for that.”

Lilia, who clearly had zero intention of behaving, leaned in, chin propped on her palm. “We were just talking about you, actually.”

Agatha shot her a warning look.

Rio raised an eyebrow, intrigued. “Yeah?”

Lilia, unfazed, beamed. “Your Halloween performance was the talk of the party, I hear.”

Rio turned to Agatha, playful. “Oh? What’d you think?”

Agatha set down her glass. “I think you’re quite accustomed to having an audience.”

Rio grinned. “And you’re not?”

Agatha refused to acknowledge the way her pulse skipped.

When Agatha only took a sip of her wine, Rio smirked, apparently infinitely amused at whatever she saw playing in Agatha’s expression.

“Anyway, I’ll let you get back to your dinner. Just wanted to say hi and wish you a happy birthday again, Harkness,” she turned to Wanda and Lilia and nodded. “Ladies, enjoy the rest of your evening.”

~*~

The night air was cool, but not cold—just enough of a crisp edge to remind Agatha that autumn had arrived, even in Los Angeles. She tugged her blazer a little tighter around herself as she and her friends stepped onto the sidewalk, the buzz of dinner still lingering between them.

“I vote for drinks at that rooftop bar Wanda likes,” Lilia said, stretching her arms over her head.

“Oh, now you want my opinion?” Wanda shot back. “I distinctly recall being ignored when I suggested the first restaurant.”

“You suggested an Italian place.” Lilia rolled her eyes. “You always suggest Italian.”

“Because Italian is good,” Wanda said, as if this was a universally agreed-upon fact.

Agatha let their bickering wash over her as she exhaled, feeling…content. She wasn’t usually one for big birthday celebrations, but shaking things up this year had been the right call. A night out in the city, good food, good company—what more could she ask for?

She barely had time to process that thought before the restaurant doors swung open again, and a fresh wave of noise spilled onto the sidewalk.

She didn’t have to turn around to know.

Rio Vidal had just stepped outside, the hum of her presence instantly shifting the energy on the street. Even without looking, Agatha could tell that a few people had noticed—whispers, stolen glances, someone subtly pulling out their phone.

Of course.

When she did glance over, she found Rio looking exactly as she always did—effortlessly magnetic, somehow both relaxed and impossible to ignore. The glow from the streetlights caught the silver rings on her fingers as she ran a hand through her dark hair, the leather jacket slung over her shoulders making her look every bit the rockstar she was.

Agatha turned her gaze forward, resisting the urge to sigh.

“Well, well,” came Rio’s voice, smooth and amused. “Fancy meeting you here.”

Agatha closed her eyes for half a second. Then, slowly, she turned.

Rio stood a few feet away, hands in her pockets, that insufferable smirk tugging at her lips. Her bandmates lingered behind her, still caught up in their own conversation, but Rio’s focus was entirely on her.

“Didn’t peg you for the ‘night out on the town’ type, Harkness,” Rio continued, head tilting slightly. “What’s next? Dancing?”

“As a matter of fact,” Agatha said pointedly, “we were just discussing where to go next.”

“Perfect,” Rio said, grinning now. “We were about to head to a club. Private spot. You should come.”

Agatha opened her mouth to refuse immediately, but—

“Oh, that actually sounds fun,” Lilia cut in before she could get a word out.

“Agreed,” Wanda added, surprising Agatha even further. “We should do something different tonight.”

Agatha turned to glare at them. “Since when are we the ‘go to a club’ type?”

“Since we got a VIP invite,” Lilia said. “Come on, Aggie. It’s your birthday.”

“She’s right,” Rio said easily, stepping just a fraction closer. “It is your birthday, Harkness. Live a little.”

Something about the way she said it—low, almost coaxing—sent an unwelcome prickle down Agatha’s spine.

She crossed her arms. “I’m already out,” she countered. “This is me living.”

Rio smirked, as if that answer delighted her. “Now you just have to take it a step further.”

Agatha hated that the challenge in Rio’s voice made something flicker in her chest.

Before she could formulate a response, Lilia leaned in and stage-whispered, “If you say no, she’s going to think you’re boring.”

Agatha shot her a withering look.

Rio, to her credit, didn’t look smug. She just looked…amused.

And maybe a little curious.

Agatha sighed again, long-suffering. “Fine,” she relented. “But one drink.”

“Obviously,” Rio said, voice full of mock innocence. “Wouldn’t dream of corrupting you, Harkness.”

Lilia cackled. Wanda pressed her lips together, clearly holding back laughter.

Agatha ignored all of them as she stepped forward.

Rio fell into step beside her, eyes gleaming in the streetlights, looking far too pleased.

Agatha refused to acknowledge the small, sharp thrill in her own chest as they started walking.

~*~

Rio led the way down the sidewalk, the city buzzing around them, her hands still stuffed in her pockets as if this was all perfectly casual. It wasn’t. Not for Agatha, at least.

She wasn’t sure if it was the way the night air carried Rio’s scent—something warm and slightly smoky, like cedarwood and leather—or the fact that she could feel Rio’s presence beside her, even without looking. Either way, something about this whole situation felt… dangerous.

“So,” Rio said, tilting her head slightly toward Agatha as they walked. “You’ve met me, but you haven’t met my band yet.”

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “And that’s a problem?”

Rio grinned. “Only if you don’t want the full experience of knowing Rio Vidal.”

“Oh, God,” Agatha muttered, just as Rio turned toward her group.

“Hey, guys,” Rio called, making the other three musicians look up. “Come meet Agatha Harkness. The Agatha Harkness.”

Agatha almost rolled her eyes.

The first to step forward was a short woman with red streaks in her dark hair and an expression that screamed troublemaker. She was dressed in a worn leather jacket, combat boots, and ripped jeans, looking exactly like someone who lived and breathed rock and roll.

“Alice Wu,” she said, voice low and confident, offering her hand. “Guitarist. It’s nice to finally meet you—Rio’s been talking about you.”

Agatha’s brows lifted at that, but she shook Alice’s hand briefly. “Has she now?”

“Oh yeah,” Alice smirked. “She’s got a lot of thoughts about classical music all of a sudden.”

Rio nudged Alice with her elbow, muttering something under her breath, but before Agatha could dig into that extremely interesting comment, another woman stepped forward.

She was striking, with a shaved head and an easy, self-assured smile. There was something effortlessly cool about her, the kind of presence that drew people in without trying.

“Jennifer Kale,” she introduced herself, shaking Agatha’s hand. “Keyboardist. And before you say anything, yes, I know I could probably learn a lot from you.”

Agatha snorted at that, finding herself a little charmed. “That remains to be seen.”

Jennifer grinned, then glanced toward the last person in their group, who had been standing slightly apart, watching with sharp blue eyes.

“Come on, Nat,” Rio said, tilting her head. “Don’t be shy.”

“Natasha Romanov,” she said as she stepped forward, extending a hand with an almost lazy elegance. “Drummer,” she added, voice smooth and cool. “And if you ever want to trade war stories about what it’s like being the serious one in a group of absolute maniacs, I’m available.”

Agatha liked her immediately. She shook her hand firmly, arching a brow. “I’ll keep that in mind.”

Rio made a wounded sound. “Excuse you, I am not a maniac.”

“Oh, you absolutely are,” Natasha said flatly.

Jennifer laughed. Alice smirked. Rio just sighed dramatically.

Agatha, against her better judgment, was amused.

“So,” Jennifer said, looking between them. “Are we all heading to the club, then?”

Agatha shot a glance at Wanda and Lilia, both of whom looked entirely too entertained by this entire exchange.

“I suppose we are,” she said.

Rio grinned. “Then let’s go.”

 

Six

Chapter Notes

I wasn't going to post this today, but I am dying to share this chapter with you. So I'm spoiling you today with a super quick update, but the next one will probably take a few days because I'm a student and a freelancer, who just decided she had to do a double major in Psychology and Biomedical Sciences, instead of just Psychology.

I know, I'm insane.

So my workload is about to double. But fear not, I have a few chapters drafted already for both this and Luminous--they just need to be polished.

Anyway, I hope you enjoy this one as much as I enjoyed writing it.

Rio had been to more clubs than she could count. She’d played them, partied in them, watched them rise and fall with the city’s ever-changing tides. There was a time when she thrived in them—when she fed off the high of neon lights, pounding bass, and the rush of people who wanted to be near her just because she was Rio Vidal.

But tonight? Tonight felt different.

She was aware of the crowd, of course. The way people whispered when they recognized her, the occasional bold ones who tried to get close. But that wasn’t what held her attention.

That was reserved for the woman currently walking just a step ahead of her, the dim lights of the club casting a soft glow against the curve of her jawline.

Agatha Harkness.

Rio still couldn’t get over the way Agatha had looked at her back at the restaurant—how her eyes had gone dark when Rio had gotten too close, the way her throat had moved when she swallowed, the tension that had crackled between them like the first warning signs of a brewing storm.

She wasn’t imagining it.

And now, watching Agatha navigate the club, stiff and poised like she wasn’t quite sure what to do with herself in this setting, Rio felt something almost like amusement curl low in her stomach.

She liked seeing Agatha a little out of her element.

More than that—she liked unsettling her.

“Oh my God, this place is packed,” Wanda shouted over the music as they weaved through the crowd toward the private section Rio’s manager had reserved.

“It’s a Saturday night,” Lilia pointed out. “Where else would people be?”

“Reading books,” Agatha muttered.

Rio huffed a laugh. “Do you actually read on Saturday nights?”

Agatha’s lips pressed together. Then, grudgingly, “Sometimes.”

“I’d love to know what Agatha Harkness’s guilty pleasure books are,” Alice teased, appearing at Rio’s side.

“I don’t have guilty pleasures,” Agatha replied primly. “I simply have good taste.”

Jennifer snorted. “Jesus. You’re even worse than Nat.”

“I resent that,” Natasha said mildly as they arrived at their section.

Rio slid onto the couch, ignoring the open space across from her and instead settling into the spot right beside Agatha. She stretched an arm along the back of the couch, her fingers nearly brushing against the back of Agatha’s shoulder.

Agatha, for her part, stiffened slightly. Not so much that anyone else would notice, but Rio noticed.

She smirked and relaxed further into the seat, watching as Agatha picked up a menu from the table, pretending to study it like it was the most interesting thing in the world.

Rio let the others talk for a bit, content to sip her drink and just watch.

It didn’t take long for her to start noticing things.

Like how Agatha avoided looking directly at her for too long.

Or how she seemed just a little too aware of where Rio was sitting, her posture stiff whenever their legs brushed under the table.

And then, of course, there was the moment Rio leaned over to pass her a fresh drink—fingers grazing against Agatha’s wrist in the process.

Goosebumps.

Rio saw them rise on Agatha’s skin, saw the way her breath hitched ever so slightly before she covered it up with a scowl.

Interesting.

Very, very interesting.

Agatha pulled her hand back, clearing her throat as she took the drink. “Thank you.”

Rio tilted her head, voice low and smooth. “Sure.”

Something flickered in Agatha’s gaze before she looked away.

Oh yeah. She was definitely affecting her.

And that knowledge settled into Rio like a slow, steady burn.

~*~

The others didn’t last long at the table.

Between the music, the drinks, and the energy of the club, it was only a matter of time before someone—Alice—decided they all needed to be on the dance floor.

“Come on,” Alice said, nudging Natasha and Jen. “We didn’t come here to sit around.”

Jen drained the rest of her cocktail, already sliding out of the booth. “She’s got a point.”

Wanda and Lilia exchanged a glance before Wanda shrugged. “I’m not saying no to dancing.”

“Neither am I,” Lilia agreed.

Agatha exhaled, already reaching for her drink as she watched her friends and Rio’s bandmates disappear into the crowd. “Thank God.”

Rio chuckled. “What? Not a fan of dancing?”

Agatha scoffed, turning her gaze back to Rio. “Not a fan of being pressed up against strangers in a room where the music is too loud, the air is too thick, and people have no concept of personal space.”

Rio stretched her arm out along the back of the couch, her fingertips brushing against the soft fabric just behind Agatha’s shoulder. “You mean to tell me you’ve never been out dancing?”

“I didn’t say that,” Agatha cut her a look. “I said I don’t enjoy it.”

Rio smirked, tilting her head. “That’s a shame.”

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “Oh?”

“I don’t know. I just feel like someone with your precision, your grace—” Rio gestured vaguely with her fingers, “—would have incredible rhythm.”

Agatha’s lips quirked slightly, as if she wasn’t sure whether to be annoyed or amused. “You’re trying to flatter me into dancing with you.”

“Is it working?”

Agatha exhaled through her nose, shaking her head. “Absolutely not.”

Rio grinned, studying her for a moment. The dim lighting of the club softened Agatha’s sharp edges, the neon glow from the dance floor casting deep purples and blues along her cheekbones.

God, she was beautiful.

“I still think you’d like it,” Rio said, tapping her fingers idly against her knee.

Agatha lifted a brow. “And why is that?”

Rio leaned in just a little, her voice lower now. “Because it’s not that different from playing music.”

Agatha scoffed, sitting back. “I highly doubt that.”

“No, really,” Rio insisted, shifting slightly so she was just a little closer, her knee almost brushing Agatha’s. “It’s rhythm. Movement. Letting the music take over.” She tilted her head, watching the way Agatha’s fingers curled slightly around her glass. “I bet if I put you in front of a piano right now, you wouldn’t even have to think about what your hands are doing. Your body would just know.”

“That’s muscle memory,” Agatha countered.

“And dancing is instinct,” Rio shot back.

Agatha huffed, amused despite herself.

“You know…” Rio said, voice dropping just a little lower, “if you came out there with me, I might be able to give you something better to add to your list of wild experiences.”

Agatha stilled, barely perceptible, but Rio caught it. She caught the way Agatha’s fingers twitched around her drink, the way her throat moved as she swallowed.

But then—of course—Agatha smoothed over whatever momentary reaction she had and scoffed. “You are relentless.”

Rio winked. “And you love it.”

Agatha opened her mouth—probably to deny it, probably to say something sharp and cutting—but before she could, someone suddenly appeared at their table.

“Excuse me—”

Rio barely held in a groan before turning to see a woman standing there, phone already in hand.

“I hate to bother you,” the woman continued, eyes wide with excitement, “but I’m such a huge fan. Could I get a picture?”

Rio sighed, already pasting on a polite smile. It wasn’t the first time this had happened tonight. Probably wouldn’t be the last.

But before she could answer, Agatha was already moving.

“I’ll give you a minute,” she said smoothly, grabbing her drink as she stood.

And for the first time that night, Rio wasn’t entirely sure if she was winning or losing this little game they were playing.

~*~

 

Agatha leaned against the bar, nursing what was left of her drink as she waited for the bartender’s attention. The momentary reprieve from the table should have felt like a relief, but she still felt unsettled.

Not just because Rio had been in her space, pushing, teasing—flirting.

And not just because Agatha had liked it.

The music thumped through the speakers, the low hum of conversation buzzing around her, but her mind was still stuck on the way Rio had leaned in close, voice low and inviting.

She exhaled, shaking it off as she caught the bartender’s eye and started to order—

Then, suddenly, a hand brushed lightly against her waist.

Agatha stiffened before she even had time to think, a wave of heat rolling through her as she turned to find Rio standing beside her, her touch already gone, but the impression of it lingering.

“Sorry,” Rio said, voice smooth and easy, as if she hadn’t just branded Agatha with that one, simple touch. “Didn’t mean to startle you.”

“You didn’t,” Agatha lied, shifting slightly, irritated by how aware she was of Rio’s presence.

Rio smirked, clearly not believing a word of it. “Sure.”

Agatha narrowed her eyes but said nothing, turning back to the bar as the bartender approached.

Rio slid into the space next to her, signaling for her own drink before tilting her head in Agatha’s direction. “So? Having fun yet?”

Agatha sighed. “You mean aside from the part where strangers keep interrupting to take a picture with you?”

Rio chuckled, leaning her elbow on the bar. “That is part of the experience.”

“How unfortunate for you,” Agatha said dryly.

“Hey, I could be worse. I could be dragging you to the dance floor.”

Agatha shot her a look. “You already tried that.”

“True.” Rio grinned. “But since that didn’t work…” She paused, then tipped her head toward the bartender. “Two shots of tequila.”

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “Absolutely not.”

Rio turned back to her with a mock-wounded look. “Come on, Harkness.”

“No.”

“Just one shot.”

“No.”

“It’s your birthday weekend.”

Agatha sighed sharply. “That is not a reason to subject myself to tequila.”

Rio smirked, watching her. “I think you’re just scared.”

Agatha scoffed. “Of what, exactly?”

“That you won’t be able to handle it.”

Agatha let out a sharp, humorless laugh. “ Please . I can handle my alcohol.”

“Oh, really?” Rio leaned in slightly, her voice lower now, knowing, teasing. “Then prove it.”

Agatha held her gaze, her pride flaring just enough to make her teeth clench.

She knew exactly what Rio was doing.

And it was working.

Agatha exhaled sharply, then turned to the bartender. “Make it double.”

Rio’s eyebrows lifted in delighted surprise, her grin widening as the bartender set up their shots.

“Well, well,” Rio mused, reaching for the salt. “Look at you.”

Agatha shot her a glare as she grabbed a lime wedge. “Don’t patronize me.”

Rio chuckled, grabbing a lime for herself before lifting her shot glass. “All right, then. Ready?”

Agatha rolled her shoulders, lifting her own shot. “More than you are.”

Rio grinned. “Now that’s what I like to hear.”

And then, together, they knocked back the first shot.

The tequila burned on the way down, smooth but with just enough bite to make it interesting. Rio hummed in approval, licking the salt from her lips before reaching for the lime wedge. She popped it into her mouth, grinning as the tartness hit her tongue.

Across from her, Agatha placed her shot glass down with a decisive clink, every movement controlled, deliberate—like she was determined to prove that tequila had no effect on her whatsoever. But Rio had been around enough people to recognize the subtle signs. The way Agatha’s shoulders had loosened just a fraction. The faintest warmth in her gaze.

And, most telling of all, the fact that she hadn’t walked away yet.

Rio smirked, tapping her fingers against the bar. “Round two.”

Agatha shot her a dry look. “You said one shot.”

“Did I?” Rio feigned innocence. “I don’t recall that.”

Agatha huffed but didn’t protest when the bartender poured again. Rio watched her as they took the second shot, noting the way Agatha exhaled slightly slower this time, the way her lips parted just a fraction as the warmth settled in.

Oh, this was fun.

“You really don’t do this often, huh?” Rio teased, propping her elbow on the bar as she turned to face Agatha fully.

Agatha dabbed at the corner of her mouth with a napkin, giving her a look. “What gave it away?”

Rio grinned. “You’re tense. Even now.”

“I am not tense.”

Rio didn’t argue. She just lifted a brow, then reached out and placed her hands on Agatha’s shoulders, giving a light, knowing squeeze.

Agatha jumped.

Rio bit back a laugh, but her smirk was impossible to hide. “Oh? What was that?”

“Nothing,” Agatha said quickly, straightening as if that would somehow erase what just happened.

Oh, this was very interesting.

Rio let her hands drift lower, smoothing over the line of Agatha’s shoulders, thumbs pressing just slightly into the fabric of her dress. She could feel the tension there—Agatha really didn’t know how to relax, did she?

Her hands drifted down Agatha’s arms, fingers barely ghosting over her forearms before skimming lower, teasing, testing.

And Agatha let her.

That was the kicker. Not just that she allowed it, but that Rio could see how it affected her. Could feel the shiver that ran through her, the way her breath caught just slightly.

“I think you like it,” Rio murmured, letting her fingertips brush the inside of Agatha’s wrist, slow and deliberate.

Agatha turned her head just enough to meet her gaze, her expression unreadable. “I think you think you’re a lot smoother than you actually are.”

Rio grinned, undeterred. “Maybe.”

Her thumb dragged lazily over Agatha’s pulse point, feeling the faint, quick beat beneath her skin.

Agatha swallowed.

Rio leaned in slightly, just enough to make it feel like a challenge. “I knew you were trouble,” Agatha muttered, though her voice was lacking its usual sharpness.

“Oh, definitely,” Rio murmured back. “But you love it.”

Agatha didn’t respond.

She didn’t have to.

The way she stood still beneath Rio’s touch, the way she hadn’t pulled away yet—that was answer enough.

~*~

Rio had never been the patient type.

She liked to move fast, feel things in real time, act on them before they slipped away. But with Agatha, she found herself savoring the moment—stretching it, pulling at the edges just to see how far she could go before Agatha pushed back.

Only… Agatha wasn’t pushing back.

Not really.

Sure, she was trying to pretend like she wasn’t affected—like Rio’s touch, her teasing, the way she leaned in just enough wasn’t sending shivers down her spine—but Rio could see it. Could feel it in the way Agatha’s body kept betraying her, in the way her pulse fluttered under her fingertips, in the way her breath hitched whenever Rio got too close.

Which was why Rio decided to take it a step further.

“So, tell me something,” she said, tilting her head, studying Agatha’s face as she sipped her drink. “When was the last time you went on a date?”

Agatha blinked, caught off guard. “What?”

“A date,” Rio repeated, grinning. “Dinner, drinks, maybe a little music in the background. You do date, right?”

Agatha scoffed, rolling her eyes. “Of course I do.”

Rio hummed. “So when was the last time?”

Agatha hesitated. Just for a second.

Then, she recovered. “That’s none of your business.”

Rio smirked, taking another sip of her drink. “That long, huh?”

Agatha shot her a glare. “I’ve been busy.”

“Right,” Rio drawled, amused. “Teaching, composing, raising a kid. Very noble, Harkness. But, uh…” She leaned in, lowering her voice just a little. “That doesn’t really answer my question.”

Agatha exhaled sharply, eyes flicking away for a moment before landing back on Rio, like she was trying to decide how much to give away.

Finally, she said, “A couple of years ago.”

Rio’s brows lifted in surprise. “Damn.”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “Like I said, I’ve been busy.”

Rio studied her for a moment, then asked, deliberately casual, “What about before that?”

Agatha frowned slightly. “What do you mean?”

Rio shrugged. “Just curious. I mean, you seem pretty… controlled. Like you don’t let people get too close. So was that a pattern or…?”

Agatha narrowed her eyes at her, catching onto something in her tone. “What exactly are you trying to ask?”

Rio smiled innocently. “Nothing. Just wondering what kind of person catches Agatha Harkness’s eye.”

Agatha’s lips parted slightly, her breath a little unsteady.

Rio saw it—the way she hesitated, like the question wasn’t just unexpected, but… complicated.

Interesting.

Finally, Agatha set her glass down on the bar with a deliberate motion and turned fully to face Rio. “What exactly are you asking, Rio?”

Rio leaned in, their faces close—so close—before grinning and pulling back just a little. “Relax, Harkness. I just like knowing what I’m up against.”

Agatha scoffed, but there was a new tension in her posture now, something defensive, uncertain. “You’re not up against anything.”

Rio just smiled. “We’ll see.”

Agatha was rattled.

Rio could see it—the way she squared her shoulders, the way she suddenly seemed too aware of every inch of space between them. And then there was the way she reached for her drink a little too quickly, as if she needed something to do with her hands.

It was fascinating.

Still, Rio let her be. She didn’t push, didn’t crowd her. Not yet. Instead, she let the moment settle, taking a slow sip of her own drink as she let Agatha wrestle with whatever thoughts were swirling in that sharp mind of hers.

Eventually, Agatha cleared her throat. “And what about you?”

Rio lifted an eyebrow. “What about me?”

Agatha’s eyes flickered to her, calculating. “What kind of person catches your eye?”

That made Rio grin.

“Oh, I have a type,” she said easily. “Women.”

Agatha’s fingers stilled on her glass. Just for a second, but Rio caught it.

A slow smirk tugged at Rio’s lips as she leaned in slightly, watching Agatha’s reaction. “I mean, I thought I was bi once. A long time ago. Turns out I just hadn’t figured myself out yet.” She shrugged, taking another sip of her drink. “I like women. Always have.”

Agatha made a noise, something half scoff, half exhale, and Rio wasn’t sure if it was amusement or something else entirely.

Rio stepped closer, but Agatha didn’t move any closer to her. There was a tension in the air, something delicate, something that Agatha wasn’t quite ready to expose just yet.

“What was it about?” Rio asked gently, her curiosity tugging at her. She could feel the weight of the music still hanging in the air between them, a question lingering unspoken.

Agatha paused, her gaze flickering briefly before she met Rio’s eyes again, but there was no immediate answer. She shifted uncomfortably, crossing her arms over her chest in a way that made her seem more distant, more protected.

“I don’t know,” she said, the words coming out in a whisper. “Just… feelings, I suppose.”

Rio didn’t push, sensing the hesitation in Agatha’s voice, the walls she had instinctively built up around herself. She smiled softly, feeling a rush of tenderness for the woman who, despite the cool exterior, was so clearly carrying something heavy beneath the surface.

“Yeah,” Rio murmured, her voice low. “I get that.”

For a long moment, neither of them spoke. The music seemed to settle between them like a bridge, and Rio could almost taste the unspoken words, the things Agatha wasn’t yet ready to say. She wanted to reach out, wanted to make Agatha see how much she wanted to be there for her, but she didn’t.

Instead, Rio took a quiet step back, allowing Agatha space, but her eyes never left her.

The silence between them held a promise. Neither of them spoke of it, but it was there—the knowledge that whatever was happening, whatever had already happened, wasn’t going to just fade away. Not so easily.

And in that moment, Rio knew she had to be patient. If Agatha wasn’t ready to take the next step, Rio could wait. But she wouldn’t walk away.

Not now. Not after all of this.

Rio stood there for a long moment, her thoughts swirling. The past few days had been a blur of restlessness. She had been dying to text Agatha, to reach out after everything that had happened, but she had held herself back. She didn’t want to spook Agatha. The last thing she wanted was to push her further away. So, Rio had kept her distance, but every day, every moment, Agatha had been on her mind—more and more.

It wasn’t just the kiss, though that had been something unforgettable. It wasn’t just the way Agatha had let herself go in that moment, or the softness of her lips against hers. No, it was everything. It was the way Agatha had opened up through her music. The way she spoke, so careful yet so deeply emotional. Rio could feel the pull, could feel it in every part of her body, but she wasn’t going to rush it. She had to let Agatha come to her, had to let her find her own way through the storm of emotions.

But damn, it was hard.

She had paced her house, texted and deleted, tried to focus on writing and band prep for their upcoming album, but Agatha was always there, in the back of her mind.

It was just that… she hadn’t expected this. She hadn’t expected someone like Agatha to bring out something so… tender in her. A desire to protect, to hold her close, but also to give her the space she clearly needed. Rio was used to the thrill of the chase, the quick spark of attraction, but Agatha wasn’t like that. She didn’t respond to those quick hits. No, Agatha was deeper. She needed time. She needed to be certain.

And Rio was willing to wait.

Her thoughts were interrupted when Agatha shifted, breaking their silence. Agatha glanced at her, her eyes scanning Rio for a second before she spoke.

“You’re early,” Agatha said, her voice soft, almost like she didn’t want to disrupt the moment they were sharing.

Rio smiled, taking a step toward her. “Yeah, I… Mia had something to take care of at school,” she explained, not wanting to dive too deep into the details of her daughter’s plans for the day. “I told her I’d meet her here afterward, but I figured I’d come early. Thought maybe… maybe I could see you.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, her lips curling up just slightly in a knowing smile. “You wanted to see me?” she repeated, a hint of amusement in her voice.

Rio nodded, her gaze steady, though there was something vulnerable in the way she met Agatha’s eyes. “Yeah, I did. I thought about you… a lot,” she admitted, her words carrying more weight than she intended. “More than I probably should have.”

Rio stepped closer, feeling the pull of Agatha’s presence as she sat at the piano. She hesitated for a moment before settling onto the bench beside her, the space between them small but enough to carry a quiet weight. The soft hum of the school’s music-filled space provided a backdrop to their conversation, but Rio could feel the silence between them almost as heavy as the weight of everything left unsaid.

Rio settled beside Agatha on the piano bench, the space between them just enough to make the air feel heavy, but not so much that it was uncomfortable. She hesitated for only a moment before running her fingers across the keys, the familiar smoothness of the ivory comforting in a way she hadn’t expected. She hadn’t played in a while—not seriously, at least—but it was something she’d done since she was a kid, so her hands moved without thinking, finding a simple melody that felt right.

Agatha watched her for a few moments, clearly surprised. “You play?” she asked, her voice soft with curiosity.

“Yeah, since I was little,” Rio replied, glancing over at Agatha with a small, easy smile. “It’s not my favorite, but I always found it kind of soothing.”

Agatha tilted her head slightly, her gaze lingering on Rio’s hands as they moved with surprising fluidity over the keys. “You’re good ,” she commented quietly, her tone genuine.

Rio chuckled lightly, giving a slight shrug as she stopped playing and turned her body slightly to face Agatha. “I don’t play much anymore. But… I thought I’d give it a shot today.”

Agatha studied her for a second, a thoughtful expression crossing her face. She could feel the quiet pull between them again, and her heart quickened at the way Rio was looking at her—almost like she wanted to say something more. But when Rio just met her gaze, her eyes soft yet unreadable, Agatha found herself at a loss for words.

Rio stayed silent for a beat, but then she let out a small sigh, her fingers absently tracing the edges of the piano. “I couldn’t stop thinking about you,” she finally said, her voice low, just above a whisper. Her words hung in the air between them, a subtle but undeniable confession. “I’ve been trying to distract myself… but every time I close my eyes, I see you. That night… everything. I just couldn’t stop thinking about it.”

Agatha’s breath hitched slightly, her heart stuttering at the rawness in Rio’s voice, but she didn’t say anything in return. She couldn’t bring herself to.

Rio wasn’t done, but she sensed the tension in the air, the way Agatha had stiffened ever so slightly, as though trying to process what she’d said. She bit her lip, her fingers lightly brushing against the piano keys again as she focused on them, giving Agatha the space she needed. “I’m not going to push you, Agatha,” Rio added, her tone quiet but firm. “I just… wanted you to know. That’s all.”

The silence between them stretched out, more comfortable than it should’ve been, but neither of them moved. Rio could tell that Agatha needed time, and she was willing to wait. She wasn’t going anywhere.

Then, just as Agatha opened her mouth to respond, the sound of footsteps echoed down the hall. Rio quickly turned her head, and Agatha’s gaze followed.

“Mom, guess what!” Nicky’s voice rang out, and before either of them could say anything else, he burst into the room, his face lighting up when he saw Rio sitting at the piano. “You’re already here! What are you doing?” he asked, firing off the question in his usual rapid-fire manner.

Agatha let out a small laugh, grateful for the interruption. She quickly turned to face her son. “Just… hanging out,” she said, keeping her voice light.

Nicky’s eyes darted from Rio’s fingers still resting on the piano keys to Agatha, then back again. “Do you play? Does she play well, mom? Is she, like, the next piano star?” he asked, his enthusiasm clearly uncontainable.

Rio smiled, unable to resist the warmth Nicky radiated. “I wouldn’t go that far,” she replied, her grin wide. “But I can hold my own.”

Nicky seemed satisfied with that, though his curiosity was still brimming. “What are you gonna play next? Can I try?”
