Agatha couldn’t help but chuckle, the moment finally feeling lighter, more like the usual routine of their days. She ruffled Nicky’s hair. “Not today, buddy. Rio’s just here for a bit.”

Nicky pouted but seemed to accept it. “Well, if you ever do a show, I wanna be front row!” he announced before turning back to Rio with wide eyes. “Do you play anything else? Like, bass? Drums?”

Rio laughed, feeling the weight of the previous conversation ebbing away, replaced by the familiar warmth of Nicky’s unfiltered energy. “Guitar, drums, a little bass, a little keyboard… I dabble,” she said with a wink.

Nicky’s eyes grew even wider, clearly starstruck. “Whoa! You’re like, a super cool rockstar.”

Rio smiled warmly, her thoughts about Agatha momentarily pushed aside as Nicky bombarded her with more questions. Agatha, feeling the moment slip away, leaned back against the bench, watching Rio handle her son with an effortless charm.

As the moment stretched on, Rio’s earlier words about not pushing Agatha still hung in her mind, simmering beneath the surface. But she was content, for now, to let the pace be what it was. She wasn’t going anywhere.

~*~

As soon as Nicky asked her if she would listen to the new song he’d been working on, Rio nodded happily. She was more than happy to indulge him, her admiration for the boy growing the more she was around him.

Agatha shifted in her seat and gave Rio’s shoulder a quick, gentle squeeze. “I’m going to get some work done in my office,” she said, her tone light but with a subtle edge Rio couldn’t quite place. Maybe it was the way Agatha avoided meeting her eyes for a second too long.

Rio watched her leave, feeling a slight disappointment in her chest, though she tried to ignore it. The closeness they shared earlier was interrupted, but Rio was determined not to overthink it.

“Come on, I can’t wait to show you!” Nicky said, bouncing on his heels, eager to share his latest creation.

Rio smiled, letting herself get swept into his energy. They headed outside to the small courtyard, where Nicky took her to the spot he made his own. It was just a small corner with some benches, but it was clear it was special to him. He set up his guitar, his fingers already dancing over the strings, and started playing with a concentration that Rio couldn’t help but admire.

The boy had talent. More than that, he had passion—a drive that reminded Rio of herself when she was his age. As she listened, she couldn’t help but smile at how effortlessly his music flowed. He was still a kid, but there was something mature about the way he expressed himself through his music.

As the next hour passed, Rio couldn’t ignore the tug in her chest. Even though she was engrossed in Nicky’s playing, part of her kept drifting back to the tension between her and Agatha. She couldn’t quite place it—maybe it was Agatha’s hesitation, maybe the way she was pulling away. Whatever it was, it lingered in the back of Rio’s mind as she continued to encourage Nicky, offering him advice and praise.

~*~

 

As Rio listened to Nicky excitedly play the riff he’d been practicing, her gaze shifted toward the entrance of the courtyard. Mia had just appeared, her posture slumped and her eyes avoiding contact. Rio could feel the shift in the air, a subtle tension she couldn’t quite place. Mia wasn’t her usual self.

“Hey, kiddo,” Rio called, offering a soft smile. “You good?”

Mia glanced up, forcing a smile, but Rio could tell it didn’t reach her eyes. “Yeah, fine,” she muttered, though the words felt empty. She hesitated for a moment, then dropped her shoulders, her gaze drifting toward the ground.

Rio watched her for a beat, instinctively knowing something wasn’t right. But Mia wasn’t in the mood to talk—Rio could see that much. Still, the silence between them was thick.

Nicky, on the other hand, was too caught up in his guitar to notice. “Rio, look! It’s that Coven song!” His enthusiasm pulled Rio back into the present. “I’ve been practicing! Watch!”

With a grin, Nicky strummed a few notes, his fingers moving quickly over the guitar strings. Rio smiled at his excitement, genuinely impressed by his progress. “You’re sounding great, buddy. That’s some real talent.”

Nicky beamed, clearly proud of himself. But as she glanced back at Mia, who still stood by the entrance, Rio felt the familiar pull of concern. “Alright, Nicky, you keep practicing,” she said, ruffling his hair affectionately. “But I need to go run some errands. I’ll be back soon to pick up Mia, okay?”

“Okay!” Nicky said, grinning up at her. 

Rio smiled at him before turning her attention to Mia once more. “Mia,” she said gently, “I’m gonna go take care of a few things, but I’ll be back to pick you up soon. You good to wait for me here?”

Mia didn’t respond right away, but she gave a short nod, her expression unreadable. “Yeah, I’ll wait.”

Rio studied her for a moment longer, but then decided not to press. She gave her a soft smile before heading toward the gate. As she walked away, Rio couldn’t help but feel the weight of the conversation that was still hanging in the air. Mia clearly had something on her mind, but she wasn’t ready to open up about it just yet.

Shaking off the thought, Rio headed out of the courtyard, telling herself she’d check in with Mia later. She had to get her errands done, and then she’d be back—ready to pick up her daughter.

As she walked away, she glanced back one last time, seeing Nicky still focused on his guitar, his enthusiasm still evident. Rio couldn’t help but smile, but the moment of peace was fleeting as she turned toward the errands awaiting her.

~*~

When Rio returned to pick up Mia, she carried a tray with two cups of coffee and two hot chocolates, the warm aroma cutting through the late afternoon air. Her eyes immediately found Agatha, who stood near the front desk, scanning something on her tablet.

Agatha glanced up as Rio approached, her gaze briefly flicking to the tray before settling on Rio’s face. “Mia’s in the bathroom,” she said, setting the tablet down.

Rio nodded, then hesitated for a fraction of a second before holding out one of the coffees. “For you.”

Agatha’s brows lifted slightly, but then—there it was. That small, pleased smile, the kind Rio was quickly learning felt like a rare reward. She accepted the cup, fingers brushing against Rio’s for the briefest moment.

Rio wasn’t sure what pleased her more: that she’d guessed right, or that Agatha was accepting it at all. “And this is for Nicky, if that’s okay. Thought he’d like a hot chocolate,” she added, nodding at one of the smaller cups.

Agatha smiled, nodding as Rio placed the hot chocolate on the counter. Agatha took a careful sip of the coffee, humming in approval before cradling the cup between her hands. “Not bad,” she admitted.

Rio smirked, leaning against the desk. “Not bad? That sounds dangerously close to a compliment, Harkness.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but the corners of her mouth twitched in amusement. “Don’t let it go to your head, Vidal.”

Rio chuckled, taking a sip of her own coffee. “Too late.”

For a moment, there was an ease between them, something warm and unspoken lingering in the air. Rio could feel it, could see it in the way Agatha’s shoulders had lost some of their tension. It made her want to push, just a little—to reach for that connection again, to remind Agatha that whatever had sparked between them that night hadn’t been a mistake.

But before she could say anything else, the sound of a door opening caught their attention.

Mia stepped out of the bathroom, her expression unreadable as she spotted Rio standing there with Agatha. Her gaze flickered to the tray in Rio’s hands, then to the way Agatha held her coffee, before settling on Rio’s face.

“Hey, kid,” Rio greeted, forcing a casual smile. “Got you a hot chocolate.”

Mia hesitated for a fraction of a second before stepping forward and taking the cup. “Thanks,” she murmured.

Rio studied her, noting the slight tension in her posture. Something was off. Something was way off.

“You all done with your lesson?” Rio asked, keeping her voice light.

Mia nodded, taking a sip of her drink. “Yeah. Just finished.”

Agatha glanced between them before speaking. “She did well today.”

Mia shifted uncomfortably, as if unsure what to do with the praise. She nodded once, then turned back to Rio. “Can we go?”

Rio raised an eyebrow at the clipped tone but nodded. “Yeah, of course.”

Mia turned around and made her way to the door. “Bye, Agatha. See you next week,” she called over her shoulder.

Rio turned back to Agatha, lowering her voice slightly. “Is she okay?”

Agatha exhaled softly, her fingers tightening briefly around her coffee cup. She glanced at Mia, who was now focused on her drink, then back at Rio.

“She was a little distracted today,” Agatha admitted in a quiet voice, careful not to let Mia overhear. “Nothing too concerning, but…” She trailed off, giving Rio a knowing look.

Rio sighed, rubbing the back of her neck. “Yeah. I noticed something was off earlier too.”

Mia shifted beside them, clearly aware they were talking about her. She didn’t say anything, just kept sipping her hot chocolate, her expression carefully blank.

Rio decided not to push it—not now. Instead, she turned back to Agatha and gave her a small, appreciative smile. “Thanks for letting me know.”

Agatha nodded. There was something about the way she was looking at Rio, something softer than before, and Rio found herself reluctant to leave just yet.

Mia sighed, shifting her weight impatiently. “Are we going?”

Rio huffed a small laugh at her daughter’s tone, then turned back to Agatha. “I’ll see you soon?”

Agatha hesitated for the briefest moment before nodding. “Yes.”

It wasn’t a promise. But it wasn’t a refusal either.

That was enough for now.

Before she turned to leave, Rio let her fingers brush against Agatha’s, then gave her hand a brief, warm squeeze. A quiet, unspoken acknowledgment—of what had happened, of what still lingered between them.

Agatha didn’t pull away. Didn’t stiffen. Just looked at her, something unreadable flickering in those sharp blue eyes before she gave a nearly imperceptible nod.

Rio pulled back, offered a small smirk, and then finally stepped away. “Take care, Harkness.”

And with that, she slung an arm around Mia’s shoulders and led her out the door.

~*~

Rio didn’t know what to do anymore.

Mia had been in a mood all day, and no matter what Rio said or did, she barely got more than a one-word response from her. It wasn’t unusual for Mia to be quiet—she had always been more reserved than Rio—but this wasn’t just quiet. This was something else.

And Rio was getting real tired of dancing around it.

She set the plates down with a little more force than necessary, the sound of ceramic meeting wood breaking the heavy silence. “Mia, dinner.”

Mia barely glanced up from her phone. “I’ll eat later.”

Rio let out a slow breath, gripping the edge of the counter. “You know the rule. When we’re both home, we eat together.”

“I know the rule,” Mia muttered. “I’m not hungry.”

“That’s not the point,” Rio said, exasperated now. “Come sit down.”

Mia didn’t move.

Rio folded her arms, her patience wearing thin. “Okay. What’s going on?”

Mia’s fingers stilled over her phone, her jaw tightening. She sighed, tossing it onto the couch beside her, then finally looked at Rio.

“They found pictures of you at school.”

Rio frowned. “What?”

“Pictures. Of you. Online.” Mia’s voice was sharp, her fingers drumming restlessly against her thigh. “Some asshole found them and thought it would be funny to show everyone.”

Rio’s stomach sank. She didn’t need to ask what pictures Mia meant. She had been in a club, she had been drinking, and she had been… well, close to someone. But nothing had happened.

Except, apparently, someone had caught it on camera.

“Jesus,” Rio muttered, dragging a hand down her face. “Mia, I—”

“They said you were making out with some woman,” Mia interrupted. “That you were probably taking her home that night. They were laughing, calling you a—” She cut herself off, pressing her lips together.

Rio’s jaw clenched. “Calling me a what?”

Mia shook her head. “Doesn’t matter.”

“It does,” Rio said, stepping closer. “What did they say?”

Mia exhaled harshly. “That you’re just slut who got famous. That you sleep around. That you—” She stopped, looking away. “That it’s no wonder I don’t know who my dad is.”

Rio’s breath caught in her throat.

It took everything in her not to punch a hole in the wall.

She took a slow breath, then another. “Mia, you know that’s bullshit.”

“I know,” Mia muttered. “But it doesn’t mean it’s fun to hear.”

Rio hesitated, then moved closer, hesitating only for a second before pulling Mia into a tight hug. “I’m sorry,” she murmured.

Mia didn’t hug her back at first, but eventually, she let out a breath and leaned into her mother’s embrace. “I just hate it,” she admitted, voice small now.

“I know,” Rio said, pressing a kiss to the top of her head. “And I’ll fix it.”

Mia pulled back, giving her a skeptical look. “How?”

Rio sighed. “I don’t know yet. But I will.”

Mia held her gaze for a long moment before sighing and finally sitting at the table. “Okay.”

It wasn’t much, but Rio would take it.

~*~

 

Later that night, long after Mia had gone to her room, Rio sat on the couch with her phone in hand, scrolling through search results with a clenched jaw.

She had to see them for herself.

It didn’t take long to find them. The photos were grainy, taken from a distance, but they were clear enough. There she was, pressed close to someone on the dance floor, her hands on the woman’s waist, their bodies aligned.

Her heart pounded as she swiped to the next one.

It was just as Mia had said—there were shots of her looking like she was about to kiss someone, their faces inches apart. But it was dark and grainy and there wasn’t much to see there. Another one caught her in the middle of a laugh, the club lights painting her skin in neon hues.

But none of them showed Agatha’s face.

Relief crashed over her so suddenly she almost sagged against the cushions.

In the clearest shot, the only thing visible of Agatha were her hands—one on Rio’s hip, the other tangled in her hair. The angle worked in their favor; Rio’s body mostly blocked Agatha from view. Anyone who didn’t already know who it was wouldn’t be able to tell.

Thank fuck.

But the headlines were still brutal.

Rockstar Rio Vidal Caught in Late-Night Club Romp—Who’s the Mystery Woman?

Another Night, Another Fling? The Coven’s Rio Vidal Spotted Getting Cozy at L.A. Hotspot

Rio Vidal: Music’s Favorite Bad Girl at It Again?

Rio exhaled sharply and tossed her phone onto the coffee table, raking a hand through her hair.

So this was what Mia had been dealing with all day. No wonder she was pissed.

Rio closed her eyes and leaned back against the couch.

She had no idea how to fix this.

But she had to try.

~*~

 

Rio sat on the edge of her bed, her fingers absently scrolling through her phone, her mind racing. She hadn’t realized that the photos even existed until Mia had told her about them, and now the tension in the house felt unbearable. Mia was withdrawn, angry, and Rio couldn’t shake the nagging feeling that everything was spiraling out of control.

What hurt the most was that Mia had found the photos. The photos that could, in the worst case, get out of hand and cause even more trouble. Mia had always been sensitive about the attention her mom’s career brought, and Rio understood that. But what she was even more pissed was that she should’ve seen this coming. She knew how those vultures worked.

I should’ve known better. I should have been more careful.

The guilt gnawed at her, but what stung more was the idea that Agatha might find out through someone else. Agatha had been nothing but supportive, and Rio knew that her world was different from this. The last thing Agatha needed was for all of this to get tangled into her life.

Rio looked down at her phone, at the images Mia had shown her. There were a couple of blurry shots of her dancing at the club with Agatha. And while the pictures weren’t clear enough to make out her face, Rio couldn’t help but feel a knot tighten in her chest. She had never wanted this kind of attention, and certainly not for Agatha to be dragged into it.

With a deep breath, Rio stood up, pacing the room. It wasn’t just about the photos—it was about making sure Agatha knew the truth, straight from her.

Rio grabbed her phone again, finding Agatha’s contact and hesitating for a moment before hitting the call button. She needed to do this. She needed to apologize, even if it wasn’t her fault.

The phone rang once, twice, and then Agatha answered.

“Hello?”

Rio swallowed hard, trying to steady her voice. “Hey, it’s Rio. We need to talk.”

“What’s wrong?” Agatha’s voice was soft but alert, and Rio felt a wave of guilt wash over her. She hadn’t even told Agatha about the photos yet.

“I just… I need to tell you something,” Rio started slowly, struggling to find the words. “Mia showed me some photos today. They’re of me in a club… with someone. And they got out, somehow.” She paused, trying to collect her thoughts. “I didn’t know about them until Mia told me. I just—I don’t want you to hear about it from anyone else. You can’t really tell it’s you. They’re blurry, and you can’t see much. They can just see your hands around me, like when we were dancing.”

There was a long silence on the other end. Rio’s heart pounded as she waited for Agatha to speak.

Finally, Agatha’s voice broke through the quiet. “I wish you had told me earlier. I… I would have wanted to know about this sooner.”

“I’m sorry,” Rio said quietly, the words heavy on her tongue. “I didn’t mean for you to be dragged into this. I didn’t want to upset you or make things harder for you.”

Agatha sighed softly. “It’s not your fault, Rio. I know that. But it’s just… complicated.”

“I know. I just—I didn’t want it to be something you had to deal with,” Rio replied. “I didn’t want you to find out from anyone else.”

“I’m glad you told me. I really am,” Agatha said after a moment. “But this isn’t just about us. It’s about Mia, and what this might mean for her. I don’t want her to see us getting caught up in all this noise.”

“I don’t want that either,” Rio murmured. “I just wanted to make sure you knew. I should have been more open with you. I should have told you sooner.”

Agatha’s tone softened. “Hey, again, it’s not your fault. It’s a lot to handle. But we’ll figure this out.”

Rio let out a breath she didn’t realize she had been holding. “I appreciate that. Really. And I’m really sorry you got dragged into this mess. I hate it.”

“You don’t need to apologize,” Agatha said gently. “We’ll handle it. But thank you for telling me. We’ll talk more later, okay?”

“Okay,” Rio said softly. 

Agatha said goodbye and the line went quiet again, and Rio let out a deep breath, feeling a bit lighter, but the weight of everything still lingered. At least Agatha knew now. She had been open, and that felt like a small relief, even if the road ahead was uncertain.



Nine

Chapter Notes

So... I know some of you are waiting for the next chapter of Luminous. It's like 90% ready but I'm not happy with it yet, so I'm still tweaking it. Since this one was mostly ready, I figured I'd post this already.

I truly hope you guys like it. Again, thank you so much for your lovely comments.

Agatha lay in bed, staring at the ceiling in the dark, her mind racing. The weight of the conversation with Rio still hung heavy, the knowledge of those photos swirling in her thoughts. She hadn’t been able to shake the uneasy feeling ever since Rio had told her. A part of her felt that old familiar pang, that dread, like the echoes of something she’d tried to bury long ago.

She rolled onto her side, pulling the covers tighter around her, but the chill had little to do with the temperature of the room. It was a memory, one that felt just as fresh now as it had all those years ago. The images of her ex—James Wilcox—flooded her mind. The world of fame she had been unwillingly dragged into. The cameras. The flashing lights. The whispers. The constant need to be perfect in a world that didn’t care about who you were beneath the surface.

She thought about the way he had looked at her when she’d told him she was pregnant. How his face had hardened, his shoulders tensing as if the weight of her announcement was a burden he couldn’t bear. It was supposed to be a moment of joy, but it hadn’t been. For him, it had been an inconvenience, something that threatened to shatter the illusion of his carefully curated life.

At first, she’d tried to tell herself it was just the pressure of his career that made him react the way he did. He was a famous musician, after all—at the height of his fame, surrounded by people who worshipped him. The idea of settling down, of raising a family, had seemed impossible in his world. But she had hoped that with time, things would change. She was wrong.

Her thoughts drifted back to that day, the day he had packed his things and left. The moment when she realized that her world would never be the same again. He’d walked out the door, not even a glance back, as though the life they had shared had never mattered to him. And just like that, he had replaced her with someone younger. Someone who didn’t come with the baggage of responsibility, who didn’t ask for things he couldn’t give.

And she, alone and pregnant, had been left behind.

It had taken years for her to rebuild, to regain her sense of self. The memory of his indifference had fueled her drive to create Sonata Grove, to make something of herself that had nothing to do with his world. It had been a sanctuary, a way to reclaim control over her life. But the fear had never truly gone away. The fear that history would repeat itself.

And now, with Rio, it felt like the past was threatening to resurface. The way Rio’s life in the spotlight seemed so familiar, so dangerous. The photos, the attention—they reminded her too much of what had happened before. She was terrified. Terrified of getting caught up in something she couldn’t control. Terrified of allowing herself to trust again, only for it to crumble in the face of the same pressures she had experienced with her ex.

Agatha squeezed her eyes shut, willing the thoughts to fade, but they refused to. They were relentless, like ghosts that refused to leave her side. And in the quiet of her bedroom, her heartbeat seemed too loud, a constant reminder that she was alone with her fears.

She glanced at the clock on her nightstand, noting that it was already past 3 a.m. The time seemed irrelevant, but the hours lost to worrying only made the fear grow stronger. She had always believed that she could keep her life separate from the chaos of fame, that she could protect herself and Nicky from the unpredictability of that world. But with Rio, things felt different. Too different.

She had promised herself that she would never allow anyone to treat her like her ex had. She wouldn’t allow herself to be dragged into the whirlwind of another world that didn’t care about her. But Rio… Rio was different. Agatha could feel it in the way she looked at her, in the way she listened. Rio made her feel things she hadn’t felt in years, and that scared her more than anything else.

Agatha sat up in bed, running a hand through her hair, trying to collect herself. The room felt suffocating, and she needed to clear her mind. She knew she couldn’t stay in this state forever. She couldn’t keep running from what was happening between her and Rio. But she wasn’t ready yet. She needed time. Time to sort through the emotions swirling inside her, to decide if she could let herself take a step forward, or if she would shut herself off and risk losing something that felt too much like a dream.

She glanced toward the window, where the first light of dawn began to creep through the blinds. In the stillness of the early morning, Agatha wondered if she had the strength to face what was ahead, or if she would pull back, afraid of the very thing that might heal her wounds.

For now, though, all she could do was wait. Wait for the storm of memories and fear to settle, and hope that she wouldn’t let herself get swept away in it again.

~*~

Agatha walked into Sonata Grove, the familiar scent of wood, paper, and the faint sound of distant piano keys immediately calming her frayed nerves, but not enough to ease the exhaustion that clung to her like a heavy weight. Her body felt like it hadn’t been given a proper rest in days, and her mind… her mind was a jumbled mess of memories, worries, and things left unsaid.

As she made her way through the main area, Wanda spotted her almost immediately.

“You look like you haven’t slept in days,” Wanda said, her sharp eyes studying Agatha with concern.

Agatha shrugged, offering her a small smile as she tried to brush it off. “I just couldn’t sleep, Wanda. It’s nothing.”

Wanda, however, wasn’t buying it. She followed Agatha closely, not allowing her to escape her gaze as she moved toward her office. “You’re lying,” she said, her voice gentle but insistent. “Come on, something’s going on. I know you too well.”

Agatha sighed, the weight of the conversation with Rio still lingering at the back of her mind. She sat down at her desk and began sorting through papers aimlessly, trying to regain some sense of control. “Really, Wanda, it’s nothing. Just… too much on my mind.”

Wanda wasn’t having any of it. She pulled up a chair and sat down across from Agatha, crossing her arms. “Nope. Not buying it. What happened? Tell me.”

Before Agatha could respond, her phone buzzed on the desk, a text notification lighting up the screen. She hesitated, her fingers itching to look but not knowing if she was ready. She snatched it up, her eyes immediately landing on the message from Rio.

Rio

Good morning. Just wanted to check in after our talk last night. Hope you’re doing okay.

Accompanying the text was a picture of a sunrise, the early light casting soft, warm colors over a cityscape, but it was Rio’s tired face that caught Agatha’s attention. The half-smile, the exhaustion behind her eyes… it was clear that Rio, too, hadn’t slept well. Her own struggles, her own worries.

Agatha’s heart gave a painful lurch. She wasn’t the only one who couldn’t seem to shake off the tension, the questions that lingered in the air between them. And yet, here was Rio, reaching out in her own quiet way, trying to check in, to offer comfort.

Her smile was instant, but short-lived. Agatha stared at the photo for a moment, the warmth of it settling in her chest. But then reality hit, like a punch to the gut. She could feel the complications, the fear, the unspoken things weighing down on her, and the reminder of Rio’s vulnerability only added to the confusion.

Agatha stared at the phone in her hand for a moment longer, her thumb lingering over the screen, but before she could respond to Rio’s message, Wanda’s voice broke through the silence.

“You’ve been off ever since our night out with Rio and her band,” Wanda said, leaning forward in her chair. “You didn’t just toss and turn because of some restless night’s sleep. There’s something else going on.”

Agatha’s heart sank at Wanda’s perceptiveness. She had been trying so hard to keep everything at bay, to convince herself that she was in control. But Wanda could see right through her, as she always had. Agatha didn’t know how to explain, not yet, so she deflected.

“It’s just… a lot on my plate, that’s all,” Agatha murmured, turning her attention back to the papers on her desk, though she didn’t really see them. “The usual. Running the school, keeping everything together… And Nicky’s been on edge lately. You know how it is.”

Wanda wasn’t fooled. She stood up and walked closer, crossing her arms as she leaned against the edge of Agatha’s desk. “You’re a terrible liar, Agatha,” she said softly, but there was a tenderness in her voice. “You’re not fine. And don’t try to tell me you are when you’ve been so quiet since that night. It’s not just Nicky you’re worrying about, is it?”

Agatha clenched her jaw, her gaze dropping to her hands. She couldn’t tell Wanda everything, not yet. It was too soon, too raw. But the words were so close to spilling out.

“I don’t know what you mean,” Agatha said, her voice barely above a whisper, though she knew it was no use.

Wanda’s eyes softened, but she wasn’t letting her off the hook. “I know you. You’re shutting yourself off, and I don’t think it’s just because of the usual stress. There’s something else eating at you.”

Agatha sighed, looking up at Wanda, her eyes brimming with a mixture of frustration and vulnerability. She could feel her resolve crumbling. It wasn’t like she could keep pretending forever. She was trying so hard to hold everything together, but it was starting to feel impossible.

The phone buzzed again, breaking the moment, and Agatha picked it up, letting the distraction pull her away from Wanda’s relentless gaze. It was Rio again. Agatha didn’t even bother to hide her smile this time, but it quickly faded as the reality of what she had to face sank in.

She opened the message from Rio:

Rio  

I know we left things in a weird place last night. Just wanted to make sure you’re doing alright.

Agatha sat back in her chair, a mixture of warmth and guilt blooming in her chest. She hadn’t realized just how much Rio had been thinking about her. The words hit a little too close to home.

Wanda noticed the change in Agatha’s face immediately, her gaze catching Rio’s name on her phone. “It’s her, isn’t it?” she asked, her voice soft. “It’s Rio. That’s what’s been on your mind, isn’t it?”

Agatha didn’t answer right away. She stared at the message on her phone, her finger hovering over the screen, unsure of what to say or how to respond. She had no idea how to process it all. Rio was reaching out, and part of Agatha wanted to reach back, but there were so many things left unsaid, so many unanswered questions. She had been so traumatized after James left her; she didn’t know if she was ready to dive into a relationship, especially not with someone who came with her own set of baggage that seemed to be so similar to her ex’s.

Wanda, sensing her hesitation, softened. “I don’t need all the details right now. But you’ve got to stop shutting people out, Agatha. Especially if you care about them.”

Agatha’s chest tightened at Wanda’s words, and she felt an overwhelming urge to confess everything that had been plaguing her. But instead, she only nodded slowly.

“I don’t know what to do,” Agatha admitted, her voice tight. 

Wanda studied her for a moment, then sighed and shook her head, a small smile tugging at the corner of her lips. “Well, you can always try talking to her, maybe let your guard down just a little bit, Aggie. It won’t get any easier if you keep burying it.”

Agatha let out a shaky breath and finally hit reply to Rio’s text. She didn’t know what she was going to say yet, but it felt like the first step toward something. Maybe that was enough for now.

As she typed, Wanda turned to leave, pausing in the doorway.

“I’ll give you some space,” she said, her tone light. “But just know that I’m here when you need to talk. About anything. And you might want to take a breath before you hit send on that message.”

Agatha smiled tiredly, looking up as Wanda left the office. She glanced back at the phone, rereading Rio’s message. Then, with a deep breath, Agatha finally started typing her response.

Agatha stared at her phone screen, the sunrise image bright and warm, an unexpected comfort. She hadn’t realized how much she needed it until now. Rio’s tired face peeking out from the edges of the frame made her heart ache in a way she wasn’t quite ready to acknowledge. It was a gentle reminder that Rio, too, wasn’t immune to the sleepless nights, that they both carried a weight on their shoulders—one that Agatha had been too busy with her own thoughts to consider.

She typed a reply, fingers hesitant but needing to connect.

Agatha

Thank you for the sunrise photo. I didn’t sleep much last night. My mind kept me up, but this was a nice distraction. I hope your morning’s going better than mine.

She hit send, looking at the message for a moment, feeling vulnerable but also relieved. Rio’s simple gesture had broken through the barrier of exhaustion Agatha had put up around herself. She didn’t know what this connection was—didn’t even know what to call it—but the quiet understanding Rio’s photo brought her was something Agatha couldn’t ignore.

The phone buzzed moments later, and Agatha’s heart skipped when she saw it was Rio replying.

Rio

I didn’t sleep much either, if it helps. You know how it goes… sometimes your mind doesn’t want to shut off. But I’m pushing through today. I’ll bring you coffee next Wednesday. Looking forward to it.

Agatha chuckled softly, picturing Rio’s easy smile. Despite the exhaustion that lingered in her words, Rio still had the ability to make Agatha smile.

Rio

Btw, I’ll be in the studio for the next few days working on the album. But I’ll check in on you now and then, if that’s okay. I’ll make sure to come back to you with better news next time.

Agatha’s heart softened as she read the last line. Rio, despite everything, still made time for her, even if it was just in short text exchanges. It felt like more than she deserved, more than she’d ever anticipated. 

Her fingers hovered over the keyboard, thinking about the best way to respond. She settled on something simple, yet truthful.

Agatha

I’m glad you’re pushing through. I’ve been keeping myself busy with composing, though it hasn’t been easy. And Mia… Was that why she seemed upset yesterday? Because of the photos?

She stared at the message, wondering if she should say more, but finally pressed send, hoping Rio would understand.

It wasn’t long before Rio’s reply came.

Rio

Yeah. Some kids at her school were talking shit about it. About me. Apparently, they got spread around, and she’s been having a hard time with it. I didn’t know until she mentioned it last night. It’s one thing when it’s just me, but Mia… she doesn’t deserve that.

Agatha’s heart tightened as she read those words. She thought about Mia—the girl who had always seemed so strong, so composed—and realized just how fragile she was beneath the surface. The weight of Rio’s words hit her harder than she expected. She could feel the frustration and helplessness in Rio’s tone. It was a harsh reminder of the world Mia had to navigate, and how much of it Rio couldn’t protect her from.

Agatha

I’m sorry to hear that. She’s been such a strong presence during her lessons, I didn’t know it was affecting her so much. You’re right, though. She doesn’t deserve that. Kids can be ruthless sometimes.

There was a pause before Rio’s next text came through.

Rio

Yeah, it’s not easy. You think you can protect them, but sometimes the world finds a way to break through. It sucks, and it’s a part of being in the public eye that no one warns you about. But I’m trying. I’m doing the best I can for Mia, even when it feels like I’m failing.

Agatha’s stomach twisted as she read Rio’s message. She hadn’t really understood before—hadn’t grasped the full weight of what it meant for Rio to be a famous mother, trying to protect her daughter from the prying eyes of the world. It wasn’t just the fame that made things difficult; it was the scrutiny, the way people always had an opinion about everything, including their families. 

Agatha sat back, feeling a sense of empathy she hadn’t expected. She wasn’t sure if Rio would want to hear it, but she had to say something.

Agatha

I can’t even imagine how hard it must be to have your personal life laid bare like that. You’re doing the best you can, Rio. I can see that. It’s not easy, but you’re not alone in this. If there’s anything I can do… I’m here.

She hit send and sat back, unsure of what would come next. She hadn’t intended to say so much, but the words felt right. She hoped Rio would hear the sincerity in them.

There was a long pause, but then Rio replied.

Rio  

Thank you, Agatha. That means a lot more than I can say. I’ll keep you posted on Mia. I just want to make sure she knows I’ve got her back, even when it feels like the world’s against us.

Agatha’s heart swelled as she read Rio’s message. There was something in those words—something real, something raw—that connected them in a way Agatha hadn’t expected. She thought about how difficult it must be for Rio to constantly fight for her daughter’s peace of mind while also carrying the burden of her own public persona. It made Agatha respect her in a way she hadn’t before.

Agatha

I know you do. And I know Mia knows it too. You’re stronger than you think, Rio .

This time, when Agatha hit send, she didn’t hesitate. It felt like the right thing to say. A reminder that, despite everything, they were all trying their best—both in their personal lives and in the world they lived in.

As she set the phone down, she couldn’t help but smile. There was something about Rio’s openness, her honesty, that made Agatha feel a little less alone in her own struggle. It wasn’t just a text—it was a moment of connection, one that made the weight of the day feel a little more manageable.

~*~

 

Over the next few days, their texts became a regular, comforting rhythm. Agatha found herself checking her phone more often than usual, her heart skipping a beat whenever a message from Rio popped up. Rio’s messages were simple, but they had a way of making Agatha feel connected, especially on the days when she was buried in her work.

Rio, being the free-spirited soul she was, didn’t just text. She sent photos of everything she was doing: her bandmates huddled in the studio, guitar in hand, laughing between takes; the dimly lit recording booth with her mic set up; and even candid moments where she looked a little tired but undeniably happy, lost in the process of creating. The photos were snapshots of her world—unfiltered, raw, and filled with an energy Agatha couldn’t help but admire.

One morning, Rio sent a photo of herself mid-jam session with her bandmates. She was hunched over her guitar, the intensity in her eyes palpable even in the blurry shot.

Rio

Here’s a sneak peek of our next album in the making! It’s chaos, but it’s the good kind. Hope your scales are going smoothly .

Agatha smiled at the photo, glad to see Rio so engaged with her work, but a little part of her also felt a pang of envy. Rio’s world was vibrant, unpredictable, and full of noise. Agatha’s world, in comparison, was quieter—structured, precise. She replied, trying to match Rio’s energy.

Agatha

I’m getting there. I’ve been working on a performance for December—getting the right pieces together. It’s a bit slower than I’d like, but I’m getting there.

She didn’t send a photo right away, but then decided to share one of Nicky. He was in the living room, guitar in hand, fingers strumming through one of The Coven’s songs. His concentration was intense, his small hands making the chords with surprising ease. Agatha snapped the photo, sending it with a quick message:

Agatha

Nicky’s taking after you. He’s been practicing one of your songs on his electric guitar. He’s obsessed with you.

She couldn’t help the fond smile that stretched across her face as she watched her son play. His passion for Rio’s music was so pure, so innocent. He had no idea what it meant for Rio to be in the spotlight, but he loved her music for what it was. Agatha sent the photo, feeling a little vulnerable, wondering how Rio would react.

A minute later, Rio’s reply came through, this time with a photo attached. Rio was standing in front of a large speaker, headphones around her neck, the band huddled behind her. She looked exhausted, but there was a glint in her eye that made Agatha’s heart flutter.

Rio

That’s amazing! Tell Nicky he’s got a real talent for this. Maybe we’ll get him up on stage one day.

The thought of Nicky performing with Rio made Agatha’s heart race, but she pushed it away, focusing instead on how much Rio seemed to appreciate the gesture. The next message from Rio caught Agatha off guard.

Rio

By the way, do you ever get the feeling like you’re just playing the same scale over and over? Sometimes I feel like we’re chasing the same sound, even when we think we’ve found something new. 

It was a simple question, but it made Agatha pause. The way Rio phrased it reminded her of the kind of deep thinking she had during her quieter, more introspective moments. She didn’t hesitate in responding.

Agatha

All the time. It’s like the sound is just out of reach, and no matter how much you try to get closer, it’s always just slightly beyond your fingertips. But when it clicks… it clicks. And that makes all the frustration worth it.

She felt oddly connected to Rio in that moment. They were both chasing something—whether it was perfection in music or finding their own rhythm in life—but they were trying to find it in their own ways.

Over the next few days, their messages continued to flow easily. Rio would share little behind-the-scenes photos of the studio, the band’s progress, and her sporadic moments of downtime. Agatha, in turn, would send pictures of her piano and the progress she was making on the December performance. She sent one particularly close-up shot of her hands on the keys, her fingers poised over the ivories, a reflection of her intense focus.

Agatha

Here’s a bit of what I’m working on. It’s coming together, slowly but surely.

This time she sent a video of her fingers working on the piano keys, and it seemed to prompt Rio’s response, which was both playful and sincere.

Rio  

I love seeing these! You make it look so easy, but I know it’s anything but. 

Agatha smiled at that. The playfulness in Rio’s words felt like a bridge between their two worlds.

Throughout the week, the photos and texts became more than just exchanges—they were moments of connection. Agatha found herself looking forward to them, especially when Nicky would join her, eagerly showing her his progress with The Coven’s songs. One evening, after a particularly long day of practice, Agatha sent Rio a picture of Nicky mid-shred on his guitar.

Agatha

Nicky’s getting better at this. I think he might be more of a rockstar than I realized.

Rio’s response came quickly, a photo of herself in the studio, a guitar slung over her shoulder.

Rio

Tell Nicky I’m coming for him. He’ll make one hell of a guitarist.

Agatha’s heart swelled at Rio’s words, and she realized that, despite the distance between them, Rio was making her feel like a part of something larger. It wasn’t just the music that connected them—it was their willingness to share these pieces of themselves, these little fragments of their worlds.

By the time Wednesday rolled around, Agatha was already looking forward to seeing Rio in person. The texts and photos had been enough to keep her heart light, but the anticipation of actually seeing Rio’s face again made her stomach flutter with nerves. She’d gotten used to their text exchanges, but she knew it would be different once they were face to face. Would Rio feel the same?

For the first time in a while, Agatha allowed herself to imagine what might happen when they saw each other. There was something about this connection—something both exciting and terrifying—that made her feel like she was on the brink of something she hadn’t expected. She wasn’t sure where it would lead, but she was beginning to believe that, maybe, it was worth exploring.

~*~

The morning passed in a blur for Agatha, as she tried to focus on her work. But with each passing hour, a feeling she hadn’t experienced in far too long fluttered inside her—anticipation. She caught herself glancing at the clock, counting the minutes, wondering if Rio would show up early again. It was a silly thing, really—just an exchange of coffee and pleasantries—but for some reason, she couldn’t help but feel the flutter of butterflies every time her phone buzzed, each time imagining Rio’s smile and that easy way she had of making everything feel just a little lighter.

It had been a week since their last meeting, and even though Agatha had been cautious with her feelings—still unsure, still hesitant—she couldn’t deny how much she was looking forward to seeing Rio in person again. The past few days had felt like an odd dance between texts, brief moments of connection, and then pulling back. But today, with the promise of their actual interaction looming, Agatha’s heart skipped a beat at the thought of finally getting to talk to Rio face to face again.

As the clock neared the hour, Agatha felt her excitement building. There was something about Rio’s energy that had a way of drawing her in, of making her forget the weight of her own careful self-protection. But Agatha wasn’t quite ready to throw caution to the wind. She couldn’t help but wonder what it would be like if she let herself fall into this…whatever this was.

She glanced at the door, wishing for a moment that Rio would walk in a bit earlier, just so they could chat, just so she could see her again without the formalities of picking up Mia, without the tension of needing to keep things in check.

There was something about Rio’s presence, something warm and confident, that had a way of making Agatha forget herself for a moment. But the next step—what came after this, what the two of them might even be heading toward—was a mystery.

So, for now, she settled back in her seat, checking her watch again and allowing herself to smile, just a little, at the thought of Rio’s inevitable arrival.

~*~

Agatha’s heart skipped when she saw Rio step through the door a little earlier than expected, holding a tray with two cups of coffee and a box of pastries. The scent of freshly brewed coffee wafted into the room, mingling with the delicate sweetness of the pastries. Rio’s smile was as bright as ever, and there was something about her casual demeanor that made Agatha feel a little more at ease.

“Got you some coffee,” Rio said with a wink, setting the tray down on the small table in the center of Agatha’s office. “And something sweet, too. Thought you might need it after a long day.”

Agatha’s stomach gave an involuntary flutter at the sight of Rio’s thoughtful gesture, and she couldn’t help but smile. It was a simple thing, yet it spoke volumes. Rio had clearly put some thought into this, and the ease with which she navigated their dynamic made Agatha’s chest tighten in an unfamiliar way. She wasn’t sure what to make of it, but she couldn’t deny that she was happy Rio had arrived early.

Agatha nodded in the direction of her office, and led them there quietly. The door clicked shut behind them, leaving just the two of them in Agatha’s office. The silence was comfortable, an unspoken understanding between them, as Rio set the tray with the coffee and pastries between them on the table. She sat down with an easy stretch, her posture relaxed but her gaze warm, like she was more than happy to share this quiet moment with Agatha.

“Thanks for letting me sneak in early,” Rio said, flashing a grin. “I figured we’d have a little time before Mia comes rushing in.” Her voice was easy, but there was a certain softness to it now—one that made Agatha’s chest tighten in a way she wasn’t prepared for.

Agatha nodded, still trying to shake off the weight of everything that had been on her mind. She took a sip of her coffee, the warmth settling in her hands, and then looked over at Rio. There was a part of her that had wanted to feel uncomfortable with Rio’s proximity, but somehow, it was different with Rio. She wasn’t sure why, but she found herself enjoying it, even in the midst of her own hesitation.

“I’m glad you came early,” Agatha admitted, her voice quieter than usual. “I’ve had a lot on my mind recently, and… well, it’s nice to have a bit of peace before the storm of kids arrive.”

Rio leaned back in her chair, her eyes catching Agatha’s with an openness that made something flutter in her stomach. “I get that,” she said, her voice warm. “I’m not exactly thrilled with what’s been going on either, but I’m glad we’re getting this time together. You’re easy to talk to, Agatha.”

Agatha’s breath caught at the way Rio said her name—like it was something she’d been meaning to say for a while. Her heart skipped a beat. But instead of overthinking it, she focused on the moment, on the gentle ease between them, and how, for the first time in a long time, she didn’t feel like she had to keep her walls up so high.

“Same here,” Agatha replied, setting her coffee down and glancing toward the pastries. She took a pastry from the box and broke off a small piece, offering it to Rio with a small, amused smile. “I’d like to think I’m more than just a piano teacher, you know. I can also appreciate a good pastry.”

Rio grinned, leaning in slightly as she accepted the piece from Agatha’s hand. “I can definitely appreciate that,” she said, her voice low as she took the bite. Her eyes lingered on Agatha for a moment longer than necessary before she casually reached for her own coffee. “So, how’s the performance prep going? Anything exciting coming up?”

Agatha chuckled softly, feeling the tension in her shoulders begin to melt as they fell into their conversation. “It’s actually been a lot of work,” she admitted. “I was invited to do this solo concert in December, and it’s got me busier than I expected. But it’s exciting too. It’s been a while since I’ve done something like this.”

“That sounds amazing,” Rio said, her eyes brightening as she leaned forward just a little bit, a subtle shift that made Agatha notice how close Rio had become. “I wish I could come see it.”

Agatha’s stomach did another little flip at the idea. She hadn’t even considered Rio wanting to attend one of her performances, but the thought made something warm spread through her chest.

“Well, you’ll be welcome if you want to come,” Agatha replied, her tone a bit more open than she meant. “It’s a special one, for me, anyway.”

Rio’s gaze softened as she looked at Agatha, her expression sincere. “I’d love that,” she said quietly, her voice almost hushed. “I really would.” She reached forward, her fingers brushing against Agatha’s hand in a casual but deliberate touch, and Agatha’s breath hitched at the unexpected connection.

It wasn’t a dramatic gesture, just a simple touch. But the way Rio did it, with the lightest pressure on Agatha’s hand, made Agatha feel the warmth of it all the way down to her toes. Rio was still looking at her, and there was something in her eyes that made Agatha’s heart race a little faster.

“How about you?” Agatha asked, trying to regain her composure as she met Rio’s gaze. “What’s been keeping you busy besides trying to be an angel in the studio?”

Rio laughed, the sound genuine and rich, and she leaned back in her chair, looking thoughtful for a moment. “Well, besides the band, there’s Mia,” she said, her voice softening a bit. “And… I’m always trying to figure out what’s next for us. It’s been a bit of a balancing act lately, trying to juggle everything without losing my mind.”

Agatha’s heart tightened a little, and she leaned forward slightly. “I think you’re doing a great job, Rio,” she said, her voice quiet but sincere. “It’s not easy, having a teenager and all the pressure from being in the spotlight. It’s… it’s a lot.”

Rio’s smile softened, and she reached out again, her fingers gently brushing against Agatha’s hand once more. “Thanks,” she said, her voice full of gratitude. “It means a lot, hearing that from you.”

Agatha’s heart skipped another beat at the contact, and for a moment, she forgot everything else—the doubts, the hesitations. All she could focus on was Rio’s hand against hers, the warmth of her touch, and the way Rio was looking at her like she had all the time in the world to just… be.

It was only when a noise from the hallway startled them both that Agatha realized they had been caught in a quiet moment of connection, a moment that she wasn’t sure what to do with. But for now, she didn’t care. It was nice, feeling this way. And for the first time in a long while, Agatha let herself enjoy it.

Mia would be here soon. Nicky would be following her shortly. But for now, it was just the two of them. And it felt like enough.

~*~

Agatha and Rio sat in comfortable silence, each savoring their coffee, the moment between them stretching longer than either of them had expected. There was something about the quiet that was soothing, and Agatha found herself enjoying the way Rio seemed so at ease in her office.

She hadn’t expected Rio to feel so… familiar. But the way Rio leaned casually on the desk, the way she touched Agatha’s arm in passing when she made a joke about the pastries, was disarming in the best way. The lingering brush of Rio’s fingers against her skin made Agatha’s pulse quicken in a way she couldn’t entirely explain.

“So what can I expect from your performance? I've never been to a concert like that.” Rio asked after a moment, her eyes soft but focused, taking in every detail of Agatha’s face.

Agatha smiled, setting her coffee cup down. “It’s a work in progress. I’m doing a few classical numbers, but I’m also including some of my own stuff. I’m still tweaking a few things, but it should be ready for December. I’ve got to get the students in shape for the recital too, which is a bit of a challenge. That’s coming up very soon.”

Rio tilted her head, her fingers brushing lightly over the edge of Agatha’s sleeve. It was a simple gesture, but it made Agatha’s breath catch.

“Sounds like a lot,” Rio murmured. Her gaze flickered to Agatha’s hands, and before Agatha could pull back, Rio’s fingers traced the back of her hand, sending a little spark of warmth through her.

Agatha swallowed, her thoughts momentarily thrown off balance. “It is,” she said quietly, her voice almost betraying how her heart had started to race. But she wasn’t about to let herself get caught up in the heat of the moment—not yet.

She had to remind herself that they were just two people sitting and chatting, sharing coffee and pastries, with no real agenda. Except for maybe… her hand brushing against Rio’s wrist as she reached for her own coffee again. Just a moment of connection.

“You don’t have to keep your hands to yourself, you know,” Rio said lightly, a playful glint in her eye, though there was something unspoken in her tone—something that made Agatha’s stomach twist in a way she didn’t want to examine too closely.

Agatha froze for a split second, the words hanging between them. Was that boldness something Agatha could handle? Could she risk letting herself get closer to Rio like that? She could feel her resolve crumbling bit by bit, and yet, she wasn’t sure if she was ready to surrender to it.

Agatha felt the weight of Rio’s words linger in the air, and for a moment, she wasn’t sure if she’d misheard. But when Rio’s playful glint didn’t fade, when her fingers remained just a little too close, Agatha knew she had to decide.

She could keep herself in check, maintain that familiar distance—or she could take the risk, just a tiny one.

With a soft exhale, Agatha reached across the desk, her fingers brushing against Rio’s wrist in a gentle, almost tentative touch. It was just a fleeting contact, but it sent a ripple of warmth through her, her pulse quickening.

Rio didn’t flinch, instead letting her gaze soften, her lips curving into a subtle smile. “Well, well,” she said, her voice still light but carrying an edge of something more. “I didn’t think you actually had it in you.”

Agatha’s heart raced at the feel of Rio’s touch lingering even after her fingers pulled away. She wasn’t used to this—this was new, this… connection that tugged at her in ways she couldn’t explain.

Rio’s fingers moved toward her hand again, this time brushing more deliberately across Agatha’s palm. The touch was soft but firm, as though Rio was silently inviting her to keep going.

Agatha’s breath caught, and for a split second, she considered pulling away, playing it safe, but the pull of curiosity won out. She hesitated, then leaned in slightly, her fingers resting lightly against the back of Rio’s hand. She could feel the warmth of her skin, the slight tremor in her own fingertips as they made contact.

Rio let out a quiet laugh, a sound that made Agatha’s chest tighten in a way she didn’t want to acknowledge. “I’m starting to think you like it when I touch you,” Rio teased, her voice low, a little daring, as she flipped her hand up so their palms could meet.

The words made Agatha’s heart skip a beat. She wasn’t sure if she should pull back or lean into it. The moment felt too intimate, too real, but there was something irresistible about the way Rio’s hand lingered on hers, the way her body seemed to speak louder than the casual jokes.

Agatha’s lips parted, but before she could say anything, Rio’s thumb caressed her skin, sending a jolt through her.

“Don’t keep your hands to yourself, Agatha,” Rio murmured, her voice nearly a whisper. The words made Agatha’s stomach flutter, a warmth spreading through her that had nothing to do with the coffee or the pastries.

Agatha felt her resolve break just a little. She let out a soft sigh, her hand lifting, not out of hesitation but out of sheer curiosity. She placed her fingers on Rio’s wrist, feeling the pulse there, steady and calm. And for just a moment, she let herself linger.

Rio smiled, her eyes bright with something playful, something far more intimate than anything Agatha had expected to feel in that moment.

But just as quickly as the mood shifted, Nicky’s voice broke the spell.

“Mom, guess what I learned today?” Nicky’s voice echoed through the door, and Agatha’s heart jumped at the sound, the reality of their situation sinking back in. She quickly pulled her hand away from Rio’s wrist, the warmth of the touch lingering on her skin.

Nicky stepped into the office, his wide eyes scanning the room as he froze in his tracks. His gaze shot from Rio to Agatha, clearly confused by the scene unfolding before him. “Wait, Rio? What are you doing in here?” he asked, his voice higher than usual, surprised to see her there.

Rio was the first to recover, her grin slipping back into place as she leaned back against the chair, her posture casual and relaxed. “I was just hanging out with your mom. We’re having coffee.”

Nicky blinked again, his eyes bouncing between Agatha and Rio, still processing the unexpected sight. “Uh, okay… I didn’t know you guys were hanging out like this.” He glanced back at Agatha, then back to Rio, still unsure of the situation.

Agatha, still flustered but trying to regain her composure, smiled at Nicky. “Well, you know, Rio’s always popping by to check on you and your guitar playing. We were just having some coffee before you got back from school.”

Nicky looked between the two of them, his expression shifting from surprise to curiosity. “Cool,” he said slowly, the moment of awkwardness quickly dissolving as his attention turned back to Rio. “So, what’s up with the band? You guys been working on new music? Mom mentioned the other day that you’ve been in the studio.”

Agatha watched as Rio and Nicky fell into an easy conversation, the tension from their brief moment of connection ebbing away. But inside, Agatha couldn’t shake the warmth that still lingered from their touches. She wasn’t sure what it meant or where it was going, but for now, she just let it sit, feeling both the pull and the uncertainty of it all.

~*~

 

Ten

Chapter Notes

As always, thank you for your lovely comments. Hope you enjoy this one!

The drive back from Sonata Grove felt longer than it should have, even with the LA traffic crawling by. Rio couldn’t shake the memory of the last hour spent with Agatha—how close they’d gotten in that moment, how easy it had felt to touch her.

It had been an unexpected rush, like something she hadn’t even realized she was craving. She hadn’t planned on any of it—especially not letting her fingers brush against Agatha’s wrist or feeling that undeniable connection spark when Agatha had hesitated but then responded to her touch. That smile Agatha had given her when she finally let herself touch her back? It was like everything else had faded away, leaving just the two of them in that small, quiet room.

But Agatha pulled away. She always did. Rio had noticed it the moment they’d first met: that guarded part of Agatha, that hesitation that ran deeper than Rio’s usual flirty encounters. Agatha wasn’t like other people. She wasn’t going to fall for charm or a pretty smile. She wasn’t even looking for anything—at least, Rio didn’t think so.

But there was something there, something beyond the politeness and the professionalism. And Rio couldn’t ignore it. Not when it felt so right.

She gripped the steering wheel tighter as the thought flashed through her mind: What if I’m pushing too hard?

But at the same time, Agatha had been slowly but surely letting her in. She couldn’t stop thinking about the way they’d connected over something as simple as coffee and casual conversation. And about that split-second hesitation, when Agatha’s fingers had brushed against her wrist, when she’d allowed herself to soften just enough.

She wanted more of that. Wanted to see if Agatha could let go of her walls, even just a little.

But that meant figuring out what Agatha wanted. And Rio wasn’t sure how to navigate this. She had always been confident in everything she did—her music, her band, even her relationship with Mia. But Agatha was different. Agatha had walls so high, so carefully constructed, Rio felt like she’d need a ladder just to peek over the top.

Rio laughed bitterly to herself. Maybe she should start by being patient. The thought of waiting wasn’t something she liked—it never had been. But this… whatever this was with Agatha, it wasn’t something to rush. She didn’t want to push too hard, scare Agatha away.

But what was the next step? She couldn’t just keep showing up with coffee and pastries. It had to mean something. There had to be a way to show Agatha she was serious without overwhelming her.

She couldn’t just let Agatha think that she wasn’t interested. She wanted Agatha to feel seen—to feel the way she made Rio feel when she’d responded to that first touch, that first little spark. There was a tenderness there that Rio didn’t usually have with anyone, and it both scared and excited her.

She needed a plan. A way to get closer without forcing Agatha into something she wasn’t ready for. A way to show her, slowly, that there was more to this than just a passing attraction.

Maybe next week, when she came back with coffee again, she could make it more personal. Maybe she could open up a little more about her own fears—the things she’d never talked about with anyone. About being a mother, about the loneliness of fame, about being a woman in the public eye who had to fight to be taken seriously.

Rio didn’t know yet, but she was going to figure it out. She just hoped that when the moment came, Agatha would be ready to take that next step with her, too.

~*~

 

That Friday night, Rio barely had time to breathe between the flashing cameras and the endless small talk. The premiere was massive—red carpets, high-profile celebrities, reporters crowding every inch of the space. It wasn’t her first time at an event like this, but it always felt surreal to be here, all because The Coven had a song on the movie’s soundtrack.

She had to admit, though—she looked good. Her stylists had outdone themselves. Her hair was swept back in loose, effortless waves, her makeup sultry but still fresh. She wore a perfectly tailored deep red suit, unbuttoned just enough to be suggestive, and beneath it, a black silk top that clung in all the right ways. When she caught her reflection in the windows of the theater, she had to smirk.

Yeah. She looked hot.

And she wasn’t the only one who thought so. She’d lost count of how many people—some she knew, some she didn’t—had complimented her that night. It was part of the job, part of the whole rockstar package that she’d learned to embrace over the years.

But the only opinion that really mattered wasn’t there.

So, in a moment of mischief (and maybe just a little bit of nerves), she snapped a selfie in the limo on the way to the afterparty. The lighting was moody, casting soft shadows over her jawline. She tilted her head slightly, lips just barely parted, and smirked.

Then she sent it to Agatha.

Rio

Guess who got all dressed up tonight?

She hesitated only a second before adding another text.

Rio

Wish you were here to see it in person .

She put her phone down, not expecting an immediate reply. Agatha wasn’t exactly the type to text back right away—especially not when Rio was being like this. Still, she couldn’t help but glance down every now and then as the limo crawled through LA traffic.

Then, her phone buzzed.

Agatha

You clean up nicely, Vidal.

Rio grinned. But then—another message.

A single emoji.

Heart eyes.

Rio blinked.

What.

She sat up straighter, staring at the screen like she’d imagined it. Agatha Harkness, queen of restraint, sent her a heart eyes emoji?

A slow, satisfied grin spread across Rio’s lips.

She needed to push her luck.

Rio

You just made my whole night, Harkness .

Three dots appeared, then disappeared. Then reappeared again.

Agatha

Don’t let it go to your head.

Rio laughed, shaking her head. Too late.

~*~

The afterparty was in full swing by the time Rio arrived, but for the first time in a long time, she wasn’t all that interested. She made her obligatory rounds, chatting with some industry folks, accepting compliments about The Coven’s track on the soundtrack, even taking a few photos with fans who were lurking near the VIP section. It was all routine, all second nature by now.

But her mind wasn’t on the party. It was on Agatha.

That damn heart eyes emoji had ruined her.

She kept checking her phone like an idiot, hoping for another message, another tiny crack in Agatha’s careful restraint. But nothing else came.

Still, that didn’t mean she couldn’t do something about it.

Slipping away from the crowd, she found a quieter corner near the balcony and snapped another photo—this time, in front of a full-body mirror. She angled it just right to capture the city lights behind her, the rich red of her suit standing out against the moody backdrop of the party.

Rio  

Alright, but just to be clear—how nicely do I clean up, exactly?

She hit send before she could second-guess herself.

Seconds passed. A full minute. Two.

Then—buzz.

Agatha

Wouldn’t you like to know?

Rio grinned.

Oh, she was in so much trouble.

Rio didn’t even hesitate before replying.

Rio

Yes. Yes, I would very much like to know.

Agatha didn’t reply right away. It was a full thirty minutes later that her phone finally buzzed again. The venue was packed, music thrummed in her chest, and people kept pulling her into conversations, offering drinks, leaning in too close. But Rio had her phone in her hand—because of course she did. She’d been waiting.

Agatha

Then I suppose you’ll just have to live with the mystery.

Rio almost choked on her champagne. Unbelievable.

A slow grin spread across her face as she read it again. Agatha Harkness was teasing her. Actually teasing her.

Oh, she was so in trouble.

Rio  

That’s just cruel, Harkness.

She leaned against the bar, absently swirling the last of her drink, her mind no longer in the room at all. Someone said her name, but she barely heard them.

Her phone buzzed again.

Agatha

Is it?

Rio let out a sharp laugh, shaking her head. She typed back quickly.

Rio

Oh, absolutely. You can’t just say something like that and then leave me hanging. That’s a crime.

The DJ switched tracks. A new wave of people moved toward the dance floor. Someone from the film crew clapped her on the shoulder, saying something about how amazing the band’s music sounded in the movie. Rio smiled, nodded—she thought she even managed a thanks—but her attention was entirely elsewhere.

Her phone buzzed.

Agatha

I’m sure you’ll survive .

Rio tapped her fingers against her thigh, her smile growing.

Rio  

Barely .

Another pause. A longer one this time.

Someone slid onto the stool beside her. A woman, gorgeous, red lips curving into something suggestive. “You look like you could use another drink.”

Rio glanced at her, smiled politely, and turned back to her phone.

Agatha

You’re more dramatic than I expected.

Rio bit her lip, considering her response.

Rio  

I contain multitudes, Harkness.

She finished off her champagne, set the glass down, and scanned the crowd absently. Somewhere, Alice was deep in conversation with a director. Natasha was charming her way through another industry connection. Jen had probably already snuck out.

Her phone buzzed again.

Agatha

I’m starting to see that.

Rio exhaled slowly.

For a second, she forgot where she was. Forgot about the noise, the crowd, the weight of all these expectant eyes.

Agatha was flirting with her. Subtly, yes—but she was engaging. She was giving Rio something to work with, something to hold onto.

Rio wet her lips, tapping out her next message.

Rio

You really know how to keep a girl on her toes.

She watched the screen, willing another reply to come through. A full minute passed. Then—

Agatha

Good night, Rio.

Rio stared at the words, an odd mix of frustration and delight pooling in her stomach.

That was it? She was going to play coy and leave her like that?

God, that was hot.

Grinning to herself, Rio typed back one last message.

Rio

Good night, Agatha.

Then, before she could overthink it, she slid her phone into her pocket and turned back toward the party.

~*~

Rio’s house was alive with noise when she woke up. The smell of coffee and something frying drifted through the air, mingling with laughter and the low hum of conversation.

She groaned, shoving a hand through her already-messy hair as she rolled out of bed.

Her band was still here.

Not that she was surprised. They had a tendency to crash at her place after big nights out—especially Alice, who always claimed Rio’s couch was the best in L.A. And honestly? Rio didn’t mind. It was nice, in a way, to have people around.

Dragging her feet toward the kitchen, she spotted Mia already up, standing by the stove in deep conversation with Natasha.

Rio blinked, rubbing her eyes as she took in the scene. Mia looked…comfortable. Focused. Natasha, despite her usual I do not do mornings demeanor, was listening intently, nodding along as Mia spoke. It didn’t surprise her. Nat had always been Mia’s favorite Aunt.

Whatever they were talking about, it clearly mattered.

Rio smiled to herself. Then, without thinking twice, she walked up behind Mia and pressed a quick kiss to the top of her head.

“Morning, mi amor.”

Mia made a face, half-heartedly swatting her away. “ Moooom, ” she whined teasingly, but that only made Rio hold onto her even tighter.

Natasha snorted. “That’s the most affection I’ve ever seen you tolerate.”

Mia rolled her eyes but didn’t move away.

Rio grinned, grabbed a mug, and poured herself some coffee before sinking onto a stool at the kitchen island. The coffee was hot—too hot—but she didn’t care. She took a sip anyway, letting the warmth jolt her fully awake.

Then, as naturally as breathing, she pulled out her phone and sent a text.

Rio

Good morning, Harkness.

She hit send, barely hesitating, and exhaled as she set her phone down.

It was becoming a habit, this—reaching for Agatha first thing in the morning.

And that? That was dangerous.

Rio took another sip of her coffee, watching Mia and Natasha with mild curiosity. They were still deep in conversation—something about music theory, she realized. Mia was animated, explaining something with her hands, and Natasha was nodding along like it was the most interesting thing she’d ever heard.

It was a good look on Mia.

Before Rio could dwell on that thought too long, her phone buzzed.

Agatha

Good morning, Vidal.

She huffed out a laugh. Of course Agatha would match her energy.

Another buzz.

Agatha

Did you even sleep?

Rio smirked, about to type a response when a loud groan came from the hallway.

Alice shuffled in first, looking half-dead, her red streaks sticking up in every direction. “Coffee,” she croaked.

Jennifer followed, looking a little more put together but still moving slowly. “How the hell do you look functional already?” she grumbled at Rio, grabbing a mug.

“I thrive on chaos,” Rio said, grinning.

Natasha raised a brow at her. “And yet, you were the first to crash last night.”

“Not the first,” Rio corrected, glancing at Mia.

Mia looked unimpressed. “You passed out on the couch like an old lady.”

“Rude,” Rio muttered, though she wasn’t entirely offended.

Her phone buzzed again.

Agatha

Or are you still running on whatever kept you awake last night?

Rio hid a grin behind her mug.

Rio

Are you asking if you kept me up, Harkness?

Agatha didn’t reply immediately, which made Rio bite her lip. She imagined her frowning at the screen, debating whether or not to dignify that with an answer.

Alice slumped onto a stool, eyeing the eggs Natasha was scrambling. “Are we just now starting breakfast?”

“It’s more like brunch at this point,” Jennifer muttered.

Mia shrugged. “I wasn't hungry earlier.”

Alice made grabby hands toward the pan. “Love that for you, but I am starving.”

Rio let the noise wash over her as she checked her phone again. Still no reply.

She took another sip of coffee, drumming her fingers on the counter.

Come on, Harkness.

Finally, Rio’s phone buzzed.

Agatha  

I’m not dignifying that with a response.

Rio grinned, imagining Agatha’s exasperated look.

Rio

So that’s a yes?

There was a long pause. Then—

Agatha  

Drink your coffee, Vidal.

Rio chuckled, setting her phone down just as Alice dropped onto a seat next to her, rubbing her eyes.

“Good morning, sunshine,” Rio said with a grin, knowing full well Alice was always the last one to rise.

“Yeah, yeah,” Alice mumbled, stealing a piece of toast off Mia’s plate.

Mia immediately swatted her hand away. “I was going to eat that.”

“Aw, come on, Mia. Share the wealth,” Alice said, her voice a little too cheerful for the morning.

Mia rolled her eyes but didn’t respond, just grabbed another piece of toast for herself.

Jennifer sat across from Rio, looking at her thoughtfully. “You’re up early today.”

“Coffee’s good,” Rio said, taking another sip.

Alice raised an eyebrow. “What’s with the smile?”

Rio shook her head. “Nothing,” she shrugged, but couldn’t help but look down at her phone again, her fingers itching to text Agatha back.

“You sure?” Jennifer asked with a teasing grin, “You’ve got that look like you’re texting someone special.”

Rio just shrugged, hiding the smile that was creeping up on her face again. “I’m just texting. Nothing special.”

“ Sure .” Alice looked at Jennifer and smirked. “We’ll just keep our eyes open.”

Mia snorted. “You’re both ridiculous.”

“Whatever,” Alice muttered. “Just tell us if anything happens. No one has the patience for your mystery, Rio.”

Natasha wandered in, clearly having heard some of the chatter. “Let’s all just enjoy our breakfast and stop trying to dissect Rio’s love life for the tenth time year.”

Jennifer rolled her eyes. “You’re no fun.”

Mia, who had been pretending to ignore them, finally spoke up. “Can we please just eat?”

Alice was about to respond, but Rio quickly shot her a look. “Later,” she muttered, trying to deflect.

With that, they all settled into a comfortable quiet as Mia went back to her toast, and the others started talking about their plans for the day.

Rio’s phone buzzed again, and she glanced at it quickly, smiling as she saw Agatha’s text.

Agatha

So how was your big night out last night?

Rio

Oh, I thought you were already done with me. And the premiere was wonderful, thanks for asking. Wish you were there with me, though. Also, does this mean I get to keep texting you, or have I exhausted my Harkness quota for the week? 

The reply came almost immediately.

Agatha

You’d never stop even if I told you to.

Rio chuckled at Agatha ignoring half her message, but let it slide for now.

Rio  

Damn right. You know me so well already.

She felt a sense of satisfaction at the easy banter, despite the chaos of the morning around her. It was something she hadn’t expected to find, but she was happy to enjoy it, especially as she finished her coffee in the calm before the rest of the band became a bit more vocal.

~*~

Rio sprawled out on the couch, lazily scrolling through her phone while sipping at her now lukewarm coffee. The house was still shaking off the last bits of sleep—Natasha and Mia were still in the kitchen, deep in conversation, while Jennifer nursed her coffee and Alice lay half-conscious on the armchair.

Rio wasn’t much of a morning person, but today, she was feeling good. She had that easy kind of contentment humming under her skin—the kind that came from a night of good music, good friends, and, most importantly, good flirting.

She smiled as she tapped out a message.

Rio

What’s on the agenda for today?

Agatha answered quicker than expected.

Agatha

I was thinking about taking Nicky out for a bit. Maybe to the park. Get some fresh air.

Rio grinned. Yeah, that sounded about right. Agatha would take him, watch him run around, pretend to be completely engrossed in a book or her phone, but she’d really be watching him the whole time, soft in a way she probably didn’t even realize.

And, okay, maybe Rio wanted to see that for herself.

She leaned forward, elbows on her knees.

Rio  

Or…

Rio

You could come over instead .

To your place?

That is what “come over” usually means, yes.

Agatha

Why?

Because I’m grilling today. And you like food. And I like your company. And Nicky seems like the type of kid who could demolish an entire rack of ribs.

Rio  

Or is it that you’re scared of seeing me again?

I’m not scared of you.

Rio

So you do want to see me.

Agatha

That is not what I said.

Oh, she was enjoying this way too much.

Rio

You didn’t deny it, either.

Nothing.
