Rio  

Besides, if you say no, I’ll be forced to text you every thirty minutes with updates about my day. And you don’t want that, do you?

That got her another quick response.

Agatha  

My God, you’re exhausting.

Rio

And yet, you’re still talking to me. Fascinating.

Rio grinned, waiting. She knew Agatha. Knew she was probably pinching the bridge of her nose, sighing dramatically, coming up with a million reasons to say no.

Rio smirked at her phone, stretching her legs out on the couch as she read Agatha’s latest reply.

Agatha

That’s not appropriate.

Oh, now they were getting somewhere.

Rio  

Define “appropriate.”

A pause. Then—

Agatha  

I'm Mia's teacher. I don’t want to make her uncomfortable.

Rio snorted. Of course Agatha was worried about that. It was such an Agatha thing to say—always thinking about structure and boundaries and professionalism. Meanwhile, Rio was over here just thinking about how good she’d looked the last time they were together and how much she wanted to see that tiny, reluctant smile again.

Rio

Mia likes you.

Agatha  

That’s beside the point.

Rio

No, it’s exactly the point. If she had a problem with you coming over, I wouldn’t invite you. But Mia is fine. She’s always fine when you’re around. Probably because she knows you’re not secretly plotting to corrupt her with rock and roll.

Rio took a slow sip of coffee, feeling the victory before it even happened.

Then—

Agatha

It’s still not appropriate.

Rio

Okay, let’s pretend you’re right. Let’s say it’s wildly inappropriate for you to eat food with me in a setting where other people will be present. That doesn’t explain why you haven’t just said no and ended this conversation.

It’s because you want to come over. You just need to find an excuse good enough to let yourself do it.

Rio  

Come onnnn, Agatha. I’m literally giving you the perfect excuse. Nicky. You’re not coming for me. You’re coming because I invited your son. You’re being a good mother, bringing him to a fun day with music and food and his favorite rock band. What’s inappropriate about that?

Another long pause. Then, finally—

Agatha

You are insufferable.

Rio

Yes, but I’m also right.

But then—

Agatha

What time?

Rio

Let's say 1:30-ish? Bring your appetite. And your kid. And that pretty little face of yours.

Rio barely held back a victorious grin as she stared at Agatha’s last message.

Oh, she was so pleased with herself right now.

She forced herself to take a slow sip of coffee like she wasn’t vibrating with satisfaction. Across the room, Alice, Natasha, and Jennifer were talking about their plans for the day, completely oblivious to the miracle that had just occurred in Rio’s text messages.

She should play it cool. Not react. Just quietly celebrate this win in her own head.

But then she saw the three dots appear again.

Another message.

Agatha

Don’t push your luck.

And that? That made Rio’s grin slip free.

Jennifer glanced at her. “What are you grinning at?”

Rio’s fingers curled tighter around her phone as she stretched her legs out, trying to feign nonchalance. “Nothing,” she said easily. “Just winning a battle of wills.”

Alice snorted. “So you’re annoying someone into submission. Got it.”

Natasha hummed. “Hope it’s not our manager. You already drive her up the wall.”

“Please.” Rio rolled her eyes. “If it was Michelle, I’d be getting a million passive-aggressive emails right now. Not texts.”

They all seemed to accept that answer, Natasha returning to her coffee, Alice flipping through her phone, Jennifer leaning into the counter to steal a piece of toast.

And meanwhile, Rio just sat there, pretending to be completely normal while staring at Agatha’s last text like a lovesick fool.

1:30pm. She was coming over at 1:30pm.

Holy shit.

~*~

Rio set her coffee down and turned to Mia, who was scrolling through her phone at the kitchen counter. With the band chatting amongst themselves in the background, Rio seized the moment to speak.

“So… Agatha and Nicky are coming over in a bit for a barbecue,” Rio said, her voice casual. “I figured it’d be nice to hang out, get to know each other outside of all the lessons and stuff.”

Mia glanced up, her eyebrow raised. “Agatha? As in Agatha Harkness, my piano teacher?” she asked, as if she was trying to understand if Rio was joking.

“Yeah, that Agatha,” Rio confirmed, giving her a small smile. “She and Nicky are coming over. It’ll be fun. Just a chill afternoon, some food, music—nothing big.”

Mia’s expression turned more skeptical, her eyes narrowing slightly. “Why?”

Rio felt the need to tread carefully. She wasn’t sure how Mia would react to the situation. “No reason, sweetheart. Just to hang out. You’re fine with that, right? It’ll just be a relaxed hangout. Agatha is great… so is Nicky. So I invited them.”

Mia paused for a moment, her gaze lingering on Rio as if she was piecing things together. “And this is just a barbecue? Nothing else? No… other plans?”

Rio chuckled softly, trying to diffuse the tension. “Yes, just a barbecue. I promise, Mia, it’s nothing complicated. I just thought it’d be nice to have Agatha and Nicky over—get to know them a bit more. You don’t have to worry about it.”

Mia didn’t seem entirely convinced, her lips pressing into a thin line. “I don’t know, Mom… it just feels weird, you know?”

Rio leaned in, offering a reassuring smile. “It’s just a casual hangout, sweetheart. You don’t have to feel awkward. I wouldn’t invite them over if I thought it would make you uncomfortable.”

Mia gave her a doubtful look, still hesitant. “Well, as long as it’s just the barbecue. I don’t want to deal with anything weird, Mom.”

Rio nodded, understanding her daughter’s need for reassurance. “Of course. Just a laid-back afternoon. Nothing weird, I promise.”

Mia seemed to relax a little, but she wasn’t entirely sold yet. She let out a sigh, clearly still mulling it over. “Alright, fine. But if it gets weird, you’re dealing with it, not me.”

Rio grinned, grateful for Mia’s understanding. “Deal. Thanks, kiddo.” She patted Mia on the head, her hand lingering for a second longer than usual. “It’s going to be fun, you’ll see.”

As she finished getting ready, Rio texted Agatha again, just to make sure everything was still on track. 

Rio

I’m all set. Come on over whenever you’re ready. See you soon.

When she received the reply, she couldn’t help but smile. Agatha was on her way.

Rio watched her go, her chest tightening at the words. “Good,” she murmured under her breath, a smile tugging at her lips as Agatha turned her back. “I’m looking forward to it.”

Rio leaned against the wall for a moment longer, her heart still pounding in her chest. She had no idea what exactly was happening between her and Agatha—maybe it was just the connection they shared, the way they were able to talk so freely without any pretense. Whatever it was, Rio wanted more of it.

She was certain about one thing: she didn’t want to let Agatha slip away.



Eleven

As Agatha stepped out of the house and back into the bright afternoon sun, she found the scene outside bustling with energy. The band had already started setting up their instruments, their laughter floating through the air like the familiar hum of a well-loved song. Nicky was standing in the middle of it all, his small hands wrapped reverently around one of the guitars. His eyes were wide with awe, his excitement palpable, and it was hard not to smile at how much he looked like he was living a dream.

But even as she felt that warmth in her chest, a flutter of nerves stirred beneath it. The day had already been such a whirlwind—spending time with Rio, getting to know her bandmates better, and now, as she watched Nicky hold the guitar with such care, a new wave of uncertainty washed over her. She’d known Rio’s friends from that night at the club, and while they had all been kind, it felt different now. Now, it wasn’t just some happenstance casual gathering—it was real. And Agatha wasn’t entirely sure how to handle it.

Her eyes automatically searched for Rio, who was now helping to get a few more instruments outside. The sight of her made Agatha’s pulse quicken—her natural charisma, the way she effortlessly commanded the space around her. She had no idea what was happening between them—what any of it meant—but she couldn’t deny that the connection between them felt… undeniable. 

She couldn’t remember the last time she felt this drawn to someone, this compelled to be near them. She couldn’t quite pinpoint it, but Rio had a way of making everything else fade into the background when they were together.

Agatha smiled softly as she watched Nicky strum the guitar gently, his eyes still wide, his hands tentative but growing more confident by the second. It was clear he was in awe of being this close to the band, let alone holding one of their prized instruments.

“You like it, buddy?” Agatha asked as she approached, her voice soft, careful not to startle him.

Nicky’s head shot up, and his face lit up with a grin so wide it nearly reached his ears. “It’s their guitar,” he said in a hushed voice, like he was afraid he might be dreaming. “The one they play in all their songs.”

Agatha’s heart softened as she watched him gently pluck a string, his fingers unsure but determined. “Yeah, it is,” she said, her voice thick with affection for how much this meant to him. “Don’t go breaking it now, alright?”

He laughed, but there was an edge of reverence in it. “I won’t,” he promised, before going back to playing the guitar with a little more confidence.

For a moment, Agatha just stood there, her arms folded across her chest, watching Nicky lose himself in the music, absorbed in the magic of being so close to something he had admired for so long. It was one of those quiet moments she knew would stay with him for the rest of his life, and in some way, it felt like she was holding her breath—like the world was holding its breath with her—waiting to see where this would all lead.

She could feel a tug on her heart, a mixture of pride and something else she couldn’t quite identify. She was more than happy that Nicky was here, happy that he was surrounded by people who genuinely seemed to care about him. But she also couldn’t ignore the small voice in the back of her head, the one that had been questioning her decision to come here in the first place. Could she really do this? Could she really just let herself get swept up in all of this—the laughter, the music, the easy way Rio made her feel?

Agatha knew she wasn’t one for spontaneous decisions, and everything about today had felt like an unpredictable, uncertain choice. But at the same time, a part of her had welcomed it—welcomed the idea of getting lost in the moment. For once, she didn’t have to think about the next step, the next responsibility. It felt… freeing.

But just as quickly as that feeling came, it was replaced with a new kind of uncertainty.

What exactly was this between me and Rio?

She shook her head softly, her thoughts threatening to spiral before she could catch them. She hadn’t even realized that Rio had stepped up beside her until the sound of her voice cut through the moment, low and soothing.

“Does he look like he’s in heaven or what?” Rio asked with a grin, leaning a little closer to Agatha.

Agatha glanced over at Rio, her breath catching slightly as their eyes met. Rio’s casual confidence, her openness, all of it seemed to wash over Agatha in waves, making her heart race in a way she hadn’t expected.

“He’s definitely in heaven,” Agatha replied, managing a soft smile. Her gaze lingered on Rio for a moment longer than she intended. “I think he’ll be telling this story for years.”

Rio chuckled, her voice dropping an octave, playful yet teasing. “Well, you can tell him you were the one who made it all possible.” She nudged Agatha’s arm with her elbow. “You’re a hero in his eyes.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but she couldn’t help but smile. “That’s a bit much, don’t you think?”

Rio raised an eyebrow, her grin growing wider. “Not at all. I mean, come on. He gets to hang out with The Coven and you brought him here. What’s not to love?”

Agatha opened her mouth to respond, but before she could, Nicky’s voice cut through their banter.

“Can I keep it?” he asked, holding the guitar a little more carefully now, his eyes hopeful.

Rio looked at Agatha, the playful glint never leaving her eyes. “What do you think? Should we let him keep the guitar?”

Agatha’s breath hitched in her throat, and for a moment, all she could do was smile at Nicky’s excited face. She could already imagine how much he would treasure this moment, the memory of it locked away for years to come.

“Maybe for today,” Agatha said, her voice filled with warmth. “But only if you promise not to drop it.”

Nicky’s grin widened, and Rio gave Agatha a playful nudge, as if to say, See? You’re a hero in his eyes.

And Agatha? She just laughed. Because maybe—just maybe—Rio was right.

As Nicky clutched the guitar with a mix of awe and excitement, Agatha felt a warmth spread through her chest. Watching her son, so engrossed in this rare moment, made everything worth it. 

It also reminded her how important it was to let him experience life outside of his usual routine, to let him chase after these fleeting, magical moments. A part of her had always been so cautious about protecting him from the unknown, from the chaos of a world filled with unexpected twists. But today, seeing the joy on his face, she realized maybe she had been too protective. Sometimes, letting go was just as important as holding on.

Rio’s teasing nudge brought Agatha back to the present. She shot Rio a look, one of half-mock annoyance, half-amusement, but there was something in Rio’s gaze—a lightness, an invitation to not take everything so seriously—that made Agatha feel like she was breathing a little easier than she had been all day.

“So, are we ready to do this?” Rio asked, her voice dropping low again, her eyes scanning the group starting to gather. The bandmates were chatting and adjusting their instruments, and even Nicky seemed to be getting ready to strum a few more chords, his fingers growing more confident with each passing second.

Agatha hesitated for only a moment before nodding, the warm feeling in her chest creeping into her throat. She wasn’t used to being part of something this spontaneous, this… carefree. But Rio had a way of making it feel natural, like the music and laughter were a language they all spoke fluently.

“Yeah,” Agatha said softly, her eyes lingering on Nicky as he tentatively strummed a few more notes. “I think we’re ready.”

Rio flashed her a grin. “Good. I’ve got a feeling this is going to be fun.”

The band had finished getting everything ready, and before Agatha knew it, they were all taking their places around the makeshift stage outside. Nicky was practically bouncing on his feet, clearly itching to jump in and join the jam session. His excitement was contagious, and even Agatha, usually so composed and reserved, found herself caught up in the energy of the moment.

As the first few chords rang out, Agatha took a step back and leaned against the porch railing, her arms crossed as she watched Rio, her bandmates, and Nicky slip into the rhythm. The music flowed through the air, a familiar, comforting thing—one Agatha had always known but never in a setting quite like this. She glanced over at Rio, who was already lost in the moment, her fingers dancing effortlessly over her guitar, her eyes closed in concentration.

It was like watching someone completely in tune with the world around them, every note, every beat a reflection of who Rio was. Agatha felt herself leaning in a little, her attention riveted by the fluidity of Rio’s playing, the way she seemed to own every movement. It was a side of Rio that Agatha hadn’t fully seen before—not just the confident, daring rockstar, but the artist, the person who lived and breathed music.

Agatha’s gaze shifted back to Nicky, who was now playing alongside Alice, his smile wide as he tried to keep up with the rest of the band. It was hard not to feel a swell of pride. Her son had always loved music, but watching him in this setting, surrounded by real musicians, it was like he had found his place. He had been nervous at first, but now, there was a sense of belonging in his movements, the way he played with confidence, as if he’d always been meant to be part of something this special.

Agatha couldn’t help but smile to herself, feeling a sense of peace wash over her. This moment, this connection between her son and Rio’s band, felt significant. It wasn’t just a casual afternoon; it was the kind of memory that would stay with Nicky, that would shape his love for music in ways Agatha couldn’t yet understand.

Rio’s voice broke through her thoughts. “You sure you don’t want to join in?” she teased, her eyes sparkling as she leaned over, strumming a few playful chords on her guitar.

Agatha glanced at the instrument Rio had handed her earlier, a hesitant smile tugging at her lips. She wasn’t exactly known for being spontaneous, and certainly not when it came to picking up an instrument on the fly. But there was something in Rio’s smile—something that urged her to let go of her hesitation, even if just for a moment.

“I don’t think I’m ready for that,” Agatha replied with a laugh, though her voice was light, playful.

Rio raised an eyebrow, a teasing grin spreading across her face. “You never know until you try,” she said, leaning a little closer.

For a second, Agatha considered it. The thought of jumping in, even for a little while, sounded… freeing. But as she watched Nicky play with such ease, she realized maybe her role today wasn’t to play, but to watch. To enjoy. To let herself soak in the moments, the laughter, the music. That, for now, was enough.

“Maybe next time,” Agatha said softly, her gaze locking with Rio’s, the smile on her lips growing a little more genuine. “I’m happy just watching for now.”

Rio’s grin softened. “I’ll hold you to that,” she said with a wink.

The music continued to swirl around them, the sun starting to dip lower in the sky, casting a golden glow over the backyard. It was one of those moments where everything felt just… right. Not perfect, not without complications, but exactly what it needed to be.

And for the first time in a long while, Agatha let herself believe that maybe—just maybe—this could be the beginning of something beautiful. Something real.

As the evening stretched on, the mood in the backyard became more relaxed. The beer kept flowing, and the jam session had turned into a comfortable, impromptu gathering of friends and family. “So, how’s everything going?” Rio asked, her voice smooth, almost purring as she looked over at Agatha with that playful, mischievous glint in her eyes.

Instead, she allowed her fingers to brush lightly against Rio’s, the touch sending a thrill through her.

Rio’s eyes flickered to Agatha’s hand for just a moment, her lips curling into that same confident smile. “You know, it’s nice to see you like this… relaxed,” she murmured, her voice barely audible over the hum of conversation around them.
