Two different people stopped her before she could even reach the wine aisle—one asking for a picture, the other just gushing about how they’d been to every one of The Coven’s LA shows.

By the time she finally got to her car, she was so completely over it.

It was the kind of thing she was used to, but tonight, it made her chest feel tight. Maybe because she was already on edge about seeing Agatha again. Maybe because she was hyper-aware of how normal Agatha’s life was compared to hers.

By the time she pulled up to Agatha’s house, she was more than ready to let all that stress go.

The house was…unexpected.

A perfect lawn, a cute little porch, and the surest sign of a kid living there—Nicky’s bike tossed haphazardly on the side of the house, like he’d abandoned it mid-adventure.

Something in Rio’s chest ached.

She climbed out of the car, balancing the pizzas in one hand and the wine in the other, but before she could knock, the door opened.

And there was Agatha.

Barefoot, in a deep purple sweatshirt and matching sweatpants, her hair loose and falling in soft waves down her back. No perfectly curated outfit, no polished presentation—just Agatha, warm and soft in the glow of her porch light.

And she was so damn beautiful it nearly knocked the breath out of Rio.

For a second, she just stood there, taking it all in, before managing a hoarse, “Hey.”

Agatha’s lips curled in a faint smile, eyes flicking to the food in Rio’s hands. “You didn’t have to do all that.”

Rio smirked. “Yeah, but I wanted to. Can I come in?”

Agatha stepped back, opening the door wider. “You’re already here, aren’t you?”

As Rio stepped inside, the warmth of Agatha’s home wrapped around her. It smelled like something faintly sweet—vanilla, maybe?—with a hint of something floral beneath it. The lights were dim, casting a soft glow over the living room, and in the far corner, a bookshelf stood tall, filled to the brim.

It was cozy. Lived-in. The kind of place that made her stomach twist with something Rio wasn’t ready to name.

She set the pizzas and the wine down on the kitchen counter, turning just as Agatha closed the door behind her.

“You look good,” Rio said before she could stop herself.

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “I look like I’ve been lounging around all evening.”

“Yeah,” Rio murmured, gaze trailing over her again. “You look good.”

Agatha let out a soft breath, shaking her head like she wasn’t sure what to do with Rio. “Hungry?” she asked instead.

“Starving,” Rio admitted, though food was rapidly slipping down her list of priorities.

Agatha grabbed two plates from the cabinet while Rio uncorked the wine, pouring them each a glass. They moved around the kitchen easily, in sync despite how new this still was, and somehow that felt just as intimate as everything else they’d done.

Nicky was nowhere to be seen, and Rio figured he was already in bed. That was probably for the best.

They settled on the couch with their food, the coffee table housing their wine glasses as they ate in easy silence. After a long week, it was exactly what Rio needed—something simple, something quiet.

“So,” Agatha finally said, watching Rio over the rim of her wine glass. “Rough day?”

Rio scoffed. “Rough week. Got stuck in the studio longer than I planned. And apparently, I can’t just go buy a pizza without it turning into a whole thing.”

Agatha gave her a knowing look. “Fame is so hard, isn’t it?”

Rio groaned, tipping her head back against the couch. “I’m so tired.”

“Poor thing,” Agatha murmured, patting Rio’s knee in mock sympathy.

Rio turned her head, smirking. “Careful, Harkness. You keep touching me like that, I’m gonna start thinking you like me or something.”

Agatha huffed, but she didn’t pull her hand away immediately. “Eat your pizza, Vidal.”

Rio did—but the entire time, her focus stayed locked on Agatha. The way she tucked her feet under her on the couch. The way she kept fidgeting with the hem of her sweatshirt. The way she was still here, sitting close, talking like this was normal.

And maybe, Rio thought, it could be.

When they finished eating, Rio leaned back, stretching her arm over the back of the couch. Agatha glanced at her wine glass, then back at Rio, something flickering in her gaze.

“I should probably head to bed soon,” she murmured, though she didn’t move.

Rio tilted her head, letting her fingers trail lightly along the back of Agatha’s shoulder. “You kicking me out?”

Agatha sighed, but there was no real exasperation behind it. “Nicky’s here, Rio.”

“I know,” Rio said, voice softer now. “I wasn’t suggesting anything.”

Agatha studied her for a long moment before finally, slowly, relaxing back against the couch.

Rio didn’t push it. Instead, she just let her fingers keep tracing absentminded patterns on Agatha’s back, feeling every slow, steady breath she took.

For a while, they just sat there, the weight of the past week settling between them.

Eventually, Agatha leaned into Rio’s side, just enough that Rio could press a kiss to the top of her head.

Then her hand gently cupped Agatha’s face, tilting her head ever so slightly to bring their lips together. It was soft at first, a slow press of warmth and the faintest taste of wine. She pulled back just a fraction, eyes searching Agatha’s as she asked, her voice a whisper, “Is this okay?”

Agatha didn’t respond with words. Instead, she closed the space between them again, her lips finding Rio’s, this time with more urgency. It was like they couldn’t get enough, as if the distance of the past week had been too much, too heavy, and now, with just this kiss, they could finally breathe again.

Rio groaned softly as Agatha kissed her deeper, pulling her closer, hands roaming over the curves of her back, pressing her against her own body. Every touch felt electric, like a puzzle piece finally snapping into place.

When they finally broke apart, Agatha’s breath was shallow, her chest rising and falling beneath Rio’s palm. Rio’s thumb traced the line of her jaw before she whispered, “I’ve missed you. So much.” She kissed her again, soft at first, but her body was already begging for more. When she finally pulled away, she rested her forehead against Agatha’s, eyes closed, and whispered in a breathless tone, “I’ve been dying to kiss you again.”

Agatha’s lips were swollen, her eyes heavy with desire, but there was something else there too—something tender. She didn’t say anything at first, just nodded, pressing a kiss to Rio’s chin. “Me too,” she murmured. “I missed this. Us.”

Rio smiled, but it was a smile laced with hunger. She leaned in again, wanting more, but just as their lips were about to meet again, a voice rang out from the top of the stairs.

“Mom?” Nicky’s voice was sleepy but loud enough to make them freeze. “Can I get some water?”

Both women paused, eyes wide for a moment, the tension between them suddenly cracking.

Agatha let out a quiet sigh, pulling back reluctantly. “Nicky…” She turned her head to the stairs, her voice soft but apologetic. “He's supposed to be asleep.”

Rio, trying to mask the grin pulling at her lips, leaned back against the couch, her hand still holding Agatha’s, not letting go. “Go get the kid his water,” she teased, voice low and playful.

Agatha shot Rio a look but couldn’t help the small laugh that escaped her lips. “Right. I guess privacy’s overrated.”

She gave Rio a quick, affectionate kiss before heading toward the kitchen. Rio stayed where she was, watching Agatha, the taste of the kiss still lingering, her heart racing from the intensity of it. She knew there was more to come between them, more to explore. But for now, the moment was interrupted, and as much as she hated to let it go, she knew that there would be more chances—more moments.

For now, though, she could just smile, content in the quiet promise of what was still to come.

~*~

As Agatha headed into the kitchen, Rio relaxed back onto the couch, her fingers still tingling from the warmth of Agatha’s touch. She exhaled slowly, her heart still racing, but the peaceful calm of being with Agatha settled over her. She allowed herself to relax for a moment, watching the soft glow of the lamps in the living room.

Then, from the stairs, she heard the familiar sound of footsteps padding down. Nicky. Rio straightened up, instinctively glancing toward the stairs. She hadn’t expected him to come down, but there he was, standing at the foot of the stairs, blinking groggily in the dim light of the living room.

His eyes immediately locked on Rio, and though he still looked sleepy, his face broke into a big grin. “Rio?” he mumbled, rubbing his eyes. “What are you doing here?”

Rio smiled, her heart warming at the sight of his excitement. “Hey, Nicky,” she greeted him, holding up a hand in a casual wave. “I was just hanging out with your mom. We were talking and, well… I thought I’d stop by and say hi.”

Nicky’s sleepy frown turned into a more awake smile as he shuffled over to her, his bare feet making soft padding sounds on the hardwood floor. “I missed you this week,” he admitted, his voice still thick with sleep. “You didn’t make it to our jam session at school.”

Rio laughed softly, touched by his words. “I know, buddy. I’m sorry. We’ve been in the studio working on stuff. But I’m glad to see you,” she said, giving him an affectionate smile. “How’ve you been? Still rocking out with your guitar?”

“Yeah,” Nicky said, his excitement evident as he glanced over at the kitchen, then back to Rio. “Mom didn’t say you were coming over tonight or I would’ve waited! I didn’t expect to see you until next week.”

Rio smiled, touched by how much Nicky clearly liked her company. “Well, here I am,” she said. “I’ve been busy, but I couldn’t miss the chance to hang out.”

Before she could say more, Agatha returned from the kitchen, catching the end of their conversation. Nicky turned toward her with a happy grin. “Mom, Rio’s here! I didn’t know she was coming over tonight.”

Agatha smiled at the exchange, her voice warm but cautious, as she handed him a glass of water. “Yes, she was in the neighborhood so she stopped by.”

Rio felt a rush of affection for both of them, and as Nicky turned back to her, she playfully ruffled his hair. “You know, I wouldn’t miss seeing you,” she said softly. “How about another jam session soon?”

Nicky’s face lit up, as he drank his water. “Yes! That’d be awesome!” he said enthusiastically, bouncing on his feet.

Agatha chuckled softly, taking the glass back from him. “Okay, buddy, it’s late. Let’s not get too crazy. It’s way past your bedtime, mister.”

“Yeah, yeah, I’m going back to bed,” Nicky grumbled good-naturedly, but he gave Rio a final smile before heading toward the stairs. “Goodnight, Rio. It was great seeing you.”

“Goodnight, Nicky,” Rio called after him, her heart full as she watched him disappear upstairs.

As Nicky disappeared upstairs, Agatha returned to the living room, her expression soft but thoughtful. She glanced at Rio, her eyes full of tenderness, before sitting down next to her on the couch.

“That went well,” Agatha said quietly, her voice warm. “He really loves playing with you.”

Rio grinned, nodding. “Yeah, he’s a natural. I love how excited he gets about the jam sessions.”

Agatha smiled but then let out a soft sigh, her shoulders relaxing. She shifted a little, her gaze turning more serious. “About earlier… I think we need to talk about privacy. I don’t want Nicky walking in on us like that again.” She met Rio’s eyes, her voice quieter now. “We need to be careful. Especially in moments like that.”

Rio felt a sudden flush creep up her neck, but she nodded, her lips curving into a sheepish smile. “I get it. I don’t want to make things awkward for Nicky. Or you. I just… I don’t know, I didn’t think we’d be interrupted.”

Agatha let out a soft laugh, her eyes still warm but cautious. “It’s just… Nicky’s already so attached to you, and I’m not sure how Mia will react to all of this.” She hesitated for a moment before continuing, “I’m not ready to talk about the future yet, but I do need to be mindful of how we go about this.”

Rio bit her lip, understanding Agatha’s hesitation. She wasn’t ready for any heavy talks about what this was, and Rio respected that. “I’m cool with that. I don’t want to rush anything either. Just… wanted to make sure you knew how I feel.”

Agatha’s expression softened as she gave a small nod. “I know you do. And I care about you too. But let’s just… take it slow, okay?”

Rio smiled, giving a slow nod in return. “Slow sounds perfect.”

Agatha leaned back against the couch, reaching for the remote control with a small sigh. “We’ll figure it out. Just, for now, maybe we keep things a little less… spontaneous,” she said with a teasing smirk, referring to their earlier moment.

Rio chuckled and nodded again. “Yeah, no more impromptu make-out sessions on your couch.”

Agatha smiled and clicked on the TV, her fingers brushing lightly against Rio’s as she did. “How about a movie? Something to just… relax.”

Rio leaned back, her body still close to Agatha’s, feeling a sense of comfort in the quiet after everything that had happened. “Sounds perfect. Nothing too serious, though. Just something to unwind.”

Agatha picked a movie, and as the opening credits rolled, Rio found herself settling in beside Agatha, the tension from the moment earlier melting away. They didn’t need to rush forward, not just yet. Right now, the quiet companionship was enough, and that was something she was willing to hold onto.

~*~

Rio’s eyes fluttered open in the dark, her body still warm from the closeness of Agatha’s. The TV was still on, the faint glow of the screen casting long shadows across the room. She blinked, the soft hum of the movie credits still playing in the background. Everything felt so peaceful, so right, and for a moment, she considered just staying there forever, with Agatha’s body just stretched out pretty much on top of her.

But then reality hit her. She fished her phone out of her back pocket, careful not to disturb Agatha as she unlocked it and checked the time.

4:15am.

A soft sigh escaped Rio’s lips as she leaned her head back into the couch cushions, the weight of exhaustion pressing down on her. She couldn’t believe how much time had passed. She’d wanted to stay, wanted to savor the moment longer, but she knew it was time to go. Agatha needed rest, and so did she. Plus, Nicky was asleep upstairs, and as much as Rio adored being here, she didn’t want to overstay her welcome.

She gently shifted, brushing her fingers over Agatha’s hair, tucking a few strands behind her ear as she whispered softly, “Agatha… it’s late. You should get to bed.”

Agatha stirred in her sleep, her body shifting slightly, but she didn’t fully wake. Rio’s heart fluttered as she realized how comfortable they had both gotten with each other. It felt like something more, even though they hadn’t officially defined what it was yet.

Rio ran a hand over Agatha’s shoulder and leaned in to kiss her softly on the cheek. “Hey, babe, it’s really late. I need to head out soon, and you should go to bed.”

Agatha mumbled something incoherent, clearly not fully awake, but Rio smiled at the sound of her voice—so warm and familiar. She gently nudged her again, a little more insistently. “Agatha,” she said softly, “you need to sleep. It’s really late, and I can’t stay much longer.”

Agatha blinked awake, her eyelids heavy as she tried to focus on Rio’s face in the dim light. It took a few moments for her to process what Rio was saying, her gaze clearing as she realized what time it was.

“Right,” Agatha mumbled groggily, her voice thick with sleep. She gave Rio a sleepy smile, rubbing her eyes. “I guess we lost track of time.”

Rio chuckled, her fingers brushing over Agatha’s cheek as she smiled back. “We really did,” she said, before leaning in to kiss her once more, tender and slow. “But it’s really late, and I think it’s time I go home.”

Agatha nodded, her expression soft but a little reluctant as she slowly pushed herself up from Rio’s chest. “I understand,” she said quietly, looking up at Rio with those quiet, unreadable eyes. “Let me walk you to the door,” she offered as she pushed herself up from the couch, stretching a bit. Her movements were still slow, her body still adjusting to waking up.

Rio smiled warmly, watching Agatha move around in her sleepy haze. “I’ll be okay, but thanks,” she said, standing up as well. “You go to bed.”

“Just… text me when you get home?” Agatha said, her voice soft but genuine, her tired eyes locking onto Rio’s as she tried to convey more than just the words.

Rio’s heart skipped a beat, her smile widening. “Of course. I will.” She leaned in, giving Agatha one last kiss, lingering just a little longer than she intended. “Goodnight, Agatha.”

“Goodnight, Rio,” Agatha whispered, watching her with a gaze that lingered a moment longer, filled with that unspoken warmth. “Drive safe.”

Rio nodded, her smile still in place as she slipped out the door. She stood on the porch for a moment, looking at the house—at Agatha, at everything that had happened, and feeling that familiar tug of something more.

As she headed down the path toward her car, she couldn’t help but think that maybe this was the start of something more than she had expected.

~*~

Rio’s eyes fluttered open, and for a moment, she couldn’t quite figure out where she was. The late-night haze still hung around her, but the soft morning light streaming through the curtains was enough to wake her fully. She groaned and stretched, feeling the exhaustion of the week hitting her all at once.

Her phone was next to her, and she grabbed it lazily, her fingers still half asleep. She smiled when she saw the text from Agatha, a simple “Good morning” with a teasing emoji. Rio chuckled and typed back: 

Rio

Morning, beautiful.

She sent it off with a grin, feeling the warmth of the moment from the night before still lingering inside her.

After a few more moments of stretching and blinking sleep from her eyes, Rio finally dragged herself out of bed. She was running late for her usual routine but didn’t care too much—she deserved a slow Saturday morning.

When she made it downstairs, she found Mia sprawled out on the couch, her eyes glued to the TV. It was one of those lazy Saturday mornings where Mia wasn’t rushing off to anything, and Rio couldn’t help but smile at how much Mia had grown.

“Morning, kiddo,” Rio said, crossing the living room with a yawn.

Mia glanced up, raising an eyebrow at Rio. “Look who’s finally decided to join the land of the living,” she teased. “I was starting to get worried about you. You were sleeping in so late.”

Rio smirked, brushing her hair out of her face as she poured herself some coffee. “Yeah, well… long week. And I had a bit of a late night last night.”

Mia sat up a little, giving her a curious look. “What time did you get in?” she asked, sounding just a bit too casual, though Rio could detect the subtle note of concern in her voice. “I went to bed around midnight, and you still weren’t home.”

Rio paused for a second, her fingers tightening around her coffee mug. She didn’t want to over explain, but she didn’t exactly want to hide anything either. “I got home a little after midnight. Just needed to get some rest,” Rio said, keeping her voice light.

Mia didn’t seem entirely convinced, her eyes narrowing for just a moment before she shrugged and picked up her phone again, as though she had already decided not to press further.

“Okay, just making sure,” Mia said, but there was something in the way she said it, a little quieter than usual, that made Rio think Mia might have picked up on something more.

“Anyway,” Rio continued, trying to shake the feeling off, “I was busy working all week. Needed some downtime, I guess.”

Mia nodded but didn’t say anything else. For a moment, the air felt heavier than usual, but then Mia leaned back against the couch, her attention back on the TV. Rio let out a breath she didn’t realize she’d been holding, feeling a bit more relaxed.

She turned toward the kitchen, sipping her coffee, and after a moment of quiet, texted Agatha again.

Rio

Mia had questions this morning. I don’t think she’s buying the whole ‘late night at the studio’ thing.

As she sent the message, Rio leaned against the counter, wondering how to navigate this situation with Mia.

Rio’s phone buzzed as she stood by the counter, taking another sip of her coffee. It was Agatha’s reply:

Agatha

Oh no, what did she say? Is everything okay?

Rio couldn’t help but smile softly at Agatha’s concern. The warmth of the message made her feel more at ease. She typed back quickly:

Rio

Mia’s good, she’s just… perceptive. She picked up on some things, you know? She was asking about the late night, but I think she’s okay for now. I think she knows something’s different, but I haven’t had the chance to have the conversation yet .

A few moments later, Agatha replied:

Agatha

She’ll come around. Kids are surprisingly resilient. You just need to be honest with her, when you’re ready. Don’t rush it .

Rio stared at the screen, her fingers hovering over the keyboard. She could feel the weight of the situation, the building pressure of Mia’s questions that she knew she couldn’t avoid for much longer. It wasn’t just Mia who had to adjust; Rio had to come to terms with how much of her life she was willing to share, especially when it came to Agatha.

Rio

I’ll talk to her. Just… I want to make sure we’re in a good place first. You know?

Agatha’s reply came almost instantly:

Agatha 

Of course. Just take your time, Rio. This isn’t something to rush. I’m definitely not ready to tell Nicky either. We’re good keeping this to ourselves for now 💜

Rio smiled as she read Agatha’s message. Her heart warmed at the reassurance, but the concern for Mia still lingered in the back of her mind.

~*~

The following Monday, Mia came home from school with a look on her face that Rio instantly recognized: a mix of frustration and discomfort. As Rio poured herself a cup of coffee, Mia dropped her bag on the chair and sat down across from her at the kitchen table.

“Mia, what’s going on?” Rio asked gently, sensing something was off.

Mia looked up at her, her brow furrowed. “People were teasing me at school today,” she said, her voice laced with annoyance. “I don’t know if you noticed, but there were some pictures of you from the other day… leaving this liquor store with two boxes of pizza and a bottle of whatever, I don’t know.”

Rio’s stomach tightened, and she set her mug down carefully. “Great. The stupid paparazzi again…” she muttered, rubbing a hand over her face.

Mia continued, voice shaky, “Yeah, well. People were saying that you were finding me a new daddy, or… well, one kid said it was probably a new mommy, and then someone else called you a ‘fucking dyke,” she said, making air quotation marks and rolling her eyes. “Which is ridiculous because apparently people judge you for buying pizza now.”

The words hit Rio harder than she expected. Mia, at 15, was still so fragile in some ways, despite the tough exterior she often put up. Rio was suddenly acutely aware of just how much weight she carried on her shoulders, not only for herself but for Mia as well.

But then Mia added, “And then someone else said, ‘No wonder Mia doesn’t have a father; her mom goes through so many people, she probably doesn’t even know who Mia’s daddy is.’”

Rio’s chest tightened at the cruelty of the comment, and her hand gripped the edge of the table. Her instinct was to protect Mia, to shield her from this kind of pain, but she knew the teasing wasn’t going to stop. She could only try her best to be there for her daughter.

Mia’s gaze was sharp as she met Rio’s eyes. “I told them they were full of shit and to leave me the hell alone. But it’s… embarrassing.”

Rio exhaled, trying to keep her voice calm, even though she was furious at whoever had dared to say that to Mia. “Mia, I’m really sorry you had to deal with that. I should’ve been more careful.”

“Well,” Mia started, crossing her arms, “I’m not a little kid anymore. I don’t need you to protect me. But… I wish you would’ve told me before it all started. I mean, you know… if you’re seeing someone. I could’ve at least been ready for it.”

Rio felt a knot in her stomach. She had been trying to protect Mia from this, trying to figure out how to handle things without making it worse. But she hadn’t prepared her daughter for what was coming. The realization made her feel guilty.

“Mia, it’s just… complicated,” Rio said softly. “I didn’t want to make it harder for you, especially with everything else you’re dealing with. But I promise, I’ll talk to you more about it soon. Just… not yet, okay?”

Mia raised an eyebrow, but she didn’t argue. Rio continued, “Just don’t let people keep saying shit like that about you,” she muttered. “It’s one thing to have people talk about me. It comes with the territory, but I don’t want anyone talking about you like that.”

Mia nodded and Rio smiled softly, relieved that her daughter didn’t seem too upset with her. “I won’t let them. I promise.” 

“Thanks for having my back.”

Mia just shrugged, looking away. “Yeah, well, it’s not like I have much choice.” Then she got up and grabbed her bag. “I’ll be upstairs. Got loads of homework”

“Okay, I’ll be here,” Rio said, watching her leave. She wasn’t sure if Mia fully understood the complexity of the situation, but at least she hadn’t completely shut her out.

Once Mia was gone, Rio sat there in the quiet of the kitchen, thinking about everything that had happened in the past week. She knew this was just the beginning of a bigger conversation, one that she wasn’t quite ready for yet. But she’d figure it out. She always did.

 

Thirteen

Chapter Notes

I know some of you are waiting for Luminous and the next chapter is like 90% ready. I'm just stuck on one scene that I just can't seem to get right. I'll give it one more shot some time today and will probably post the new chapter tomorrow or Tuesday.

But in the meantime, I hope you enjoy this one.

Agatha had woken early, as usual, her mind already moving through the rhythm of the day ahead. Wednesdays meant the usual hum of Sonata Grove, followed by Mia’s piano lesson—something that usually brought a quiet sense of purpose. 

But today she felt a bit worried that Mia had been asking questions about what Rio’s been doing. She felt a bit guilty, but at this point, she didn’t feel like she could walk away unscathed.

Nicky had already rushed out the door, full of chatter and barely zipped up, as he climbed into Wanda’s car, and now the house was quiet. Agatha was halfway through her coffee and had just pulled out her notes for the morning when her phone buzzed.

It was Rio.

Rio

Hey, Agatha. Just wanted to give you a heads-up about Mia. She’s been upset. Some photos of me leaving a liquor store with pizza and wine last Friday got out, and now kids at school are saying stuff. The pics are harmless, and they’re talking mostly shit about me, but you know how kids are. She’s been really down.

Agatha stared at the message for a second, her brows drawing together. She could already feel it—that tight little knot in her chest. Poor Mia. And Rio… God, she must’ve felt helpless.

She typed back.

Agatha

I’m sorry, Rio. That’s awful. I’ll keep a close eye on her today.

She paused, then added:

Agatha

And I’ll be gentle with her. Promise.

The words felt right—quiet, but steady. Mia didn’t need a lecture or forced smiles. She just needed space to be herself, to know she wasn’t being judged. Agatha knew what it was like to be young and guarded, to carry more than you knew how to name.

A new buzz.

Rio

Thanks. I’m going to try talking to her when she gets home. I don’t know if I’ll say the right thing. I feel like I keep getting it all wrong lately. 

Agatha leaned back against the counter, her phone resting in her hand. She could hear Rio’s voice in her head—low, frustrated, maybe a little tired. The kind of tired that didn’t come from lack of sleep, but from caring too much and not being able to fix things.

She smiled, just a little. That was something they had in common.

Agatha

You’re doing better than you think, you know. Mia’s lucky to have you. And I’ll take care of her today. You don’t have to worry.

She hovered for a second before hitting send. It felt… strange, letting something soft slip through like that. But it was the truth. And Rio should hear it.

Agatha set her phone down and looked at the time. The hours would fly. Mia would be here soon enough, and Agatha wanted her to feel, if nothing else, that this space—this small corner of the world—was still safe.

She went to the piano, fingers brushing over the keys, but her thoughts lingered on the girl who was hurting—and on the woman trying so hard to protect her.

~*~

The day had been a whirlwind already. Agatha had just finished a few lessons at Sonata Grove and was heading back to her office when she received a call from the school nurse. Nicky wasn’t feeling well—she needed to come pick him up. Agatha’s heart sank, and she hurried to grab her things.

When she arrived, Nicky was sitting in the nurse’s office, his cheeks flushed with color, and his eyes heavy. He was trying to be brave, but Agatha could see the telltale signs of a fever. She knelt down beside him, brushing a hand through his messy hair.

“You okay, kiddo?” she asked softly.

“I’m just tired, Mom,” he mumbled, his voice weak.

Agatha sighed and helped him gather his things before taking him to Sonata Grove. She wasn’t sure what had caused the fever, but she knew he’d need rest. Since her schedule was light, she decided to take him to her office so he could sleep while she finished up the last class of the day.

“Let’s get you settled, sweetheart,” Agatha murmured, leading him to her office. She set him up on the small couch with a blanket and tucked him in.

“Thanks, Mom,” he whispered, already drifting off.

With a small smile, Agatha kissed his forehead and tiptoed out of the room, closing the door quietly behind her. The last thing she wanted was for him to be disturbed while he rested.

Just as Agatha was returning to the reception, she saw Rio and Mia walk in together. Mia looked tired, but she didn’t seem to be in any kind of distress. Agatha smiled at them both, though she could feel the tension between herself and Rio, and it had only been a few days since they’d shared that passionate moment on her couch.

“Hey, Mia,” Agatha greeted her student, giving her a quick but warm smile. “Go ahead and head to the classroom. I’ll be right there.”

Mia nodded, her eyes flickering between Agatha and Rio. As Mia walked away, Agatha gestured for Rio to follow her.

They slipped into the office quickly, Agatha closing the door behind them. She hadn’t expected to have this much time alone with Rio, especially with Nicky sleeping in the room, but the urge to be close to Rio hit her like a tidal wave.

“Everything okay with Mia?” Agatha asked, though her voice sounded more distracted than she intended.

Rio let out a soft sigh, her brow furrowing as she looked at Agatha. “She’s had a tough day,” Rio said quietly, leaning against the desk. “She’s worried about the teasing at school. I just want her to feel safe.”

Agatha’s heart clenched for both of them. “She will,” she said softly, her eyes meeting Rio’s. “Mia’s strong. She’s got you, and she’s got her safe space here. We’ll help her through this.”

There was a long pause. Rio was looking at her with those dark eyes, and Agatha could feel the intensity of the moment building. She wanted nothing more than to step closer, to kiss her again, to feel that warmth.

But then, Rio’s eyes flickered to the couch, and she tensed slightly. “Is Nicky okay?” she asked softly, her concern evident as she saw the small figure curled up on the couch, fast asleep.

Agatha sighed, running a hand through her hair. “He’s got a fever,” she explained quietly, her gaze lingering on Nicky. “It's probably just the flu. He should be okay. He just needs some sleep.”

Rio’s eyes softened with sympathy, and then she stepped toward Agatha, her presence calming. Agatha’s breath caught in her throat as she felt the pull between them.

With Nicky still asleep, Agatha found herself unable to resist. She stepped into Rio’s space, their gazes locking, and Rio leaned in slowly, brushing her lips against Agatha’s. It was soft, gentle, but it carried the weight of everything Agatha had been holding back.

Agatha let out a breathless sigh as Rio deepened the kiss, her hand coming up to cup Agatha’s cheek. The kiss was everything she had been craving, everything she hadn’t allowed herself to feel in the rush of the past few days. Rio’s lips were warm, her touch tender, and Agatha melted into it.

When they broke apart, Agatha’s heart raced, and she looked up at Rio, her chest rising and falling rapidly. “Rio…” she whispered, her voice thick with emotion. “I… I don’t want to be reckless with him in the room.”

Rio’s thumb brushed over Agatha’s cheek, her smile soft but knowing. “It’s okay,” she whispered back, her voice low and steady. “You’re not being reckless. I’ve just missed you.”

Agatha closed her eyes for a moment, trying to steady herself. This was more than she had expected today, more than she was prepared to handle—but Rio was here, and it felt so right. And she couldn’t help herself when she leaned in again, capturing Rio’s lips in a quick but powerful kiss.

After a moment, Agatha pulled away slowly, her heart racing. Rio’s warmth still lingered on her lips, and it was hard to shake the feeling of her closeness, of how easily they had fallen back into each other.

“I hate to leave him like this,” Agatha said quietly, glancing back at Nicky on the couch. She felt a pang of guilt at the thought of leaving him while he was sick, even though he was resting.

Rio, sensing her hesitation, gave her a reassuring smile. “I can stay with Nicky while you go to class with Mia,” she offered, her voice soft but certain. “He’s already asleep, and I can keep an eye on him. I don’t mind.”

Agatha hesitated for a moment, surprised by Rio’s offer. She had been so preoccupied with the tension of the situation that she hadn’t even thought about it. But Rio was right—Nicky was sleeping, and Agatha’s class with Mia was about to start.

“You’d be okay with that?” Agatha asked, her brow furrowed slightly. “I don’t want to put you out.”

Rio smiled again, her eyes soft with affection. “Of course, Agatha,” she said gently. “I’m happy to help.”

Agatha’s chest tightened at the thought of Rio staying, even if just for a little while. “Okay,” she finally said, her voice quiet, “thank you.”

Rio gave her a warm, knowing smile and reached out, brushing a hand over Agatha’s arm. “It’s nothing,” she replied, her thumb gently caressing the soft skin of Agatha’s forearm. “Go ahead. I’ll be right here.”

With that, Agatha took a deep breath and walked toward the door. She glanced back over her shoulder to find Rio already settling into the chair by Nicky’s side, looking at him with a watchful, protective gaze.

Agatha’s heart softened as she opened the door to head to Mia’s class. The connection between them was undeniable, and seeing Rio so easily take on a role that felt so natural for her—caring for Nicky, making sure everything was okay—was a reminder of just how much Rio had already become a part of their lives. It wasn’t just about the chemistry between them anymore. It was about the way Rio fit so effortlessly into the rhythm of Agatha’s world, like she’d belonged there all along.

~*~

Agatha sat at the piano, her fingers gently pressing the keys, guiding Mia through the familiar song that the young girl was struggling with. The notes, though challenging, should have come more naturally by now. But as Mia played, her timing was off, and her fingers stuttered over the keys as if she was in a different world entirely. It was becoming more and more evident that Mia was somewhere else, lost in her thoughts.

“Mia,” Agatha said, her voice warm but firm. “Slow down. Focus on the melody. Don’t rush it.”

Mia didn’t respond immediately. She stared at the keys in front of her, eyes unfocused. Agatha’s concern deepened. Mia had been distracted through the entire lesson, her usual energy replaced by a quiet tension that Agatha couldn’t ignore.

“Mia,” Agatha repeated, her tone softer now. “What’s on your mind? You’ve been off today. Talk to me.”

Mia looked up at Agatha then, her expression guarded, as though she was weighing how much to say. Agatha waited patiently, giving her the space to open up. It took a while, but Mia finally sighed and let out a quiet, almost imperceptible groan of frustration.

“It’s… school,” Mia muttered, her voice barely above a whisper. “I don’t know. People have been saying stuff about my mom.” She paused, biting her lip. “They said she’s seeing someone now. Like, a new person. And I’m getting teased, like… they’re saying the worst things about her, you know? Which is so stupid. It’s like my mom can’t do anything without people talking about it.”

Agatha felt a pang in her chest. She knew how much Mia cared about her mother and how much pressure she already carried as the daughter of a public figure. The idea of people making cruel comments about Rio didn’t sit well with Agatha, especially when Mia was already vulnerable from all the chaos of her teenage years.

“I’m sorry, Mia,” Agatha said, her voice low and understanding. “What exactly are they saying?”

Mia shifted uncomfortably in her seat, clearly reluctant to delve too deep into the details. “Some kids are making jokes,” she said with a touch of bitterness. “Saying stuff like… no wonder I don’t  have a father, like she’s gone through so many people. They even said she probably doesn’t even know who my father is. It’s just… ugh, it feels like everyone’s talking about her. It’s embarrassing.”

Agatha nodded slowly, understanding the weight of Mia’s words. She could hear the hurt in Mia’s voice, the way she had to swallow back her emotions as she tried to brush it off. Agatha leaned forward, her eyes meeting Mia’s with a quiet, reassuring intensity.

“Mia,” Agatha said softly, her voice gentle but filled with certainty. “You know none of that is true, right? None of it matters.”

Mia’s eyes flickered with a mix of confusion and frustration. “It doesn’t matter? Everyone’s talking about it, and—”

“People will always talk,” Agatha interrupted, her tone calm but firm. “But it doesn’t change anything. What matters is that your mom loves you. And you know that. Whatever people are saying, it doesn’t define you or your mom. Your mom isn’t some public spectacle; she’s a person. And she’s not defined by anyone’s assumptions or cruel comments.”

Mia’s shoulders drooped a little, and for the first time that afternoon, she seemed to relax, just slightly. Agatha reached out, placing a hand gently on her shoulder in a gesture of reassurance.

“Your mom’s a strong woman. And if she’s seeing someone, she trusts them, Mia. And she deserves to be happy.” Agatha gave her a small smile. “You deserve to see her happy, too.”

Mia stayed quiet for a moment, then nodded, though she still seemed troubled. “I know. It just… feels weird. I don’t know. I don’t want to be that kid at school, you know? The one whose mom is some sort of joke. The one whose mom is so… open about everything.”

Agatha’s heart softened for her. She could see that Mia was struggling with the balance between protecting her mom and also finding her own space to be a teenager, something that had to be incredibly complicated with the added pressure of being in Rio’s world.

“I understand,” Agatha said quietly, her voice full of empathy. “But you’re not alone in this, Mia. Your mom’s been through a lot, and she’s still standing strong. And you’re the same way. You’re strong too. Just know that you have people around you who care. Including me.” She smiled a little more widely. “And if you ever need to talk, you know I’m always here.”

Mia looked up at her, her eyes softening as she seemed to take in Agatha’s words. “Thanks, Agatha,” she said, her voice barely a whisper, but sincere.

Agatha gave her a small nod and gestured back to the piano. “Let’s get back to the song, okay? One note at a time.”

Mia gave a small nod in return, and this time, when she placed her hands on the keys, there was less tension in her fingers. She played with a little more focus, though Agatha could tell there was still a lot on her mind.

As they continued the lesson, Agatha couldn’t shake the feeling that there was so much more Mia was carrying beneath the surface. But for now, all Agatha could do was be there, offer a little comfort, and make sure she knew that she was not alone in facing whatever came next.

~*~

As the lesson wrapped up, Agatha looked up from the piano and noticed Mia’s shoulders had relaxed slightly, though the weight of her earlier thoughts still seemed to linger in her eyes. Agatha decided to bring up Nicky’s condition, hoping to shift the focus a little.

“Mia,” Agatha said softly as she gathered her music sheets, “Your mom stayed with Nicky while I was with you. He has a fever.”

Mia’s brow furrowed with concern, her earlier tension softening. “Nicky’s sick? Is he okay?”

Agatha smiled gently. “He’s fine. Just a fever. He’s been resting in my office, and Rio’s been keeping him company while we had our lesson.”

Mia nodded and, without further hesitation, the two of them made their way out of the music room and down the hall to Agatha’s office. The closer they got, the more Mia’s pace slowed, her thoughts clearly still caught up in the earlier conversation.

As they reached the doorway, Agatha could hear Nicky’s voice, soft and comforting, his words a gentle murmur in the otherwise quiet room. When they walked in, the sight before them was unexpected but somehow soothing.

Nicky, propped up against the side of the couch, was leaning against Rio, his head resting on her shoulder. Rio was bent slightly toward him, her voice quiet but kind, asking him about his day at school as she ran her fingers through his hair in a comforting, almost maternal gesture. They were both so absorbed in their conversation that they didn’t notice Agatha and Mia standing in the doorway for a moment.

Nicky’s eyes flicked up, finally noticing the two of them. A soft smile tugged at the corners of his lips. “Hey, Mia!”

Mia returned his smile, though her expression was still somewhat distant. “How’s the fever?” she asked, her voice still holding a bit of concern.

“It’s better,” Nicky said, giving a small shrug. He shifted so that he wasn’t leaning on Rio as much but stayed close to her. “Rio’s been keeping me company. Told me about the band and everything.”

Rio gave a soft chuckle, her arm still wrapped loosely around Nicky’s shoulders. “Yeah, we were just talking about how loud our band can get sometimes. It’s kind of a miracle we ever practice at all with all the noise.”

Mia nodded, though there was still a glint of something unspoken in her eyes as she glanced at Rio. 

Agatha stepped in to break the small tension, a gentle smile curving her lips as she looked between Rio and Nicky. “I’ll take over now. Thanks for staying with him, Rio.”

Rio gave her a knowing look and nodded, standing up slowly from the couch. “Of course. Yeah, I think it’s time we get going. I have a few things I need to take care of.”

She gave Nicky a quick ruffle of his hair before looking over at Agatha, the two of them sharing a brief, silent exchange. Agatha’s heart skipped a beat, the pull between them still undeniable, though she kept her composure as they spoke in front of Mia.

“Thanks for letting me hang out with him,” Rio said to Agatha with a smile, “I’ll check in on you later?”

Agatha nodded, her tone light yet sincere. “Of course. And if you need anything, don’t hesitate to reach out.”

As Rio stood to leave, she gave Nicky a soft ruffle of his hair. “Rest up, okay? I’ll see you soon.”

Nicky beamed up at her, giving her a thumbs up. “See you, Rio.”

Agatha’s heart tightened as she watched Rio, a mix of longing and uncertainty in her chest. It hadn’t been long since their last conversation, but something about seeing her with Nicky made it all feel more real—more significant. She tried to push the feelings down, reminding herself to stay focused.

Mia followed her mother to the door, but called out over her shoulder, “Feel better, Nicky!” 

Rio smiled down at her daughter, though there was a flicker of something else in her eyes—concern, maybe, or relief. Whatever it was, it didn’t quite reach her voice when she turned to Agatha.

“I’ll see you guys soon.”

With that, Rio and Mia left together, the door clicking softly behind them. Agatha stood in the quiet of her office for a moment, staring at the now-empty space where they’d just been.

She let out a breath, her thoughts swirling as she returned to the desk to organize a few papers. There was something about the way Rio and Mia had left together—something solid, even if she couldn’t quite name it.

She knew the dynamics between them were complex, but for now, she had to focus on the here and now. Mia’s lesson had gone well, and Nicky was recovering. There was enough to be grateful for, even if there were still questions she wasn’t ready to answer yet.

~*~

Agatha had spent the next few days tending to a feverish, miserable Nicky. His flu had hit him hard, keeping him glued to the couch with tissues scattered around him, his usually boundless energy replaced with exhaustion. She hated seeing him like this, but at least his fever had started to break.

She’d just finished making him a bowl of soup when her phone buzzed.

Rio

Hey, how’s the patient?

Agatha exhaled, leaning against the kitchen counter.

Agatha

Still a little feverish, but better than yesterday. He’s mostly sleeping now.

Rio  

Poor kid. You holding up?

Agatha stared at the question for a moment. She was exhausted, to be honest. She hadn’t left the house in days, barely sleeping as she checked on Nicky every few hours. But something about Rio checking in made warmth bloom in her chest.

Agatha  

I’ve been better. But I’ll survive.

She expected that to be the end of it, but Rio’s next text made her blink.

Rio

I miss you .

Agatha’s fingers hesitated over the keyboard. It wasn’t unexpected, not after the night they’d spent together and the texts they’d exchanged since. But reading it still made her pulse quicken.

Before she could overthink it, another message popped up.

Rio

Let me bring you something. Both of you. A little care package. Maybe some soup, tea, some cookies?

Agatha smiled despite herself, shaking her head.

Agatha

You don’t have to do that.

Rio

I know. But I want to.

Agatha bit her lip, hesitating. She should probably say no. But the idea of seeing Rio, even just for a few minutes, was too tempting to resist.

Agatha

Okay. Just nothing too much. It’s been a battle to get him to eat, and I don’t want you going overboard.

Rio

No promises ;)

Agatha rolled her eyes, but she felt lighter than she had in days.

~*~

 

A little over an hour later, Agatha heard the sound of a car pulling into her driveway. She quickly checked on Nicky—still fast asleep on the couch, his little body curled under a blanket—before heading to the door.

When she opened it, Rio stood there, balancing two large paper bags in her arms, a lopsided grin on her face. She was bundled up in a hoodie and leather jacket, her hair tucked under a beanie.

“Before you say anything,” Rio said, stepping inside without waiting for an invitation, “I did go overboard, but in my defense, I don’t know how to do things halfway.”

Agatha crossed her arms, arching an eyebrow as she closed the door behind her. “I said nothing too much.”

Rio gave her a pointed look. “And I ignored you. You’ll live.”

She set the bags on the kitchen counter and started unpacking: homemade soup from a little place she swore had the best broth in the city, a variety of teas, a jar of honey, fresh bread, lemon cookies, and—Agatha huffed a laugh—a small plush guitar with oversized eyes and a cute smile.

“For Nicky,” Rio said, holding up the toy. “Thought he could use a little buddy while he’s sick.”

Agatha’s heart twisted unexpectedly at the thoughtfulness of it all. “You’re ridiculous,” she murmured, but there was no bite to her words.

Rio smirked, stepping a little closer. “You love it.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but her body betrayed her, leaning into Rio’s warmth. “I tolerate it.”

Rio hummed. “Uh-huh.” Her hand brushed Agatha’s waist, subtle but deliberate, and Agatha exhaled slowly, letting her eyes flutter shut for just a second.

God, she’d missed this. Missed her.

But before either of them could lean in any further, a small groggy voice interrupted them.

“Rio?”

Agatha stepped back quickly, turning to see Nicky standing in the hallway, blanket draped over his shoulders. His hair was a mess, and his face was still flushed with fever, but his eyes lit up at the sight of Rio.

“Hey, kiddo,” Rio said, her voice warm. “You’re supposed to be resting.”

“I heard your voice,” he mumbled, rubbing at his eyes. “And I missed you.”

Agatha felt something crack wide open in her chest at the way Rio’s face softened completely.

“Well, lucky for you, I brought you some good stuff.” Rio crouched down to his level, pulling the plush guitar from the counter and handing it to him. “And I figured you might need a little sick-day companion.”

Nicky took the plush with a small smile, pressing his face into it. “I love it.”

Rio grinned. “Good. Now come on, let’s get you back on the couch before your mom yells at me.”

Agatha scoffed. “I don’t yell.”

Rio shot her an amused look as she helped Nicky shuffle back toward the living room. “You give looks, though. Very sharp, very scary.”

Nicky giggled, his voice still a little hoarse, and Agatha sighed but didn’t argue. It was hardly worth it when Rio had already won Nicky over completely.

By the time they got him settled with a cup of tea and a small bowl of soup, he was looking more awake. He clutched the plush guitar to his chest, occasionally sneaking small smiles at Rio between spoonfuls.

Rio stayed for a while, keeping both Agatha and Nicky company as they lounged in the living room. She didn’t push for anything, didn’t steal any more touches or kisses, but she was there, warm and steady, filling the space with quiet ease.

Eventually, Nicky started nodding off again, and Agatha stood to adjust his blanket. She glanced over at Rio, hesitating for only a moment before jerking her head toward the kitchen.

Rio followed without a word.

The moment they were out of sight, Agatha turned to her, keeping her voice low. “Thank you. For all of this.”

Rio smiled, leaning casually against the counter. “You don’t have to thank me.”

“I do.” Agatha took a breath, glancing toward the living room before meeting Rio’s gaze again. “I don’t—this isn’t… easy for me.”

Rio’s expression softened. “I know.” She reached out, brushing her fingers lightly against Agatha’s wrist. “I’m not in a rush. You know that, right?”

Agatha swallowed, nodding. She did know. It was probably the only reason she hadn’t run yet.

Rio squeezed her hand once before pulling away. “Alright. I should get out of your hair. Let you rest.”

Agatha wanted to tell her she didn’t have to go, but the words caught in her throat.

Instead, she walked her to the door, lingering as Rio slipped her jacket back on.

“Text me later?” Rio asked, voice quieter now.

Agatha exhaled softly. “Yeah.”

Rio smirked. “Good.” She reached for the doorknob, then hesitated. “Oh, and, uh—make sure Nicky drinks plenty of fluids.”

Agatha rolled her eyes but smiled. “I know how to take care of my son, Rio.”

“Just checking.” Rio grinned, and then, with a final lingering glance, she stepped outside into the cool evening air.

Just as Rio turned to leave, Agatha reached out without thinking, fingers curling around the sleeve of her jacket.

Rio barely had time to react before Agatha tugged her back, closing the space between them. Their bodies brushed, and Agatha hesitated for only a second before tilting her chin up and pressing her lips to Rio’s.

It wasn’t hurried, wasn’t desperate—just something inevitable, something Agatha had no desire to resist.

Rio made a soft sound against her mouth, surprised but pleased, her hands settling instinctively at Agatha’s waist. The kiss lingered, slow and deep, leaving them both a little breathless when they finally pulled apart.

Rio’s forehead rested against hers, her voice hushed. “Not that I’m complaining, but what was that for?”

Agatha swallowed, her fingers still gripping the fabric of Rio’s jacket. “I don’t know,” she admitted, but that wasn’t entirely true. She just wanted—wanted this, wanted her, wanted to stop pretending like she didn’t.

Rio smiled, her thumb grazing Agatha’s hip. “Well, I liked it.”

Agatha exhaled, stepping back before she did something reckless like pull her inside. “Go home, Vidal.”

Rio chuckled, backing down the steps. “Yes, ma’am.”

She was still grinning when she climbed into her car, and Agatha watched her drive away, lips tingling, stomach tight with something she refused to name.

This thing with Rio—whatever it was—was already slipping past the point of control. And for once, she wasn’t sure she minded.

~*~

The weekend passed in a blur of tending to Nicky—monitoring his fever, coaxing him to drink fluids, and watching more episodes of his favorite cartoon than Agatha cared to count. It wasn’t until Monday morning, when he finally woke up without glassy eyes and congestion thick in his voice, that she allowed herself to breathe a little easier.

By the time she arrived at Sonata Grove, she was exhausted but relieved to be back in her routine. She was sorting through lesson plans in her office when her phone buzzed.

Rio

How’s our little dude today?

Agatha huffed a quiet laugh, already biting back a smile as she typed a response.

Agatha  

Feeling much better, thankfully. I’ll still keep him home from school one more day just to be safe, but I think the worst is over.

Rio’s reply came almost immediately.

Rio

That’s good. I missed you this weekend.

Agatha’s fingers hovered over her keyboard. It was one thing to kiss Rio on her doorstep in the quiet of the night, caught up in something she couldn’t name. It was another thing entirely to acknowledge it in the stark light of day.

And yet—

Agatha

I missed you too .

Her stomach flipped as soon as she sent it. Ridiculous. She was a grown woman, not some love-struck teenager.

Before she could dwell on it, another text popped up.

Rio  

Any chance I can see you soon?

Agatha bit her lip.

Nicky would be home from school tomorrow, but Wednesday… Wednesday was Mia’s lesson.

And Rio always came with her.

Agatha

You’ll see me Wednesday .

She could practically feel Rio’s smirk through the screen.

Rio

Oh, you’re making me wait? That’s cold, Harkness.

Agatha rolled her eyes, but there was no real bite behind it.

Agatha

Patience is a virtue, Vidal.

A pause, then—

Rio

Never been one of mine.

Agatha exhaled slowly, shaking her head. She was in trouble.

Because Wednesday suddenly felt much too far away.

~*~




Fourteen

Chapter Notes

I apologize for disappearing last week. Health issues, midterm week... I feel like I lived months in one week with everything that happened. But fear not, I am back and happy to report that this story is almost 100% outlined and I have a rough draft for the next few chapters, so updates should be back to their normal schedule.

I hope you enjoy this one. Let me know what you think!

Wednesday arrived too slowly for Rio’s liking. She wasn’t sure if it was the exhaustion of back-to-back studio sessions or the way Agatha’s text had stuck with her, but by the time she parked outside Sonata Grove, she was buzzing with restless energy.

Mia, sitting in the passenger seat, gave her a suspicious look. “You’re weirdly chipper for someone who’s been complaining about how busy work is.”

Rio shrugged, keeping her face neutral. “Maybe I just like watching you suffer through scales.”

Mia rolled her eyes but let it go, grabbing her bag and hopping out of the car.

Inside, Sonata Grove was its usual hum of quiet activity—students moving between rooms, soft melodies drifting from behind closed doors. Agatha was at the main area talking to a student, dressed in her usual professional attire, her hair neatly pinned back.

“Mia,” Agatha greeted, giving Mia a small nod before flicking her gaze toward Rio. “Vidal.”

It was subtle, but Rio caught the way Agatha’s expression softened for just a second, the ghost of something private passing between them before she turned her attention back to Mia.

Patience is a virtue, patience is a virtue, Rio reminded herself.

Mia gave a half-hearted wave. “Hey.”

“Let’s get started,” Agatha said, already leading Mia toward her classroom. But as she passed Rio, her fingers barely, barely brushed against Rio’s wrist.

It was nothing. Barely contact at all.

And yet, Rio swore she felt it everywhere.

She exhaled sharply and made her way to Agatha’s office, where she’d planned to wait. She wasn’t inside for more than a minute before the door opened again, and there Agatha stood, looking at her like she was debating something.

Then, without a word, she stepped inside, shut the door, and crossed the room in three strides.

Rio barely had a second to react before Agatha’s lips were on hers—firm, insistent, like she’d been holding back just as much as Rio had.

Rio groaned, immediately pulling her close, her hands finding the curve of Agatha’s waist. “You could’ve at least pretended to make me wait,” she murmured against her lips.

Agatha huffed a quiet laugh, brushing her nose against Rio’s. “I changed my mind.”

Rio grinned. “Good.”

She kissed her again, slower this time, savoring the way Agatha melted just a little bit more against her. But the moment was fleeting, and soon Agatha was reluctantly pulling back.

“I have a lesson to teach,” she murmured, smoothing a hand over her shirt as if that would erase the flush in her cheeks.

Rio leaned against the desk, arms crossed, watching her with an amused smirk. “Sure. And I’m supposed to just sit here and behave?”

Agatha shot her a pointed look as she opened the door. “I trust you’ll manage.”

Rio sighed dramatically. “Fine.”

But as Agatha left, Rio caught the way her fingers lingered on the doorknob just a little too long, like she wasn’t quite ready to walk away either.

Yeah.

It was getting harder and harder to ignore just how deep she was falling.

~*~

Rio sighed, running a hand through her hair as the office door clicked shut behind Agatha.

She was supposed to just sit here after that? Like nothing had happened? Like Agatha Harkness hadn’t just walked in, kissed her like she’d been starving for it, and then walked right back out like it was nothing?

Rio groaned, dropping onto the couch and throwing her head back.

She’s killing me.

There was a restless energy buzzing under her skin, a low hum of frustration mixed with satisfaction. Agatha was driving her crazy—this push and pull, this maddening restraint followed by these fleeting moments of indulgence. It was intoxicating, and Rio wasn’t sure how much longer she could handle it.

She wanted more.

She wanted to kiss Agatha in broad daylight, where anyone could see. She wanted to pull her into her arms whenever she felt like it. She wanted to be with her in a way that wasn’t hidden behind closed doors and stolen moments.

But she also wanted Agatha comfortable. She wanted her to want this just as much as she did, without hesitation or fear.

So she’d wait.

Even if it killed her.

Still, she wasn’t about to sit there and sulk like a lovesick teenager. She pushed herself up, rolling her shoulders, and decided to take a walk around Sonata Grove. She passed a few students on the way, nodding at them as she moved through the halls. Most of them were too young to care about who she was, which was honestly a relief.

She found herself lingering near the classroom where Agatha and Mia were, the faint sound of a piano drifting through the slightly open door.

Mia was playing something slow and intricate, but Rio could hear the tension in it—the way her daughter’s usual confidence was absent. It wasn’t like her to second-guess herself when she played, but she had been off the past few days.

Rio leaned against the wall just outside the room, listening.

“That was better,” Agatha’s voice filtered through, calm and steady. “But you’re hesitating. What’s distracting you?”

Mia was quiet for a moment before muttering, “Nothing.”

“Mia.”

A sigh. “It’s stupid.”

“I highly doubt that.”

There was a pause, and then Mia spoke again, her voice quieter now. “People at school have been talking about my mom again.”

Rio tensed.

She hadn’t told Agatha the specifics of what Mia had gone through earlier in the week—how cruel kids could be, how vicious they had been with their words. It wasn’t just about Rio dating again. It was about her, about the way she lived her life, the way people had always judged her for being unconventional, for being different.

She could hear Agatha shifting in her seat. “What did they say?”

Mia let out a humorless laugh. “Oh, more of the same, you know? That she goes through people. That I’ll end up the same way, stuff like that. It’s stupid. And I shouldn’t let it get to me. But it does.”

Rio clenched her jaw, her hands curling into fists at her sides.

“I see.” Agatha’s voice was even, but there was a sharpness to it now, a quiet anger simmering beneath the surface.

Mia let out a breath. “It’s not like it’s the first time people have talked shit. But I guess it got to me more this time. I just… I don’t care if my mom’s seeing someone. I just wish people would stop acting like it’s a bad thing.”

Rio felt her throat tighten.

For so long, she had worried about what Mia thought, about how her daughter might react to her dating again. But here she was, more upset about the way people talked about Rio than the fact that Rio might have someone in her life.

God, she loved this kid.

There was a brief silence before Agatha spoke again, her voice softer now. “I’m sorry they said those things to you.”

Mia shrugged. “Not your fault.”

“No. But I wish you didn’t have to deal with it.” A pause. “For what it’s worth, your mother is one of the best people I know.”

Rio froze.

Mia was quiet for a long moment. And then, in a much smaller voice, “You really think that?”

“Yes,” Agatha said without hesitation. “I do.”

Something in Rio’s chest ached.

She didn’t move from her spot outside the door, barely even breathed, just listening.

Mia sniffed. “She’s kind of a disaster.”

Agatha let out a quiet chuckle. “Maybe. But she’s also brilliant. And kind. And she loves you more than anything.”

Mia didn’t say anything right away, but when she spoke again, her voice was steadier. “Yeah. I know.”

Rio swallowed against the lump in her throat.

Agatha clapped her hands together once. “Alright. Enough heavy conversation. Again, from the top. And this time, trust yourself.”

Mia sighed, but when she started playing again, there was more confidence in the notes.

Rio exhaled, finally stepping away from the door.

She wasn’t sure if she could fall for Agatha any more than she already had.

But somehow, she just kept proving her wrong.

~*~

Rio stayed outside the classroom a little longer, listening to the way Mia’s playing shifted. It wasn’t perfect—Mia was still holding onto some tension—but there was a newfound steadiness to it. A quiet resilience. It made Rio’s chest tighten, a strange mix of pride and heartbreak settling in her ribs.

She had spent her entire life fighting for people to take her seriously—first as a musician, then as a mother, then as a lesbian in the public eye. And no matter what she did, no matter how much she tried to just live her fucking life, people always had something to say.

And now they were turning their cruelty on Mia.

Rio ran a hand down her face, exhaling sharply.

Later. She’d deal with this later. 

She made her way back to Agatha’s office, heart still aching from what she’d overheard. She needed a distraction. Something to ground her. Something to—

The moment she stepped inside, Nicky lifted his head from where he was curled up on the couch, reading a book. His hair was a mess, and he looked downright adorable.

“Rio.” His voice was rough with the remnants of the flu, but there was no mistaking the little spark of excitement in it.

Some of the weight in her chest lifted.

“Hey, buddy,” she said, shutting the door behind her. “You feeling any better?”

Nicky shrugged. “Ugh, kinda. I just wish this stupid flu would go away already.”

“She’s finishing up a lesson with Mia,” Rio told him. “Shouldn’t be too long.”

At the mention of Mia, Nicky made a little face. “Mia’s cool. But she’s so serious.”

Rio grinned. “Yeah, she can be. But she’s got a good heart.”

Nicky nodded, yawning. “I know.”

She stayed where she was, letting him lean against her, his hand curling into the fabric of her hoodie like it was the most natural thing in the world.

Something warm settled in Rio’s chest.

This thing with Agatha was still new. It was still uncertain. But this—Nicky trusting her enough to fall asleep against her, Agatha trusting her enough to leave her with him—this was something real. Something steady.

And for someone like Rio, who had spent her whole life chasing the next thing, the next thrill, the next stage—this kind of steadiness was something she had never even realized she wanted.

She closed her eyes for a moment, letting herself just be in it.

Letting herself have this.

And for once, she wasn’t afraid of it.

Nicky was still a little sniffly, but he was in much better spirits than the last time she’d seen him. Which, in Rio’s book, meant he was officially cleared for some musical distraction.

“I’m fine now,” he insisted, but Rio arched an eyebrow.

“Uh-huh,” she said, strumming a few chords. “You say that, but I think you still need a little cheering up. Lucky for you, I happen to be really good at that.”

Nicky eyed her suspiciously but didn’t protest when she started playing. The melody was light and familiar, and as soon as recognition flickered across his face, Rio grinned.

“You know this one, don’t you?” she asked.

Nicky nodded. “Mom plays it sometimes.”

And she couldn’t help the way her whole body warmed at the contact.

“Where’s Mia?” she asked, keeping her voice low.

Agatha hummed, glancing toward the door. “Last I saw, she was talking to a girl in the reception area.”

Rio’s eyebrows shot up. “Oh?”

Agatha gave her a wry smile. “I believe her name is Sophia. Small, dark hair, looked a bit nervous?”

Rio let out a thoughtful noise, running the name through her head. She didn’t recognize it, but that didn’t mean much.

“She nervous because she likes Mia?” Rio asked, intrigued.

Agatha chuckled. “If I had to guess, I’d say it’s a strong possibility.”

Rio smirked, resisting the urge to tease. Mia would kill her if she said anything.

“Fair point,” she admitted. “Still, interesting development.”

Agatha nodded, glancing toward the door again. “Very.”

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “I know she won’t tell you.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but the smile on her lips was unmistakable.

“The twins!” he exclaimed, already scrambling off the couch. His energy levels had clearly bounced back completely. “Can I go, Mom?”

Agatha barely had time to nod before Nicky was rushing out the door, calling out to his best friends. His voice mixed with the twins’ laughter as they disappeared down the hall, leaving Rio and Agatha alone in the office.

Rio smirked and stood up. “Guess he’s feeling better.”

Agatha exhaled, shaking her head. “That child bounces back faster than anyone I’ve ever met.”

Rio turned toward her, lifting a hand like she might tuck a strand of hair behind Agatha’s ear. She hesitated for half a second—just long enough for Agatha to lean in slightly, to silently invite the touch—before she let her fingers graze the edge of her jaw, then her chin, tilting her face up just enough for a kiss.

It was soft, lingering.

Agatha sighed against her mouth, her own fingers brushing lightly against the edge of Rio’s jacket.

For a moment, it was easy to forget where they were, to just be.

But then, Agatha exhaled and pulled back just slightly. “I wish I could see you this weekend,” she murmured, almost apologetically.

Rio frowned. “You can’t?”

Agatha shook her head. “My students start rehearsals for our annual performance this weekend. It’ll be non-stop from here until the recital on the 15th.”

Rio groaned dramatically, dropping her forehead against Agatha’s. “Great. You’re gonna be swamped.”

Agatha chuckled. “I am.”

Rio pulled back, hands finding Agatha’s hips, thumbs pressing against the fabric of her sweater. “Alright, but I’m stealing you away at some point. Just warning you now.”

Agatha smiled, shaking her head in amusement. “I’d expect nothing less.”

Rio leaned in for one last kiss, pressing their lips together for just a moment longer before finally stepping back.

“Text me later?” Rio asked as she took a step toward the door.

“Of course.” Agatha’s eyes softened. “Take care, Rio.”

Rio grinned. “You too, Ms. Harkness.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but she was smiling as Rio disappeared down the hall.

~*~

Sonata Grove was buzzing with energy that Saturday afternoon. Students hurried around the rehearsal space, tuning instruments, checking sheet music, chatting excitedly. Parents lingered by the entrance, some taking quick peeks into the auditorium before heading off. The annual performance was a big deal, and it showed.

Rio walked in beside Mia, hands stuffed in the pockets of her leather jacket as she surveyed the organized chaos.

“Are you sure you need me here?” she asked, arching an eyebrow at her daughter.

Mia sighed, clearly exasperated. “I told you, I don’t need you here. I just said you could come, if you wanted.”

That was teenager code for I don’t mind you being here but I’ll die before I actually say that out loud.

Rio smirked. “Right. So basically, I’m your emotional support rockstar.”

Mia shot her a flat look but didn’t argue.

Rio grinned, satisfied, and turned toward the stage, where Agatha stood at the piano, speaking to a group of students. She was all business—hair pinned up in a neat bun, dark rimmed glasses perched on her nose, dressed in black slacks and a fitted blouse that made Rio want to drag her into the nearest empty room and undo every button.

As if sensing the thought, Agatha’s gaze flickered toward Rio across the room. It lasted only a second—just long enough for a small, knowing smile to tug at the corners of her mouth before she turned her attention back to the students.

That was all Rio needed.

She waited until Mia was distracted—some girl from the orchestra had come up to talk to her—before she slipped away, moving through the hallways until she found an empty dressing room near the back of the building.

A few minutes later, the door creaked open, and Agatha stepped inside, closing it behind her.

“You’re terrible,” she said in a hushed voice, but there was amusement in her eyes as she crossed the room.

Rio leaned against the vanity table, arms crossed. “Am I?”

“Yes. You lured me away from my students.”

Rio smirked. “I didn’t even say anything. And yet… here you are.”

Agatha sighed, exasperated, but she didn’t step away when Rio reached for her waist, fingers slipping under the hem of her blouse to press against warm skin.

“It’s been days,” Rio murmured, leaning in. “I missed you.”

The kiss was slow, deliberate, lingering.

Agatha’s hands found their way into Rio’s jacket, resting against her ribs.

Rio hummed against her mouth, nipping at her bottom lip before kissing her again, deeper this time.

But just as she started to press Agatha against the vanity, there was a loud bang outside, followed by the unmistakable chatter of students passing by.

Agatha pulled away with a sharp inhale, eyes flickering toward the door.

Rio groaned, dropping her forehead against Agatha’s shoulder. “I hate this.”

Agatha chuckled softly, her fingers brushing against Rio’s sides. “You hate not getting your way.”

Rio sighed dramatically. “Same thing.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, then pressed a quick, final kiss to Rio’s lips. “I do need to get back.”

Rio stepped back with an exaggerated pout. “Fine. Go be a responsible teacher.”

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “What are you going to do?”

Rio shrugged. “I’ll behave.”

Agatha snorted. “Somehow, I doubt that.”

Rio grinned, watching as Agatha straightened her blouse and smoothed her hair before slipping out of the room.

She had no idea how she was supposed to just sit through rehearsal now.

~*~
