Mia was on stage, her posture stiff but determined, her fingers expertly dancing over the piano keys. Rio watched her daughter play, a quiet sense of pride swelling in her chest. Mia’s form was perfect—like a statue, rigid and focused, even if her face didn’t quite show it. Every note she played was careful, precise, but there was something in the way her brow furrowed slightly, as if she was pushing herself to be perfect that made Rio’s heart ache a little.

Rio’s gaze shifted from Mia to Agatha, who stood off to the side of the stage, a quiet observer but very much a part of the scene. Agatha’s attention was entirely on Mia, her eyes gleaming with pride. Rio noticed how she leaned forward slightly, her posture poised as she subtly corrected Mia’s technique when she stumbled, offering a word of encouragement after each note that didn’t quite land.

It was in that moment that Rio realized just how much Agatha had invested in Mia’s progress. Agatha’s love for teaching, for helping Mia and all of her students, was palpable.

When Mia finished her piece, she hesitated for a second before looking over at Agatha, clearly waiting for feedback. Agatha smiled softly and gave a subtle nod, her praise quiet but genuine.

“Mia, that was beautiful. Just remember to breathe—let the music flow through you, don’t force it.”

Rio couldn’t help but smile at the tenderness in Agatha’s voice. She’d heard Agatha give critiques before, but there was always this sense of care in the way she spoke to Mia. Rio found herself mesmerized, her heart swelling with an unexpected rush of affection.

And then, just as if she could read Rio’s thoughts, Agatha caught her eye from across the room. For a fleeting moment, their gazes locked, and everything else seemed to fade away. Agatha’s lips parted slightly in a soft smile, and Rio felt her pulse quicken. Agatha’s presence had this effect on her—calming yet electrifying.

The room was still buzzing with students as they began packing up, but Rio found herself rooted in place, watching Agatha’s every move. As Agatha moved to help Mia with her sheet music, Rio’s admiration for her grew. She could see the pride Agatha had in her students, especially Mia, and it made Rio’s chest tighten with something that could only be described as longing.

For a moment, everything else melted away, and Rio knew that this—this—was the kind of woman she wanted in her life.

When Agatha glanced back, meeting her eyes again, Rio couldn’t help but feel the pull. And as the rehearsal ended, she found herself walking toward Agatha without thinking, eager for that quiet, private connection.

~*~

As the lights dimmed in the auditorium and the rehearsal came to an end, Agatha stepped onto the stage, ready for the final performance of the night. Rio, who had been quietly watching from the side, was taken aback when she saw Agatha take her seat at the piano.

She had heard Agatha play before, of course—she was a world-renowned pianist, after all—but there was something about the way she commanded the space now that made Rio’s heart skip a beat. Agatha’s fingers hovered over the keys, her posture graceful and confident. She exuded an elegance that was so effortless, it was like she was one with the instrument.

The room fell silent as Agatha began to play.

Rio’s breath caught in her throat as the first few notes flowed from Agatha’s hands, smooth and rich, filling the room with a deep, resonant sound. It wasn’t just the technical skill that had Rio in awe—it was the emotion that Agatha poured into every note, every chord. She could feel the depth of the music, the subtle rise and fall, as if Agatha was telling a story with her fingertips.

The beauty of it was overwhelming. Rio could see the passion, the love for music that radiated from Agatha as she played, and it stirred something deep within her. It was as though Agatha was exposing a part of herself that she rarely allowed the world to see.

Agatha’s eyes were closed, completely immersed in the performance, but Rio was completely captivated. She couldn’t look away. Every movement of Agatha’s hands, every shift in her posture, every tiny nuance of her expression was mesmerizing. The piano seemed to become an extension of Agatha herself, and the music—that music—was a reflection of her soul.

By the time the final note resonated through the hall, Rio was left breathless, her heart hammering in her chest. She wasn’t sure when she’d started holding her breath, but she let it out now, her exhale shaky. She had always known Agatha was a brilliant pianist, but seeing her perform live—feeling the music like this—had taken it to an entirely new level.

When Agatha finished, the room erupted in applause. Rio was still standing in stunned silence, her heart full. Agatha opened her eyes slowly, a small, quiet smile tugging at her lips as she took a moment to gather herself. Rio didn’t even realize she had been staring at her, utterly captivated, until Agatha met her eyes.

And in that moment, Rio knew without a doubt that there was no one else quite like her.

Agatha Harkness was everything.

~*~

As the crowd of students and parents slowly began to disperse, Agatha let out a quiet breath, smoothing a hand down her blouse as she gathered the last of her sheet music. The adrenaline of the performance still hummed in her veins, but she had to admit—she was exhausted.

Rio, on the other hand, looked like she was still buzzing.

“That was unreal,” Rio said, voice full of awe as she leaned against the piano, watching Agatha. “I mean, I already knew you were talented, but that was something else entirely. I think I forgot to breathe at one point.”

Agatha huffed a soft laugh, shaking her head as she stacked her sheet music into a neat pile. “Well, I’m glad I didn’t cause any medical emergencies.”

“No promises,” Rio shot back with a grin. “But really, that was… incredible. Watching you play like that, it’s like the world kind of fades away.”

Agatha hesitated, caught in the sincerity of the compliment. Her hands stilled over the music, her fingers lightly grazing the pages. It wasn’t often that someone spoke about her playing like that. With such reverence. With such admiration.

When she finally glanced up, Rio was still watching her, eyes warm, smile easy.

“I—” Agatha started, but before she could form a proper response, a small voice interrupted.

“That was so cool.”

They both turned to find Nicky trudging toward them, rubbing at his sleepy eyes. “I think that was even better than the last time you played for me, Mom.”

A fond smile softened Agatha’s face. “Thank you, sweetheart.”

Rio looked between them, and a spark of an idea lit in her expression. “You know what?” she said suddenly. “I think we should celebrate. How about dinner?”

Nicky perked up immediately. “Dinner?”

“Yeah,” Rio said, slipping her hands into her jacket pockets. “You, me, Mia, and your mom.” She turned to Agatha with a teasing grin. “Unless, of course, Agatha is too famous to be seen with us common folk now.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, though amusement flickered across her features. “Oh, please.”

“So that’s a yes?” Rio pressed.

Nicky was already bouncing on his heels, looking up at Agatha with wide, pleading eyes. “Can we? Please?”

Agatha let out a quiet sigh, knowing full well that she was outnumbered. “Fine,” she relented, shaking her head.

“Yes!” Nicky pumped his fist in the air, suddenly full of energy.

Rio shot Agatha a triumphant grin. “Great. I know just the place.”

Agatha only sighed again, though the small smile tugging at her lips betrayed her.

“Go find Mia, sweetheart,” she told Nicky. “Tell her we’re heading out soon.”

“Okay!” Nicky turned and darted off without hesitation.

Agatha watched him go before exhaling, rolling her shoulders back as if finally allowing herself to come down from the night’s high. “I need to grab my things from the dressing room,” she murmured.

“I’ll walk with you,” Rio said immediately.

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “Are you planning to carry my bag for me?”

Rio smirked. “Of course, I’m a courteous lady.”

Agatha let out a small laugh, shaking her head as she led the way to the dressing room.

Once inside, she moved toward her chair, gathering the bag she had stashed in the corner earlier. Rio lingered by the doorway, watching her, hands still casually tucked into her pockets.

“You really were incredible tonight,” Rio said, softer this time. “I mean it.”

Agatha glanced at her, pausing for a moment before offering the barest hint of a smile. “Thank you.”

Rio took a small step closer, just enough for her voice to lower. “I don’t think I’ll ever get tired of watching you play.”

Something fluttered in Agatha’s chest, unfamiliar and warm. It was one thing to be admired for her skill, her precision—but this? This was something else.

She shouldered her bag, glancing toward the door. “We should get going,” she murmured.

Rio nodded, but before Agatha could move past her, she reached out, fingers brushing lightly against Agatha’s wrist. “Wait.”

Agatha stilled.

Rio leaned in just slightly, her voice dropping to something softer. “Admit it,” she murmured. “You wanted to have dinner with me anyway.”

Agatha exhaled a small chuckle, shaking her head. “Let’s just say you’re very persistent.”

Rio’s grin widened. “That’s a yes.”

Agatha didn’t answer, but the way her lips twitched upward was all the confirmation Rio needed.

“Come here,” Rio murmured, stepping closer.

Rio grinned, pressing one last kiss to the corner of her mouth before stepping back. “Guess we’d better not keep them waiting.”

Agatha shook her head, amusement flickering in her expression as she grabbed her bag. Rio took a deep breath, forcing herself to focus on anything other than the fact that she was about to sit through dinner with their kids, pretending she hadn’t just kissed Agatha like she was starving for it.

Rio pulled into the parking lot of Eclipse Pizza, one of her favorite spots in the city. It wasn’t some fancy, overpriced LA joint trying too hard to be trendy—it was cozy, family-owned, and made the best damn brick-oven pizza in town. More importantly, Rio knew the owner, Dom, well enough that she could count on a little privacy.

She glanced in the rearview mirror at the kids. Mia had her usual unreadable expression, scrolling through her phone, while Nicky sat forward in his seat, eyes flicking between the restaurant entrance and Agatha, like he wasn’t sure if they were actually allowed to be here. Agatha, next to Rio, looked composed as ever, but Rio could feel the tension in her posture.

“Relax,” Rio murmured, nudging her knee against Agatha’s under the console. “Dom’s got us covered.”

Agatha shot her a look but didn’t pull away. “Covered how?”

“Covered as in, we’re not gonna be out in the middle of everything. Just trust me.”

The place was packed—families, groups of friends, a couple of teenagers on what was clearly a first date—but, as promised, Dom was already waiting for them near the entrance, a knowing grin on his face.

“Rio!” He clapped a big hand on her shoulder, then tipped his chin at the others. “Got you set up in the back, like we talked about.”

“Thanks, man.”

Dom led them through the main dining area and into a smaller, more secluded section with just a few tables. It wasn’t totally private—there were other diners, but the noise was lower, the lighting softer. It was the kind of place where no one would be looking too closely at them.

“This good?” Rio asked, looking at Agatha.

She exhaled, some of the tension leaving her shoulders. “Yes. Thank you.”

Mia slid into one side of the booth without a word, and Nicky, with all the enthusiasm of a ten-year-old who had been stuck inside for days, scrambled in next to her. Agatha took the seat next to Nicky, leaving Rio to sit across from her and next to Mia.

“Alright,” Rio said, rubbing her hands together. “Let’s get some food.”

Eclipse Pizza was perfect.

The food was incredible—the kind of pizza that made you close your eyes for a second because the combination of flavors was just that good. The crust had the perfect crisp on the outside but was still soft inside, the sauce was tangy and rich, and the cheese stretched just right with every bite. Even Agatha, who carried herself with a perpetual air of restraint, made a quiet, pleased sound when she bit into a slice of margherita.

But the best part? They were actually enjoying themselves.

Mia and Nicky had somehow fallen into an easy rhythm, bantering back and forth about music. It had started with Nicky declaring that rock music was “cooler” than classical music, which had made Mia scoff and declare, “That’s because you don’t get it.”

“Get what?” Nicky asked, mouth half-full of pizza.

“That’s what rock is too,” Nicky shot back. “Just with words.”

Agatha’s chest tightened again, but this time it wasn’t with sadness. It was something warmer, something more vulnerable. The truth in Rio’s words settled into her, filling the space between them. For the first time in a long time, she allowed herself to trust, just a little.

And for the first time in a long time, Agatha let herself embrace the moment fully, knowing she had no control over what was coming. But maybe, just maybe, she didn’t need to.

There's a change in POV towards the end of this chapter. You'll know when you see it.

The warmth of the morning sun bathed the kitchen in a soft golden glow, the gentle light illuminating the space in a way that made everything feel serene, almost magical. Rio moved around the kitchen with the ease of someone who had spent countless mornings like this—except this was different. This was their first true moment of quiet, undisturbed time, just the two of them, and Rio could feel the magic in the air.

Agatha noticed Rio’s smile, catching her eye as she placed a glass of water on the table. A little blush crept up her cheeks, the intimacy of the moment not lost on her.

She grabbed her guitar and a worn notebook, settling on the couch as the city’s hum echoed faintly through the windows. She strummed softly, her thoughts drifting to Agatha—the way she had slowly, cautiously begun to open up, like a flower unsure whether to bloom. It hadn’t just been kisses. It had been everything between them: the hesitation, the hunger, the quiet trust that neither of them quite knew how to name.

The chorus came to her like a breath: I’m the reason you’re letting go tonight . And just like that, it felt right. It wasn’t just a lyric; it was a confession. She wasn’t writing about a song anymore—she was writing to Agatha. About them. About the way love had found them in the cracks of their defenses.

“You’re still on that song?” she asked, tuning her guitar.

Rio shrugged, not bothering to hide the preoccupation on her face. “It’s not done yet.”

Rio didn’t answer, but the way her lips curved gave her away.

“So,” Alice said, her voice full of teasing curiosity, “who’s it for?”

Rio’s eyes dropped to the floor, a flush creeping into her cheeks. She sighed and pushed a hand through her hair. “It’s… personal.”

She leaned back in her chair, pulse fluttering like she’d just said too much. But Agatha’s face wouldn’t leave her mind—the sharp wit, the hidden warmth, the way she looked at Rio like she might be dangerous in the best way.

“Just someone who’s changed everything,” she murmured.

Alice let out a knowing grin. “So. It’s for Agatha.. You’re so in love it’s disgusting.”

Rio groaned, but the smile tugging at her mouth betrayed her. “You guys are impossible. I’m not—” She hesitated. Then exhaled. “Okay, fine. Yeah, I am.”

Their laughter filled the studio, but Rio was already thinking about the track again, about how much of herself she’d poured into this song.

On Thursday, she arrived at the studio early. The band had the day off, and Rio relished the solitude. No distractions—just her, the mic, and the song. She ran through the chords, adjusting the tempo, shifting lyrics, chasing that perfect blend of vulnerability and fire.

The first few takes fell flat, the emotion not quite landing. But then she thought of Agatha again—how she’d looked that night after their last kiss, soft and real in a way Rio hadn’t expected. That image struck something deep. When she sang the next take, the sound that came out of her felt like magic.

She hit the final note and sat in the silence that followed, letting out a shaky breath she hadn’t realized she’d been holding. That was it. It was raw. It was honest. It was everything.

Later that night, lying in bed with the finished track playing quietly in the background, Rio stared at the ceiling, her heart thudding slow and full. Relief washed over her, but it wasn’t just about finishing the song—it was about what it meant.

She thought of Agatha’s reaction when she’d hear it, of how far they’d both come. The way Agatha had let herself bend, the way Rio had let herself feel. And in that moment, Rio understood something she hadn’t before.

The song wasn’t just about letting go of control.

It was about loving someone enough to let the chaos in.

~*~

The auditorium was dimly lit when Rio arrived, the warm glow from the stage lights casting long shadows across the empty seats. A few students were still lingering, packing up their instruments, but Rio only had eyes for one person.

Agatha stood near the stage, flipping through sheet music with that same intense focus that made Rio want to both admire and thoroughly distract her. She had her reading glasses on— Jesus Christ —and her hair was loosely pinned up, like she’d shoved it out of the way in frustration hours ago.

And just like every time Rio saw her, she felt that familiar pull.

“You really know how to make a place feel dramatic, huh?” Rio teased as she made her way down the aisle.

Agatha glanced up, and the small, knowing smile she gave Rio nearly knocked the air out of her.

“Says the woman who sells out arenas for a living,” Agatha retorted, setting the sheet music down.

Rio grinned. “Touché. But I was thinking more about this moody lighting, the half-empty stage… it’s got that ‘haunted genius at work’ vibe. You should have a tragic backstory to match.”

“Should I?” Agatha arched an eyebrow, clearly amused.

Rio leaned on the edge of the stage. “I mean, don’t you? You’re a world-famous pianist with a tragic love life and a habit of working yourself into the ground.” She smirked. “You’re like one emotional breakdown away from becoming a tortured artist cliché.”

Agatha huffed a soft laugh, shaking her head. “I’ll have you know, my love life is looking much less tragic these days.”

Rio’s smirk faltered just slightly, replaced by something softer.

“Yeah?” she asked, voice quieter now.

Agatha held her gaze for a long moment before giving a small shrug. “Yeah.”

And fuck, Rio wanted to kiss her.

“Mom?”

Rio turned just in time to see her daughter emerging from backstage, hoodie slung over her shoulder, looking surprised but not upset to see her.

“Hey, kid,” Rio said, schooling her expression into something a little less I desperately want to kiss your teacher right now. “You done for the night?”

“Yeah, Agatha wanted me to run through one more piece before I left.” Mia crossed her arms, giving Rio a knowing once-over. “What are you doing here?”

“Just checking in, I haven’t seen you all day.” Rio said easily. “Just wanted to make sure you and Agatha aren’t secretly plotting my downfall.”

“Not tonight,” Mia deadpanned. “You’re safe for now.”

“Good to know.” Rio stole a glance at Agatha, who was watching the interaction with quiet amusement.

“You heading home?” Rio asked Mia.

“In a bit. Gonna meet up with Will first. Is that okay?” Mia was already pulling out her phone, barely paying attention.

“Sure, sweetie,” Rio said, “Text me when you get home, okay?”

Mia hummed in acknowledgment, clearly distracted. Rio sighed, shaking her head. Teenagers.

Once Mia walked off, Rio turned back to Agatha, stuffing her hands in her pockets.

“You work too hard, you know that?” she said, tilting her head.

Agatha smirked. “So I’ve been told. Mostly by a certain rockstar who conveniently forgets she’s just as bad.”

Rio let out a laugh, rocking back on her heels. “Okay, fair. But at least I have the good sense to take a break when I need one.”

“Do you?” Agatha arched an eyebrow. “Because last I checked, you were running on caffeine and sheer determination trying to get your album finished.”

“Alright, Ms. Harkness, point taken.” Rio held up her hands in surrender. “How much longer are you staying?”

“Just need to finish up here, then I’m heading home.”

Rio hesitated for half a second, then said, “Then let me help. At least keep you company while you finish.”

Agatha gave her a long, considering look, something unreadable passing over her face. Then, finally, she smiled.

“Alright,” she said, amusement dancing in her eyes. “But no distractions.”

Rio grinned, shifting a little closer. “No promises.”

And the way Agatha’s lips twitched—like she knew Rio was absolutely going to be a distraction—made Rio want to push her luck just a little more. But instead, she simply leaned against the piano, watching Agatha work, already counting down the minutes until she could have her to herself again.

~*~

The drive over had been easy—comfortable in the way things had settled between them. Rio followed Agatha’s car through the streets of LA, resisting the urge to press too hard on the gas just to close the distance between them. The whole taking-separate-cars thing was necessary, but that didn’t mean she had to like it.

When they pulled into the small strip mall where the Thai place was tucked away, Rio took a quick, careful scan of the area. The place wasn’t exactly a hotspot, but that didn’t mean she could let her guard down. Fame had a way of creeping up in unexpected places.

So before she even stepped out of the car, she checked her surroundings—the few patrons inside, the empty sidewalk, the parked cars nearby. No signs of paparazzi. No lingering fans with their phones out. Still, she adjusted her hoodie just a bit before stepping out, keeping her posture loose but alert.

Agatha was already waiting for her by the entrance, hands in the pockets of her coat. When she met Rio’s gaze, she gave her a small, warm smile—one that made Rio momentarily forget all about caution and carefully curated distance.

“This place is a hidden gem,” Agatha said as they walked inside, the warm scent of spices and herbs wrapping around them. “Wanda and I used to come here all the time before Nicky was born.”

“Then I’m trusting you with my dinner,” Rio said. “You pick.”

Agatha hummed in consideration, stepping up to the counter while Rio kept her back angled toward the entrance. She wasn’t about to take any chances. She was being careful—watching for cameras, for anyone that might recognize her.

And she was doing a good job keeping things professional. She was.

Until Agatha glanced at her through those damn glasses and asked, “You okay with spice, or are you a baby about it?”

Rio narrowed her eyes. “Excuse you? I can handle spice just fine.”

Agatha’s lips curled into the slightest smirk. “Mm. We’ll see.”

And just like that, Rio lost every ounce of patience.

“You’re playing a dangerous game, Harkness,” she murmured, stepping just close enough that Agatha could feel the warmth of her presence.

Agatha didn’t look at her, but Rio saw the tiny shift in her posture—the way she inhaled a fraction deeper.

“Am I?” Agatha asked, still scanning the menu like she wasn’t trying to kill Rio on the spot.

“Mmhmm,” Rio breathed, keeping her voice low, intimate. “And I don’t think you’re ready for the consequences.”

Agatha made the smallest noise, barely audible, but Rio felt it—felt it in the way Agatha tensed, in the way her fingers curled just slightly at her sides.

But then—Agatha’s expression schooled itself back into something sharp, unreadable, and she turned just enough to shoot Rio a pointed look over the rim of her glasses.

“Behave,” she murmured.

Rio barely resisted the urge to grin. “I am behaving.”

“Rio.”

“What?” Rio took a half-step back, but let her fingers graze just lightly along the back of Agatha’s hand before pulling away. “I haven’t even done anything.”

Agatha inhaled slowly, then exhaled like she was summoning patience from the depths of her soul.

Rio, of course, had no intention of making this easy.

She forced herself to glance toward the restaurant windows—still clear, no one lingering too long, no phones held up suspiciously. Good. Safe. She could afford to have a little fun.

So while Agatha turned back to finalize their order, Rio let her fingers trace just slightly along the inside of Agatha’s wrist before pulling away.

Agatha definitely noticed.

But she didn’t react—just finished paying, took the receipt, and turned back to Rio with an unreadable expression.

“Something interesting?” Rio asked, watching the way Agatha’s fingers tightened slightly around her phone.

“Emails.” Agatha didn’t look up. “You wouldn’t find them entertaining.”

Rio smirked. “You don’t know that.”

“Rio.”

“Yeah?”

Agatha finally looked at her. Her eyes were sharp, her expression calm—too calm.

“Behave.”

Rio tilted her head, considering. “I’ll think about it.”

Agatha rolled her eyes and went back to her emails, pointedly ignoring the way her ears had gone pink.

Rio, on the other hand, was having way too much fun.

They stood near the counter, waiting for their order number to be called. Agatha busied herself scrolling through her emails, but Rio saw the way her fingers hovered over the screen, not actually typing. She was distracted. Good.

Rio rocked on her heels, stuffing her hands into her hoodie pocket like she wasn’t dying to touch Agatha again. They weren’t being watched—not as far as she could tell—but she wasn’t about to take the risk. Not when they’d made it this far without anyone figuring them out.

Still, that didn’t mean she couldn’t have a little fun.

“You know,” Rio murmured, leaning in just enough that only Agatha could hear, “I can think of at least three ways I’d rather be spending this waiting time.”

Agatha didn’t look at her. “Is one of them standing quietly until our food is ready?”

Rio grinned. “Not even close.”

Agatha sighed, still staring at her phone. “I don’t even have to ask to know exactly where your mind is right now.”

“Oh yeah?” Rio nudged her gently with her elbow. “Where am I, then?”

Agatha finally turned her head, giving her a flat, unimpressed look. “Not where you should be.”

Rio bit her lip to keep from laughing. God, she was cute when she was trying to be stern.

“If I remember correctly,” Rio said, “you were the one stealing kisses earlier. So who’s really at fault here?”

Agatha huffed, turning back to her phone. “That was before we were in public.”

Rio smirked. “So you’re saying if we weren’t in public, you wouldn’t be able to resist me?”

Agatha let out a slow, measured breath, her fingers tightening around her phone again. “I hate you.”

“No, you don’t.”

“I do.”

“Nope.”

“Rio.”

“Yes, dear?”

Agatha closed her eyes briefly, as if summoning patience from the depths of the universe.

Rio couldn’t help but grin. “You’re adorable when you’re trying not to murder me.”

Before Agatha could respond, the cashier called out their order number. Agatha immediately stepped forward, grabbing the bags like they were a lifeline. Rio trailed after her, stuffing her hands back into her hoodie as they walked toward the door.

“You’re impossible,” Agatha muttered as she pushed it open.

“You love it.”

Agatha shot her a look over her glasses, then shook her head as she walked toward her car. “Drive safe, Vidal.”

“See you at home, Harkness.”

Agatha paused at her car door, just for a second. And then, before she got in, she finally let a small smile break through.

Rio felt it in her chest.

And as she got into her own car, watching Agatha pull out first, she grinned to herself.

God, she was so gone for her.

As soon as they stepped inside, Agatha set the bags of Thai food on the counter, shrugging off her coat. Rio did the same, rolling her shoulders with a sigh, finally relaxing now that they were home.

“Where’s Nicky, by the way?” Rio asked as she leaned against the counter. “I didn’t see him at the auditorium, and he’s not here either.”

Agatha turned to her, tucking her hair behind her ear. “He’s at a friend’s sleepover birthday party.”

Rio’s head tilted slightly, processing the words. Then, slowly, a grin spread across her face. “So you’re telling me we have the place to ourselves?”

She barely gave Agatha a chance to confirm before she was on her.

“I missed you,” Rio murmured against her mouth.

Agatha’s fingers tightened on her hips. “You’ve been with me for the past two hours.”

Rio’s throat went dry.

“I still missed you.”

Agatha exhaled, her expression softening. Then, with a small, knowing smile, she threaded her fingers through Rio’s hair and pulled her back in.

The food could wait.

Heat curled between them like a living thing, impossible to contain. Agatha’s hands were in Rio’s hair, nails scratching lightly against her scalp as she pulled her in, deepening the kiss. Rio groaned, her fingers digging into Agatha’s thighs where they were wrapped around her. She pressed closer, rolling her hips just enough to make Agatha gasp.

“Rio,” Agatha breathed against her lips, a mix of need and warning.

Rio wasn’t one to disobey warnings, but when it came to Agatha, all bets were off. She dragged her mouth down the elegant line of Agatha’s throat, savoring the little hitch in her breath. “Tell me to stop,” she murmured, voice husky.

Agatha shuddered. “I won’t.”

And that was all Rio needed before she was lifting Agatha off the counter and carrying her toward the bedroom.

~*~

Later, much later, they sat together in the living room, sated, wrapped in the glow of dim lighting and the warmth of each other. The Thai food had gone untouched for far too long, but neither of them cared.

Rio sat with her back against the couch, legs stretched out, one arm resting over the cushions where Agatha leaned against her. Agatha’s sweater was loose on one shoulder, her hair a mess, and Rio couldn’t stop looking at her, at the way she looked soft like this—content, at peace.

“You’re staring,” Agatha murmured, taking a sip of wine.

Rio smirked. “Can you blame me?”

Agatha huffed a laugh, shaking her head as she picked up a piece of crispy spring roll and took a bite. She chewed, swallowed, then turned her head just enough to meet Rio’s gaze.

“So,” Agatha said slowly, “are you planning to actually eat dinner or just keep looking at me all night?”

Rio reached for a dumpling and popped it into her mouth, chewing as she eyed Agatha playfully. “Happy?”

Agatha smirked. “Very.”

Rio grinned, leaning in to press a lingering kiss to her bare shoulder. “Good. Now, tell me—what’s the real reason you invited me over tonight? Was it the food? The company? Or were you hoping I’d sweep you off your feet and carry you to bed?”

Agatha rolled her eyes but couldn’t quite hide the way her lips curved. “A little of all three, I suppose.”

Rio chuckled, reaching for her wine glass. “You really know how to make a girl feel special, Harkness.”

Agatha leaned back against the couch, lazily swirling the wine in her glass as she studied Rio. “So,” she started, casual but curious, “what’s this mysterious new song you’ve been obsessing over all week?”

Rio smirked, stretching her arms over her head before letting one settle around Agatha’s shoulders. “Wouldn’t you like to know?”

Agatha gave her a dry look. “Obviously. That’s why I asked.”

Rio chuckled, leaning in to brush her lips against Agatha’s temple before whispering, “You’ll hear it soon enough. Hopefully at our first show at the Staples Arena.” She pulled back just enough to see Agatha’s reaction, her smirk widening when she saw the flicker of interest in those sharp blue eyes.

“You’re going, right? Bringing Nicky too?”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, taking a slow sip of wine as if to pretend she wasn’t just slightly thrown by the casual expectation in Rio’s voice. “That depends. Are you planning to put me under the spotlight again?”

Rio grinned, tilting her head. “You’ll have to wait and see.”

Agatha sighed, setting her glass down with a dramatic air. “Why do I put up with you?”

Rio laughed, nuzzling against her shoulder. “Because you love me.”

Agatha let out an exaggerated sigh, shaking her head as if in deep contemplation. “I have absolutely no idea why I love you.”

Rio gasped, pressing a dramatic hand to her chest. “Wow. Wounded. Right through the heart.”

Agatha smirked, sipping her wine leisurely. “I mean, you’re a menace. You never give me a straight answer. You make my life unnecessarily complicated.”

Rio grinned, inching closer. “And yet…”

Agatha narrowed her eyes playfully, her smirk growing as she leaned in. “And yet, I do.”

Rio didn’t think she had ever been happier in her life. She took Agatha’s glass from her hands, setting it aside before pulling her into a slow, lingering kiss. Their banter, their rhythm, the warmth between them—it was all so effortless, so natural.

When she pulled back, resting her forehead against Agatha’s, she murmured, “Good. Because I have no idea why you love me either, but I’m really glad you do.”

~*~

 

Mia stood outside the practice room, glancing down at her phone. She’d been waiting for Agatha to finish whatever she was doing in there so they could start rehearsing, and the music was starting to mess with her focus. The closer it got to the recital, the more nervous she became, as Agatha wanted her to do a solo performance. Just thinking about it made her chest ache and her anxiety kick up a notch.

She was about to give up and maybe get some tea or something, when she heard Agatha’s voice. It wasn’t loud or demanding—just soft and familiar. Mia knew Agatha well enough by now to recognize when she was talking to someone she trusted.

What Mia didn’t expect, though, was the light laughter that followed. It was warm and intimate, and for some reason, it made her stomach churn.

She stepped closer to the door, and her instincts screamed at her to stop, but curiosity pushed her forward. She needed to know who was in there with her.

As she got closer, she overheard Agatha say, “I’m glad you’re here.” Her voice was warm, almost affectionate.

“I couldn’t stay away,” came a voice Mia recognized instantly—Rio’s. It sounded like Rio, but softer, like she was saying something important. Something more than what Mia had ever heard from her. Curiosity won out and she looked through the small glass on the door.

Agatha was sitting on the piano bench while her mother stood in front of her.

Mia froze, her heart racing when she saw her mother take a step forward, standing in between her teacher’s legs, as Agatha’s hands immediately landed on her hips.

“Agatha…” Rio’s voice was quieter now, serious. “You know how much I care about you, right?”

Mia’s heart dropped. This wasn’t what she’d expected at all. She knew her mom and Agatha had gotten closer over the past few months, but this? This was different.

Agatha’s response was low, almost too soft to hear. “I know.”

And then, as if to answer her own question, Rio added, “I don’t want you to think I’m just going to leave, like everyone else. I’m in this. I’m staying.”

Agatha nodded, standing up, before wrapping her arms around her mom’s waist. 

Then they kissed. 

On the lips.

She’d seen the notes on the counter before—notes scribbled with lyrics, always in Rio’s handwriting. She’d seen the way they’d look at each other, but she never wanted to believe it. Not this. She thought they were just friends. Hell, she hadn’t even known Agatha was into women.

She had always thought Agatha was her rock. Agatha was steady, reliable. Everything Mia wanted her to be when the rest of her life had been chaos. But now… now it felt like that safe, solid place was crumbling.

Her chest tightened. Why didn’t anyone tell her? She felt like something was being taken from her—like her one piece of stability, the one part of her life that hadn’t been tainted by Rio Vidal’s chaotic world, was slipping away.

It was the kind of laughter that made her stomach twist, not because it was forced or awkward, but because it sounded… happy. Too happy. Familiar. It didn’t sound like Agatha’s usual warmth with her students or the casual, friendly tone she sometimes used with her. It sounded… intimate.

Mia’s breath caught in her throat, and her heart felt like it had dropped to her stomach. This wasn’t what she thought. This wasn’t what she expected at all. The pieces clicked together in a way she wasn’t ready for, and all at once, she felt like the floor had been ripped out from under her. The connection Agatha and Rio shared was something more than she’d ever imagined. They weren’t just friends. They were something… deeper.

Now that she thought about it…how much they had been hanging out lately, how often her mother came to rehearsal, to Sonata Grove. At first, she’d thought it was because of Nicky, because her mom was fond of the kid, but now…

God, she was such an idiot!

The revelation stung like a slap to the face. Agatha, the one person Mia had come to rely on as the rock in her chaotic world, was now tangled up with the one person who’d always been unpredictable. Her mind raced, overwhelmed with a wave of emotions. Confusion, betrayal, and worst of all, a deep, aching fear that she was being replaced in a way she couldn’t quite explain.

She stepped back, trying to get away from the door, but in her panic, her foot caught on the leg of a chair that had been left in the hall. The chair scraped loudly across the floor, and Mia’s heart leapt into her throat as she instinctively flattened herself against the wall, hoping to disappear.

For a moment, the silence was suffocating. Had they heard her? Were they coming out here to confront her? Her breath came faster as she fought the urge to bolt, to run away and hide from the overwhelming reality she’d just uncovered. She had no idea how to process it. She couldn’t process it. Her mind screamed for escape, but her body stayed frozen, waiting for the inevitable.

“Did you hear that?” Agatha’s voice drifted out from the room, breaking the tension.

Mia held her breath, praying that Agatha would just ignore it and go back inside. She didn’t want to be found. Not like this.

After a long, painful silence, Agatha came to the door and Mia held her breath as it swung open. 

She had no choice. She couldn’t hide forever.

Slowly, Mia pushed herself off the wall and turned toward the corner, stepping forward into the hall. Her heart hammered in her chest, her throat tight as she looked up at Agatha.

“Um… hi. I’m, uh… I’m not feeling all that great,” Mia lied quickly, her voice sounding more uncertain than she intended. She hadn’t planned to say it, but the words just tumbled out of her mouth as she tried to make her escape. “I think I’m just going to go home.”

“Oh, Mia,” Agatha said gently, her voice filled with worry. “You’re sure you’re okay? You don’t have to stay if you don’t feel well. I can—”

“I’m fine,” Mia cut her off, forcing a small, tight smile onto her face, though it felt like a mask she couldn’t hold up. “I just… I think I need some space, that’s all. I’ll be fine.”

Agatha seemed to hesitate, clearly unsure of what to say. Finally, she nodded, though her expression still held concern. “Okay. If you’re sure. You know I’m here if you need me.”

Mia just nodded, not trusting herself to say anything else. She turned quickly, before Agatha could say more, and hurried to the door.

~*~

Mia sat silently in the passenger seat, her face pressed against the cool glass of the car window. She didn’t want to look at her mom, didn’t want to have to deal with the mess inside her head. It was too much—too much to process, too much to feel. The overwhelming ache of being left out, the sting of seeing Agatha and Rio together—it all swirled inside her like a storm.

Rio hesitated before responding. “You’ve been pushing yourself lately, huh? Maybe you just need to rest. You’re going to rock this recital, baby, you’ll see.”

“Hey, Mia,” Rio’s voice stopped her as she reached for the door handle. “Are you sure you’re okay?”

Sonata Grove was mine , and now you’re just taking that too. That’s my world. I don’t want that. I don’t want to share her with you. Or the school. You already have Nicky hanging onto everything you say!”

Rio’s hand reached for her, but Mia flinched away, not ready to be touched, not ready to hear Rio’s reassurance. “Mia, listen to me,” Rio said, her voice softer now, but still full of concern. “I’m not trying to take anything from you. You’re not losing your safe place, sweetheart.”

Mia looked away, her eyes burning with unshed tears. “You’re not even here, Mom. You’re always so busy. You’ve been so focused on everything else, and now there’s her. She’s… she’s taking up all your attention. It’s like I don’t even matter anymore.”

Rio’s hand hovered in the air for a moment, unsure, before she gently placed it on Mia’s arm. “I’m sorry, Mia,” she said, her voice low and sincere. “I didn’t realize how much this was hurting you. I love you, you know that, right? You’ll always be my first priority.”

But Mia couldn’t shake the feeling of being left behind, of watching Rio drift away from her. She pulled her arm back, feeling the weight of everything crash down on her. “I don’t know how to fix this,” Mia muttered, her voice thick with emotion. “I don’t know how to feel about all of this.”

For a moment, neither of them spoke. Mia’s heart ached, a gnawing pain that made her want to curl up and disappear. She wasn’t sure what to do with all of these feelings, how to make sense of them, or if they’d even ever go away.

Finally, Rio spoke, her voice gentle but full of resolve. “I can’t undo what’s happened, Mia. But I can promise you, nothing will change between us. You’ll always be my priority, and nothing—not even her—will take that from you.”

Mia bit her lip, trying to hold back the flood of tears threatening to spill. She nodded, though she didn’t fully believe it. Maybe she would, one day, but right now, it didn’t feel like that was possible.

Rio squeezed her shoulder before she spoke again, quieter this time. “When you’re ready to talk, I’m here. I’m always here.”

Mia didn’t reply. She simply turned away, heading into the house without another word. The weight of everything felt suffocating, but she didn’t have the strength to fight it anymore.
